My mother might be alive, she thought for the thousandth time since Verica had relayed Night's information a short notch ago. I thought I had no mother, when I do. She has been imprisoned all these years while I grew up unloved.
Her scalp itched, a sign that the Immortal Asgaroth, Tearer of Bones, was preparing to speak. 
"Or she might be dead." Asgaroth's voice pealed like thunder in her head. "Your father might have killed her."
"I refuse to accept that."
"Instead you believe a girl who bears the dark mark of the wraiths."
"Will you give up trying to turn me against Verica? She's my friend."
As Jazlyn paced, she bumped a haunch of salted meat, which nudged another, creating a pendulum of swaying animal corpses. Verica perched on a barrel, feet dangling carelessly, delivering the news in a calm voice. 
Did she not care that Jazlyn's world had been turned upside down? Did she not understand how it felt that her mother might have been alive all these years, while Jazlyn grew up cared for only by an interchangeable array of nannies? All the nights she'd cried herself to sleep, wishing she had a mother, not just the cold fish of a stepmother, or her heartless father.
Ec, a Mantu chef, with bulbous golden eyes and jade skin, leaned over the caldera hearth, stirring a steaming cauldron.
	"I can't believe this," Jazlyn said, in common speech.
	"Use the Red Tongue, Jaz," Verica said, using the ancient dialect herself. 
 Normally Jazlyn loved speaking in the Red Tongue, but now she found the multisyllabic words burdensome rather than expressive. She wanted some new language where she could release fiery emotions straight from the heart.
Ec took a batch of the pastries out of the oven with a long, wooden paddle. She slid them onto a cooling rack. Verica reached for one, but Ec said, "Too hot, mistress."
 "Do you think . . ." Jazlyn said in common tongue, before remembering to switch to the Red Tongue. "Do you think my mother is still alive?"
	Verica's eyes never met Jazlyn's. Instead, she stared at the cooling pastries. "Not sure."
	Jazlyn fought an impulse to throttle her friend. "How can she be so cold? Doesn't she realize this is tearing me apart?"
	"She doesn't care about you," Asgaroth, the Immortal in her mind thought. "Why should she?" 
"You're manipulating me," Jazlyn thought. "You don't have a sword so you attack me with words." 
"I attack with the truth."
"The truth."  Jazlyn took a deep breath. "The truth is it's not her fault. The wraith part of her doesn't understand human emotions."
	"Wraiths are an enemy," Asgaroth said. "But Verica has never truly been your friend. The scar gives you a glimpse into her true self."
	 "Oh, stop it. She isn't my enemy. It's my father," Jazlyn thought. "He's the one who locked my mother away somewhere, and told everyone she was dead."
	"Your father is most of all to blame, on that we agree. Use my power. Tear the bones from his traitorous body."
	"Why is it always bones with you? You're four-thousand-years old, and all you can think of is tearing the bones from people's bodies?"
	"Enemies need to be dealt with, not coddled. If you were as old as me, you'd come to recognize the folly of mercy and the truth of bones."
	An image coalesced in Jazlyn's mind: Asgaroth holding the tip of his black sword beneath Darius Dragonking's red beard. The light of the huge green moon glinted off his blade. Normally even his great weapon was incapable of killing an Immortal, but this was a Three Moons' Night. Its magic was amplified. His blade had taken the Weaver's ear on such a night. Asgaroth hesitated. No Immortal had ever slain another. And Darius had been an ally during the First Dark War.
"I'll spare you this time, Darius, but cross me again, and I shall be less forgiving."
The memory shifted, and Jazlyn saw a beautiful blonde woman on a stone slab, her face pale and her eyes closed. Asgaroth stood by her side, clutching a silver bracelet on her wrist. "Lyssa . . . no . . . no . . ."
The image faded quickly, as if Asgaroth yanked it from her.
"I'm sorry you lost her," Jazlyn thought.
"Save your precious pity."
Verica took a pastry, blew on it, and nibbled its edges. She had a system for eating her desserts that took a long notch of the sundial. "These. . . are. . . amazing!"
Ec curtsied. "This one is glad to please, mistress."
 "Jazlyn you have to try one."
 How can she think about food at a time like this?
Through the window, the sky darkened over Deep Woods, gray clouds canopying the forest. 
Jazlyn spun on her heels, facing Verica. "I must ask you something that might put you in grave personal danger. Would you use your shadow form to find out where my father is imprisoning my mother?"
Verica frowned. "What am I? Your personal spy?"
Jazlyn ran her hand over her friend's scar. "I feel terrible for what happened to you. I wish I could go back in time and stop myself from daring you. I wish it more than anything. Can you ever forgive me?"
Verica sighed. "There's nothing to forgive, it was an accident. But Jaz, spying on the Dracon . . . that's serious business. Treason, if I'm caught. I took an impulsive chance, rushing into the lab and now look at me. I'm a monster."
"You're not!" Jazlyn said, grabbing her hand. "You're beautiful. There's no one like you in the entire world." 
"Lucky for them."
Jazlyn stroked Verica's cheek. "Lucky for you. Who else can perform such an amazing feat?"
Verica's lip twitched, not quite a smile.
Thunder rumbled outside. Jazlyn looked out the window at the gathering clouds. "It's going to be a big one."
Verica nodded, the shadows lengthening across her face. "Then we best get ready for it."
					
-<>- 
Wayden
A scream awoke Wayden and the other orphans the next morning. Rif's scream. Wayden remembered Big Darius had awoken Rif before sunrise and told him Rory needed him and Big Darius for something. That might not have been that long ago, it was just dawn now. Rif was yelling, "H-h-help! Help! He's dead!" 
Wayden and the other orphans raced down the stairs, wondering who was dead. When he got to the main room, the front door was wide open. A cool breeze blew in. The orphans gathered outside in the yard. He approached the Dariuses, trying to see what they had encircled, but he couldn't get through. A sense of frightened excitement electrified the air.
Frog-faced Darius turned to Wayden, his face pale and shaken. When Handsome moved, Wayden caught a glimpse of Big Darius lying prone.
"Is he-"
 "Dead," Frog-faced Darius whispered, "Rif found him."
"Did Rif see what had happened?"
"He says he didn't. He said he was working with Big D, and then it was like something hit his head. He blacked out for a moment and when he awoke, Big D was dead."
Blacked out. Had Rif done it? Maybe Arth had taken over his mind. Oh Source no, this was bad.
Rif leaned over the body, crying, pumping at Big Darius's chest. 
Blond Darius shook his head. "It ain't no good, Rif."
Handsome Darius turned to Wayden. "Rif might have done it. You saw what he did to the scagazi. Big Darius and Rory were right about him. We should have turned him over to the Guard."
"And me?" Wayden hissed. "You'll turn me over too?"
Handsome hesitated. "Well, you didn't murder anyone." 
Cursed Darius grunted. "Yet."
Wayden's mind whirred. Big Darius had become involved delivering messages for Gior, the man who sucked souls in alleyways for money. Gior seemed much more the murdering type than Rif.
"I don't think Rif did it," Wayden said, "and I think I can find out who did."
Then Crag raced down the stairs and stared at Big Darius. "Oh Balwart claws, this is going to be trouble." He glared at the orphans. "No one breathes a word about this until I say so, or this morning's breakfast will be your last. Who found the body?"
"Rif did," Handsome Darius said.
"Rif. Come with me."
Wayden headed to the alley. He hid behind kegs and waited, crouching in the shadows. Water dripped from a gutter, pooling between the cracked cobblestones. He waited, watching the sun rise higher in the sky. 
 "Gior's a dangerous man," Kolram said.
"I can slip away if needed." 
The barrels were positioned near the crack between two buildings. Viper-Tattoo was too big to fit through it, but Wayden could.
While he waited, his legs cramped. Finally footsteps and voices drew nearer. Wayden peeked through a crack between the barrels. Gior and Viper-Tattoo arrived. The acolyte who paid for soul-stealing slunk alongside. His face was pale. Wayden held his breath, not daring to make any noise. 
The acolyte handed Gior a single silver coin.
"One silver? Where's the rest?" Gior asked.
"I don't have it," the acolyte said. "Please. I need it."
"One coin, will buy you one pull." Gior gestured with his hands and chanted: "Pull the mist for our young friend, one silver, one pull, and now it ends."
"I'm better at rhymes than that," Wayden thought.
"It is times like this I miss having my own eyes, so I could roll them," Kolram said.
The acolyte's soul mist emerged from his lips. He purred in delight, "Yes! Yes!" Then Gior let his soul mist slide back into his mouth and the acolyte's face fell. "A little more, please. Just a little more."
"Come back with more coin and I'll oblige," Gior said. "Now get."
"But?
	Viper-Tattoo towered over the acolyte menacingly. The acolyte scurried off.
Could Big Darius have witnessed something like this and tried to blackmail the acolyte? Then the acolyte, already broke and desperate for money, might have killed Big Darius to silence him. 
"But there was no mark on Big D's body," Kolram pointed out. "It had to be a Soul-stealer."
 That really only left two soul-stealers: Rif and Gior. Three if you wanted to count the Dracon. 
The big man stared in Wayden's direction. 
"Does he see me?" Wayden asked.
"Time to get out of here," Kolram said.
Wayden moved towards the gap between the two buildings, but too late. Viper-Tattoo's big hands squeezed him in his iron grip.

Chapter 12   							
The Fragility of Life

						 
	That's what patience is. Waiting past the point of tiredness. -Jijari

   						   -<>-
Jazlyn
Jazlyn's footsteps echoed off the basalt walls of the Red Palace as she strode down the corridor thinking: "My mother might be alive. She might be alive."
 "Or she might not be," Asgaroth pointed out, his voice cold as the stone walls of the volcanic fortress she walked through. 
Her new body guard, a towering Ozac named Org, escorted her. Verica had nicknamed him the Gray Shadow because he never talked. At seven feet tall, Org had to duck beneath the oil lamps dangling from copper chains.
Org had been only guarding her for the last two months. Jazlyn missed her old Nanny as her escort. True, she had fussed at her for skipping and considered anything fun unladylike, but at least she talked. Her constant banter drove Asgaroth away. Org was as silent as he was stupid. She had selected him for that very reason, but now it just annoyed her.
Jazlyn passed the jewelry shop without a second look which caused Org to raise an eyebrow. 
Jazlyn changed her opinion about Org. He was way too communicative. "Silence!" she commanded the eyebrow.
	Org lowered it. 
	"I'll thank you to keep it lowered!" Jazlyn straightened her dress and raised her pointed chin before continuing her brisk pace. "There are more important things to life then dress shopping and broaches, you know! Now I command you to say no more unless requested."
Org kept his eyebrow silent.
	She bee-lined for the archives, determined to find the truth even if it killed her. Which it might. Her father probably wouldn't hesitate to add daughter-slaying to his list of sins. Especially seeing as he treated Jazlyn like an anathema.
They passed one of the few windows in the Red Palace. Holes had been dug into the exterior wall by Doblin, the Digger Mage, and mullioned glass fixed in the expanse. Jazlyn had been talking to perfectly-healthy Doblin one day and had been shocked when the next he'd been placed under quarantine having fallen victim to a highly contagious plague. He'd been like a kindly uncle to her giving her treats and telling her jokes. He did funny tricks with his fingers pretending to remove them. And now he had the plague. Sad. How quickly one's health could transform: the fragility of life.
 Some children who'd been staring out the window, scurried away at her and Org's approach. She allowed herself to pause briefly to stare out at the majestic view. 
Devil's Valley stretched in a wide expanse below. A stream of molten lava crept down the mountainous sides of the Red Palace, oozing into Cooks Lake. Where the fiery fingers of magma touched the water, spouts of steam rocketed upwards from the mist.
A crow flew past the window, hovering, as if watching Jazlyn. Something about the dark bird brought back one of Asgaroth's memories: Dakarth and Asgaroth had just finished their game when Karsgoth asked him to come look at the prophecy he had painted.
Asgaroth stepped warily towards his son Karsgoth's painting. The crow flew onto Asgaroth's shoulder. He shooed the wretched bird away. He wasn't a man who was unsettled easily, but these prophecies had unnerved him. Would it show him being trapped again? Indeed, the watercolor showed amber Guardian snakes surrounding a skeleton with a crown. It was the same theme as the last three of his prophecies. Asgaroth kicked the easel over, sending the water colors dripping across the floor. "The wraiths take Centuron! The same prophecy again. We killed more than half the Guardians and still we see it."
"Wiping out half the Guardians just made the other half angrier and more likely to fulfill the prophecy," Dakarth said. "Prophecies are as slippery as snakes. Your attempt to avoid them is what traps you in the end." 
"Curse of the Wraith! Is there nothing we can do to escape this? Am I doomed to be entombed in Guardian magic?" Asgaroth asked.
The crow landed back on Karsgoth's shoulder. He fed the bird a piece of corn as he spoke: "What cannot be eluded must be embraced. It is this second portrait that I wanted you to see."
Karsgoth's second picture displayed the huge green moon of a Three Moons' Night. The light from the emerald orb formed into the shape of a key. Karsgoth and Dakarth were pulling Asgaroth out from a pool of amber snakes. All around them were men, bleeding through woolen robes. 
Karsgoth fed his crow a piece of corn. "It appears that Dakarth and I shall find a way to free you."
"But when? How?" Asgaroth asked. "Who are these wounded men? Guardians? Why are some of them missing fingers?"
He did not like the feeling of not knowing, not being in control. His own prophecy powers were minimal, and he felt as vulnerable as a blind man dancing on a cliff's edge.
Karsgoth shook his head. "As to that, I have no answers."
The memory faded. Jazlyn moved away from the window, musing on what she'd seen. Dakarth, son of Asgaroth had been king of Raslo for the last two thousand years, with the exception of during the Thornbird Rebellions. He was still alive and ruled Raslo with an iron fist. As for his brother Karsgoth he had disappeared on an expedition to the Kaldian Isles and was presumed dead. The brothers plan to free their father seemed to have never transpired.
"Yet," Asgaroth said.
 "How?"
"I do not know." Asgaroth sounded as frustrated as Jazlyn herself was.
The corridors circled deeper into the heart of the castle. Glower-Stones, iridescent gems set in the ceiling at regular intervals, lit the corridors. The Glower Magi who were in charge of the stones had also been confined to the Plague room and the Glower Stones were starting to grow dim. It seemed the magi were the only ones catching the plague. Perhaps the practice of magic made them more susceptible for some reason. She wondered if Healer Berik had considered that. She'd make mention of it next time she saw him.
She passed the guarded entrance to the Court of Flames, where Volkanus the Fourteenth slumbered. The dragon's deep snores echoed off the walls. Up ahead, the book-shaped door to the archives loomed.
	Though she sought the archives, the information she needed wasn't held in the leather bound tomes. It rested inside the mind of Gol, librarian and close friend of Jazlyn's mother. Perhaps Gol had some information that would help Jazlyn find her mother's whereabouts. 
	A heavy-set Flicker, standing guard over the archives, fell to one knee. "May the Flame light your way, Daughter Draconi." 
Jazlyn, not bothering to respond to the guard with the proper ritualistic nonsense, ordered Org to wait.
	 The door to the archives was designed like a giant book cover. Jazlyn put her fingers at the edge of the cover, and flipped it open. Instead of a squeak, the door emitted the fluttering sound of turned pages.
	The crowded stone chamber, beyond the door, overflowed with rolled scrolls, leather-bound manuscripts, and clay tablets. Several acolytes, in their maroon robes, sat copying scrolls under the guidance of Fire-whisperer Ko.
 Ko's tall, lean figure rose as the Daughter Draconi entered, his silver veil swaying on his face. On his sloped forehead was the circular burn mark of the Purist. He glared at Jazlyn with icy blue eyes flecked with gray. "Daughter Draconi. May your Ember burn bright on the darkest of nights. What are you doing here?"
"I do not answer to you, Lord Ko, and you may address me as Your Majesty."
"Of course, Your Majesty," Ko said the words with malice.
Jazlyn had never liked Ko. He was one of the Purists who preached Verica should be put to death, and non-humans should be exiled or enslaved.
	Gol emerged from a side door, her silver hair pulled back into a bun. Beneath the twinkle of her spectacled green eyes seemed to lay a sea of sadness. "Daughter Draconi! What a pleasant surprise. You've grown so much. You look more like your mother every day."
	"It is she I wish to speak to you about, Mistress Gol. Is there a place we could speak privately?"
	Gol led Jazlyn back through her office door, the book cover closing behind her. The archivist's alcove held a cluttered writing desk, glowing candles, a lava hearth, and a small round table. They sat on stools with oak legs shaped like dragon tails. The librarian poured tea and offered Jazlyn a porcelain cup bearing enameled flames.
My mother has been in prison all these years, she thought for the thousandth time. While I've been crying myself to sleep thinking her dead, she is alive.
"Or she might not be," Asgaroth said. "You must face the likelihood that your father had her executed." 
"I won't accept that."
"Then you're weak. You deny hard truths."
The skin on the back of Jazlyn's neck prickled. "That's not a hard truth! It's a cruel supposition."
"You know your father. Is he one to let emotions betray his ambitions?"
Jazlyn's hands trembled and tea sloshed onto her gown, turning the fabric a darker shade of red.
"Your Majesty, are you alright?" Gol dried Jazlyn with a rag. "Oh, your poor dress. What ails, my princess? You shake like a leaf in the wind." 
Jazlyn took a breath before continue, in a whisper, conscious of Ko just a room over. "Do you know what happened to my mother after my birth?"
Gol draped the damp rag on an edge of the red-glowing hearth. "Your Highness knows very well your mother died during your birth." 
"Did you see my mother's body?" 
"Of course. We all did." Gol took Jazlyn's hand in her own and squeezed. "There was a funeral. Her wrapped remains were burned in the caldera in the Court of Flames itself."
Jazlyn clenched her cup so tightly it nearly shattered. "Wrapped remains. So, you do not know it was her?"
Gol blew a breath across the surface of her tea. Steam rose from it like the surface of Cook's Lake. "What else could it have been?"
"Why anything, if it was wrapped. Let's assume for a moment that my mother wasn't killed. Where would they have locked her away? So she would tell no tales?"
There were too many options. She needed more information.
Gol's face paled. "The act you suggest is horrendous. I'll hear no more of it."
"Do you put it past my father?"
Gol's eye closed and she let out a sigh. "No. I don't."
"Then help me, for the Love of Darius," Jazlyn pleaded. "For the love you had for my mother, help right this wrong."
 Gol sat her tea down without taking a sip. The steam rose like ghosts from the surface of her tea. She placed the cup down and stepped towards the door. She cracked it open and peeked out. Closing the door, she kept her voice soft, "There is a man who might be of help. An Ember . . . or maybe he's a Flame now if he's been promoted. Haldur. He's the officer in charge of records. He can help you for a coin. But this is not a path I recommend. Give up this foolish inquiry. It will only lead to trouble. Of course, I know good advice will fall on deaf ears."
"Thank you, Mistress." Jazlyn squeezed Gol's bony arm.
"Before you go, there is something you should have." Gol opened a drawer and withdrew a necklace. Candlelight splintered off a clear crystal that hung from its golden thread. All the light of the world seemed to dance in the stone's heart.
"This necklace belonged to your mother. I admired it and she gave it to me as a gift. I've been meaning to give it to you." Gol placed it around Jazlyn's neck. "I'm dreadfully afraid for you. Do be careful. Delicate things can be so easily broken."	
					
					    -<>- 

Viper-Tattoo's grip held Wayden's robed arm tight. The ruffian's breath stunk of a concoction of sardines, onion, tobacco, and salt-whiskey. Saliva flecked his cracked lips and his bloodshot eyes bulged. Wayden wondered fleetingly if part of his pay was engaging in Gior's magical narcotics.
Gior approached Wayden. The mole loomed amazingly large, like a grape was growing from his nose. And so much hair sprung from the black monstrosity, would Gior have to comb the beast? 
 "You really know how to focus on the least important things, don't you?" Kolram remonstrated.
"Distracting myself from horrific and deadly situations in which I find myself has become something of an art form for me."
Gior's breath smelled like he'd gargled perfume. "Who you spying for? And don't tell me you were just sun bathing behind the barrels."
"I want to know what happened to Big D," Wayden demanded, trying to sound brave, but his voice betrayed by rising an octave.
"You are in no position to demand information. Tell me, why shouldn't I slit your throat?"
A fair question, if not a kind one. The bloodstains might be difficult to scrub out of Gior's fine robes? Wayden desperately tried to think of something, when he realized he was tired of being afraid. Tired of being bossed around by people like Gior. Wayden narrowed his eyes at Gior and this time his voice did not tremble. 
"Because Dracon and Dakarth kicked you out of their school of soul-stealing. You want revenge on them. I know what they are up to." 
Gior's eyes widened. "How did you know that?"
"Arth told me."
"Arth is dead."
"That doesn't stop people as much as it used to."
Gior screwed up his lips and thought for a moment before asking, "Are you a Death-Speech?"
"Fair trade. Information for information."
Gior laughed, looking up at Viper-Tattoo. "I like this boy."
A rat scurried from the alley, seeking refuge behind one of the casks. A hammering sound from a nearby cooper's shop resonated against the brick walls.
"Swear on the Source, you'll let me go once we share truths," Wayden demanded.
"First prove to me you possess knowledge worth trading."
"Very well. How about this. Your former school chums, Dakarth and the Dracon, are going to try the Soul-stealing magic again on the next Three Moons' Night. "
 "How did you know that?"
"Is that one of your questions? No more free ones for you."
Gior stood in silence for a moment, and then smiled, his lips as thin as a crescent moon. "Fine. If you tell me valuable information, I'll let you go unscathed and what I tell you will be true, may the wraiths steal my soul if I lie. You need to swear as well."
Wayden hesitated. A wraith oath would be binding.
"I too will tell the truth, may the Source strike me down if I lie. Are you responsible for Big D's death?"
"No. How are Dakarth and the Dracon going to do this?" Gior asked. "They failed last time."
"Another Three Moons' Night is coming. I believe they've been gathering more information and feel they can achieve their goal this time. Is Arth a murderer?"
"No."
"How can you be sure?"
"Arth was squeamish," Gior said. "He didn't like killing unless necessary. How could you talk to Arth?" 
"Arth's soul, after being sucked, found a host. What did you have Big D delivering?"
"Information to a Sky Raider lady who is paying me handsomely for it," Gior said. "Who is Arth's host?"
"I won't tell you that. You might hurt him."
"Then you lose." Gior pressed the tip of his blade against Wayden's jugular.
 It felt like a claw digging into his Adam's apple. "Wait, I can tell you something else instead. Something you'll find important."
"Which is . . . ?"
What else do I know that could interest Gior without endangering Rif or me? Something about Verica? Then what if Gior or his thugs did something to her? She wasn't much more protected than Wayden was. Gior looked like he was losing patience. He needed to say something about someone. Jazlyn had that entourage of guards. "Jazlyn hosts Asgaroth."
"The Daughter Draconi?" Gior whistled. "Glad I didn't kill you. That's a valuable tidbit."
Valuable to whom? He said he was giving information to a Sky Raider woman. Why would the Sky Raiders care? A tingling like mice building a nest in his spine caused him to shiver.
"Alright, boy, get lost," Gior said. As soon as Viper-Tattoo released Wayden, he raced out of the alley. Once behind the gate, his shoulder's slumped. Gior had won the exchange. His insides felt watery. Had he placed Jazlyn in danger? What have I done?

-<>-
						Mavik
Mavik trudged towards the sled, arms stiff as the firewood he cradled in his nine fingers. The sled, already heavily laden, sank further into the snow with Mavik's addition. He wished Emerelda had been assigned to go with him, or he to be in her crew. For some reason it felt worse to be lonely now than when there was no one around that he truly hoped to spend time with.
"You think too much on sin," Jijari thought. "You will drown in it."
"This whole place is drowning in sin and none of it has anything to do with Emerelda and me."
A shadow enveloped him. Above him, he saw Desha's black skywolf spiraling downwards, wings extended. The wolf folded in its wing as it landed. Melting snowflakes glistened on black feathered wings and furred body, and mixed in with the white and black were large patches of gray. The wolf looked more its age with each passing year, as did its rider. More silver than purple streaked Desha's ponytail. His eyes were unchanged, as cruel as the day he shot Mavik's mother. Desha's dried-finger necklace jiggled as the wolf stretched. Which finger belonged to which slave was a puzzle best left unsolved. 
Desha, with a pat on the saddle, motioned Mavik atop the skywolf. "The Lord Skymaster wants a word." 
Knowing better than to argue, he clambered onto the front part of the saddle. Desha tightened leather straps around Mavik's legs and tied his wrists behind his back. The wolf launched itself into the air, shot like an arrow from a bow, flying in an arc up the steep incline of Mount Odesis. 
The air grew thinner, as they ascended, and ragged clouds of cold escaped Mavik's lips. The ground spun dizzily beneath him. In the last seven years Mavik had not been seen the Skymaster himself once. And now Gar wants me.
The slave camp shrank, patched tents no more than tiny squares of tan from the dizzying altitude, as they ascended in a steep spiral. The ramparts were manned with Skytowers. A guard wearing black fur over leather armor nodded at Desha, signaling him permission to pass. To those who knew no better, the Nest resembled nothing more than a mountain ringed with a wall. The rock was pierced with tunnels and corridors. What looked at first like a boulder with a crack in it, swung open, revealing an iron skygate. A blond skyraider on a marmalade colored skywolf launched, waving at Desha as he flew past. The gate closed behind the Sky Raider. Desha guided his skywolf towards the summit.
The tip of Beacon's fiery hands swayed in the wind. Desha's black skywolf glided to a landing near the fire. The flames licked the air. Its heat felt blessedly good. 
Gar was perhaps the only despot to have his throne placed on a frozen mountaintop. The firewood Mavik and the other slaves gathered kept him warm. Anger broiled inside Mavik. The Skymaster didn't deserve to have firewood. He deserved to be firewood.
Desha leapt nimbly off the wolf and jerked Mavik down in front of Gar's gilded eagle throne. The bonfire-melted snow soaked through the knees of Mavik's crudely patched leggings.
The Skymaster's family perched on golden bird-shaped thrones. Gar sat in the center throne. The gilded chair was carved into the likeness of an eagle. A vulture would have been more apt.
 Gar's leather clad arms rested on gilded wings. Snowfall dotted his shaven head. Around his tree trunk of a neck, he wore a pearl necklace and on his wrist a golden armband set with the emblem of a leaf. Why a leaf? Gar was hardly a follower of Bantos's Way of the Trees.
"Those armbands are of fine make. I suspect they are Source-forged," Jijari said, "perhaps even God-weapons." 
A scar stretched from Gar's jaw to his missing eye. That wound was from one of a dozen occasions Gar had miraculously escaped death. Some claimed he was an Immortal. Jijari suspected he might have practiced Invulnerability magic, a type of magic that was all but lost. Mavik had heard about some fighters who fought in the Tulkarian Blood Games who practiced it. It was said they were undefeatable.
 The Skymaster drew a whet stone from his cloak, and began sharpening his dagger. The blue blade glistened like an icicle. 
The owl throne belonged to Gar's newest Sky Wife, Yveka, daughter of the Wolf. Yveka drew one of the half dozen blades she wore in her shoulder belt. Her face seemed as jagged as the wood she whittled, all sharp angles and planes. As she moved, her blue hair swung, unveiling an ugly purple bruise beneath her left eye. The expression 'as cursed as a Sky Wife' had sprung up because misfortune always befell Gar's brides. Some were exiled, a few were confined to the slave camp, but most were sent flying off the mountain without a wolf.
"Maybe I could leap at Gar," Mavik thought, "Knock him into the fire."
"You would give up your life," Jijari said.
"Might be worth it."
"Your life is not yours to give away, Child. The Source has plans for you. Patience."
"I'm tired of patience."
"That's what patience is. Waiting past the point of tiredness."
The hawk throne belonged to Alaina Skydaughter, a half-Mantu. Her face was a light shade of jade and her eyes a dazzling gold. She was garbed in thick black moleskin fur over a leather jerkin. Her red hair, streaked with green, hung in a sleek ponytail. 
An invisible web, similar to the one he felt towards Wayden and Emerelda, was strung between himself and Alaina. There was no mistaking Zaburn's Connection Spell.
"The next time you complain how useless my visions are remember this," Jijari said. "The Connection would never have been cast if I had not urged Zaburn too."
"Does she bear a Grandmaster inside of her?" Mavik wondered. "Zaburn? Arth? Nadra? What irony, a Grandmaster ending up in the Skydaughter." 
"Three of us Grandmasters ended up here," Jijari said, "That seems beyond coincidence."
 Alaina stared at Mavik with a wrinkled brow and pursed lips. He could see it in her widened golden eyes- she felt the Connection as well. If only he could speak with her alone. 
A blank canvas set on an easel swayed against its tethers, straining to hold ground against the mountain wind. They'd taken his left pinky and his right hand was still more the capable of wielding a brush. Mavik had to stifle a laugh when he saw Gar hadn't provided watercolors. Oil paints wouldn't work with Splasher magic. The Skymaster might have been a powerful Beast Tongue, but he didn't know the first thing about water prophecy. For one thing, they required water! The most basic of liquids bound all living things and channeled the Source. Perhaps I can find a way to turn Gar's misunderstanding to my advantage.
"Paint me a prophecy, boy," Gar said. "I want to know my future."
 "Why don't you get Laeko to make you another prophecy?" Yveka said, her words spoken in mocking forgetfulness. "Oh, I remember, now. You hated her last one. Why do you think this boy's prophecy will be any better? The future is the future."
What had Gar had done with Laeko? He had to think of what to paint, but his mind was as blank as the canvas before him. Mavik stared down at the slave camp, shrunken by the elevation. It was harder to breathe up here, and not just because of the height. Sky Raiders were all around him. There was no making a run for it. This was the wrong time to suffer a creative block.
Gar glared at her. "Lock your lips, woman. Did I ask you to speak?" 
Alaina climbed off her throne and stepped towards Mavik, squinting at him with dazzling golden eyes. She asked Gar: "Do you feel something strange about this boy? Like a pull in your chest?" A savage blast of wind sent her green hair billowing and momentarily turned the Beacon's smoke towards Mavik. He squinted and choked on ash, but then mercifully the wind shifted again.
"I feel nothing. Go and see the Shaman if you are ill."
"I'm fine."
"I said 'go!'" Gar turned to Yveka. "Cursed girl grows more like you every day. Maybe I should blacken her eyes as well."
"Maybe you should open your own," Yveka shot back.
Gar laughed, a smile tugging on his snaky lips. He genuinely likes her feistiness. Could that be the hole in the tyrant's armor? Could this Yveka become an ally?
"Good," Jijari said. "Cling to hope. Keep searching for a way out. Trust in the Source."
"Hope is a bastard who's let me down to many times," Mavik thought.
Alaina stood, her jaw quivering, and headed towards a stone rampart. She dug her fingers into a groove in the stone and a hidden door slid open with a grinding sound. Mavik studied it for a hint of how to find others of the Weaver's camouflaged doors.
According to some of the slave magi, the Nest used to be the Weaver's fortress. She'd dug tunnels inside of the mountain itself. Beneath the ground, wove the tunnels of the Woven Ones, a secret underground world. If the stories were true and the tunnels existed, no slave ever found them, and not for lack of looking. Every rock in the slave camp had been well worn from prodding. 
Alaina gave Mavik one last scrutinizing glance, before disappearing into the door. When it closed behind her, leaving no trace of it being anything but solid rock. 
Gar examined the edge of his knife. "Is that painting done yet? I brought you up here to paint, not gawk. Hurry up, unless you want to go flying without a wolf."
Mavik stared down the steep, icy cliff, and the shriveled slave camp below. The slave's fires were tiny orange dots, the tents the size of his missing pinky. It was such a long way to fall.

Chapter 13 
The Seventh of Never

You don't spit in the face of power without the wind blowing it back. -Nadra

						-<>- 
					
Wayden returned through the orphanage yard still replaying his conversation with Gior in his mind. He shouldn't have named the Daughter Draconi. He should have said something else, or even risked a wraith curse with a lie. Jazlyn could be killed and it would be his fault. 
Wayden kicked a stone. "I might have a bigger mouth than you, Kolram."
"Impossible. My mouth is the size of the Tulkarian Canyons."
"Even your jokes won't cheer me up, if I got my one true love killed."
"Your one true love. What was that she asked of you again- to withhold your courtesies until the seventh of never?"
"Have you checked the calendar? That day has finally arrived."
Wayden passed Rory and Crag who were sitting on a bench supervising several of the older Dariuses digging Big D's grave. 
"We have to tell the Fire Guard." Rory never quite mastered the art of whispering while conversely Wayden was finding numerous opportunities to hone his eavesdropping skills. 
"Bah, the Fire guard," Crag spat a wad of foul-smelling sour chew into the dirt. "Every time they come here 'to help' they leave with a pocket full of my coins." 
"But the Tulkarian- he is a murderer and an unauthorized mage." 
"Pish Posh balwart claws! How could that little boy have murdered Big D?"
"With magic, like he did on them scagazi."
"Rory, children can't use magic. The youngest known mage was thirty years of age. It takes decades to learn magic. Big D- well he never was healthy. He was susceptible is all. Got the Tulkarian Flu or maybe a wraith curse."
"What if Rif gives the Tulkarian Flu to the rest of us?"
"If we were going to get it we would have gotten it by now and callin' the Fireguard or the seven sons of Borleat for that matter wouldn't make a difference. I'm sorry for Big D, I liked the boy, but he's beyond our help now."
Wayden hurried into the main room. Too-tall was clearing dishes.
"Have you seen Rif?" 
"He's delivering Night's stew."
Wayden hurried up the stairwell. He passed Cook who jumped.
"Have you noticed you haven't received a single piece of burnt toast since becoming a suspected dark mage?" Kolram said.
Wayden smiled. When he reached the fifth floor landing he heard muffled voices. He decided to press his ear against the grain of the door.
"You will be at the center of the juncture," Night said. "I've seen it."
"H-h-how?" Rif asked.
"I see you and the Dracon. Blood flowing red. You battle friends and enemies. I see you serving my Queen. The shadows parade. Magi fall from the sky. The boy with the half-skull face, he made the statues. You blow the life into their mouths . . . wait, I hear someone on the stairwell."
Wayden rushed down the stairs, uncertain if he was fleeing from friends or foes, or if such simple labels even applied anymore.

<>

Mavik touched his brush lightly to the canvas, still desperate for ideas of what to paint. Gar on top of the Beacon? No, Gar, already owned the Beacon. He'd want to see some grand vision of his future- but what? He searched the skyline, desperate for inspiration.
To the south, far in the distance, gleamed the southern wall of the world. Instead of flame, this was a wall of glittering ice, stretching endlessly into the air. Once, while gathering firewood, Desha had brought them within a few feet of the wall. Too frosted and thick to see through, the wall exuded no cold, cast no shadow. Mavik had touched it with a stick, and its tip froze and then shattered into a thousand pieces. 
Should he paint Gar breaking a hole through the wall? No, even Gar would doubt himself capable of that feat. To the east, loomed the tall, twisted spires of the Bone Palace where Dakarth sat on his throne. Gar on the Raslonian Throne of Bone? Outside of the Thornbird rebellions, Dakarth had been dictator for the last two thousand years.
To the north, Temple Dark Fist burst through the ice, a stone fist raised in defiance against the sky. Surrounding the temple were four large black boulders, each a different shape: the Anvil, the Moon, the Maiden, and the Skull. Beyond that, far in the distance, lay Deep Woods, the border between Raslonia and Helos. 
If he painted Gar in the Red Palace, the Skymaster would take that as an omen and invade Mavik's homeland. He needed to paint something, but fear robbed him of creativity, and his mind and canvas were both as blank as the endless plains of ice that stretched to the east and west. 
An amber skywolf landed on the Beacon. Mavik didn't recognize the tall brunette riding it. The woman kneeled before Gar. "The Sky is the Master."
"Stand," Gar commanded. "Does the Dracon plan to betray me?"
"Yes."
Yveka shook her whittled wood at Gar. "I warned you." 
"Silence, wife." Gar stood and paced towards the Beacon, so close that for a moment it looked to Mavik like he would step into the flames. All eyes were on the Skymaster and the only noise was the wind flapping against Mavik's canvas. After a moment, Gar turned back to his informant. 
"Can we trust Crow?"
"Trust no one, but other contacts are of the same opinion." 
"Politics!" Gar threw his hands upwards. Desha's wolf, still tethered to a nearby post, howled. "Give me a sword over a parchment any day. What's the Dracon's plan?"
"On the Three Moons' Night, he'll have his soldiers seize you, and you're to be sacrificed with the other magi. The Dracon will soul-steal your powers along with the rest."
Gar's face paled. "I'll have to talk to Dakarth about this."
Yveka looked up from her whittling. Her wooden statuette had taken the shape of a wolf woman. "You trust the son of the Bone King?"
Gar snarled at Yveka. "You think you are so wise, woman. I have sources in Raslo. Dakarth wants to free his father, plain and simple. He believes once Asgaroth has risen, the rest will follow."
"Dakarth is right. The rest will follow." Yveka's hair swung to the side revealing her swollen eye. The bruise was like a purple leaf, and beneath it were glimmering brown eyes, which darted from side to side. "Asgaroth will be unstoppable. It will be you and me down in the slave camps, while Asgaroth rules, or perhaps he'll use our bones for his next temple."
"Let him try." Gar lifted his curved dirk, as pale blue as the Beacon's inner most flames. "These Immortals are no stronger than me. I'm a better Beast Tongue than the Dragonking ever was."
"You're not invulnerable."
Gar fingered his armband. "You'd be surprised."
"You can't control Volkanus. You're no Dragonking or Borleat."
Gar leapt from his chair and put the tip of his knife against Yveka's neck. "Why do you try me, wench?"
Yveka furrowed her brow. "Put that knife away before I put your last eye out with it."
Gar's knife glittered in the Beacon's light. Then Gar sheathed the blade with a laugh. "May the Gods help me, I like this woman. Go into the Nest and stop causing trouble before I mistake you for a piece of kindling and feed you to the Beacon."
"You have to be careful of fire, my husband. You might get burned," Yveka said before disappearing into the doorway to the Nest. Gar took a step towards Mavik. Mavik's chest constricted. The canvas was blank, save a few dabs of blue. But then Gar reversed course, and paced back towards his informant.
"What else?"
"It's possible the Daughter Draconi may host Asgaroth."
"Interesting. Perhaps she is the answer to my problem."
"One last thing. A white female dragon was sighted near the Wall of Flames."
In a flash, Mavik knew what he must paint. He plunged his paintbrush into the pallet.
"A female dragon?" The excitement in Gar's voice was palpable. Mavik could understand why. The last known dragon clutch hatched almost fifty years ago and most of those had died in their youth. "What was that Yveka was saying? I'm no Dragonking. We shall see. Is the dragon large?"
"She's no Volkanus. A mere thrice the size of your skywolf. Definitely a she though, with that a cat-like face."
"Still." Gar rubbed his hands and held them to the fire. "A dragon is a dragon."
Mavik examined the pallet trying desperately to remember what he knew about female dragon anatomy. Male dragon's faces tended to be more horse-like and females more catlike. Before Kelsen had kept rats, he had kept dragoncats, a male and a female. Mavik still remembered their features vaguely. It would have to do. 
"Excellent. There is a possibility of her laying a clutch of dragon eggs for me. Where do they think she came from?"
"Some say she flew through the Wall of Fire."
Gar laughed. "Everyone knows the Walls are the edges of the world."
 "Others say it must have been an unhatched egg. Those clutches can be underground a long time before they hatch. No real way of knowing."
 "I see. Well done. You must be tired after your journey. Skarak, take her down to the scullery. See she is treated well."
Skarak pumped his fist. "The Sky is the Master."
Gar nodded. "Dismissed."
 The huge Ozac touched the groove of stone, opening the trapdoor, and descended down a long stairwell. The spy trailed behind him.
Gar glanced at Mavik. "Boy, how comes my prophecy? Done yet?"
Mavik stared at the image he'd created. He'd more practice with watercolors, and this painting looked a bit clumsy to him. Still, the portrait was clear enough, Gar on the back of a white dragon, sword raised, like the Dragonking himself. Mavik just hoped it wouldn't become true.
Gar admired Mavik's painting with a smug smile.
Without quite knowing why, Mavik tipped the remaining paint onto the Beacon-melted snow by his feet. The oil paints swirled into the pool of melted slush. A beam of sunlight shone on it, and an image formed so clear to Mavik, though no one else seemed to see it. A blonde held an amber snake against an Anvil and a door appeared. One of the Weaver's doorways.
Mavik had painted a prophecy all right, but it wasn't of Gar's glories. It was his escape route.
	
-<>-
Alaina

Alaina, daughter of Gar Skymaster, heir to the eagle throne, petted her skywolf's thick red fur. Red Paw licked the tears from her cheeks, but even the elixir of wolf slobber couldn't cheer her up on this darkest of days. 
"Poor Laeko," Alaina thought, "She was like a mother to me."
"And you let them take her," Grandmistress Nadra, Fire-Whisperer, spoke from inside Alaina's mind, her voice filled with more venom than an ice adder.
Alaina ignored the bitter old witch and brushed old feathers off Red Paw's wings, uncovering a layer of new red feathers springing up beneath the old gray blanket. The feathers stuck to Alaina's fingers. The Sky Wolf let out an annoyed growl.
"Don't be a baby," Alaina said, rubbing her furry head. She looked around to make sure no one had heard her. Sky Raiders considered it unseemly to treat your skywolf like a friend, as the dirt-dwellers treated their pets. Not that she'd any friends left to lose. The other young Sky Raiders seemed afraid to talk to the Skydaughter, after what her father did to that Ozac boy who called her lime-skin. She could still hear his screams in her nightmares.
Only Laeko, the former librarian, had understood Alaina's love for Red Paw. She'd told Alaina on more than one occasion, 'In the olden days, the wolves were considered a rider's soul. If a skywolf died, the owner would mourn for a year, until they were given a new wolf, and therefore a new soul. For that year they would be the Shunned, and none would talk with the soulless for fear of losing their own soul.'
Poor Laeko, she thought again. Father, why did you have to toss the Weaver's statue off of the Nest? Laeko, why did you have to denounce him?
A few days ago, Laeko had shouted, 'Gar, you think yourself a god, but you are just a vain fool. You are nothing and your legacy will be dust.'
 Gar had laughed. 'I should have sent you down to the slave camps when you made that false prophecy about me. Me killed by fire. I don't die so easily. I was going to send you down to the slave camp soon, anyway. The Dracon will pay nicely for a prophet. The fool doesn't know false prophets from real ones.'
The memory of Laeko being dragged to the camps haunted Alaina's dreams. She hadn't slept more than a few hours since Laeko's enslavement.
"Your father thinks he is the Dragonking reborn, but he's nothing more than a barbarian," Nadra said, "Your whole tribe is nothing but a gaggle of thugs, thieves, and pretenders. Your father surrounds himself with wealth, but never class." 
Alaina wished she could tell Nadra she was being unfair, but her father, despite his wealth, was neither gentle nor refined the way characters were in the Book of Princes or the other stories she loved from the Golden Age of Literature. Gar had all the external trappings: paintings, silks, wines, sculptures, but you could throw a dress on an Ozac and it would not make him the queen of the fairies.
Where to go? The smell of the kennel was making her nauseous. The Temple now displayed her father's statue. That would make her even more nauseous. Her chamber was as small and cramped as a prison cell. Not the training room, she couldn't deal with combat lessons today. Not the Beacon, she would say something to cross her father, and earn a bruise to match Yveka's. The library would have been the perfect tribute to Laeko, but it remained closed since her arrest. The archives had been her true home. Laeko used to read aloud to Alaina from the Book of Princes and other works. They huddled up in front of a fire. Laeko could have been a mummer, with the way she threw herself into the characters voices and emotions.
Poor Laeko.
"Poor Laeko?" Nadra said, "She sealed her own fate. You don't spit in the face of power without the wind blowing it back."
The sound of footsteps and her father's voice echoed from the corridor. Alaina went to the kennel door and listened at the key hole. Her father was saying, "I have four thousands reasons to keep her around."
Her step-mother answered, "Don't you have enough with the others? Blood means nothing to you?"
"Silence, wench. If I wanted your opinion, I would have asked for it." 
"Why do you bother talking to me at all?" Yveka asked. "If all you want to hear is the sound of your own voice, find a canyon with a strong echo and you can moon over the sound of your own voice all day."
The sound of a slap resonated down the hallway. 
"As I said, a thug," Nadra said.
Alaina's stomach twisted at the truth of the witch's words.
The wolves howled as the iron sky gate on the side of the kennel rattled and clanged open. The cold hand of the wind blew in, Desha and his skywolf in its palm. The winged beast landed, kicking up straw. Desha dismounted in one graceful leap. 
Desha's leathery face was handsome, but his eyes were cruel. 'Handsome on the outside, ugly on the inside,' Laeko used to say. His frequent boasts about his finger necklace did not endear him to Alaina.
"Skydaughter, may the winds be with you," the Tulkarian bowed. "It's a glorious day. Will you be taking Red Paw for a fly, My Lady?"
Red Paw might not have known much, but she knew the word fly. She looked up and panted eagerly.
Why didn't I think of that? A flight might lift my spirits.
 Alaina grabbed a fur robe from a hook on the kennel's wall. "I'm just leaving now."
She took a saddle from a nearby rack and placed it on the winged wolf's back, clambering onto it, and tightening the straps.
Alaina whispered, "Fly" and Red Paw launched herself, whistling through the sky gate, bulleting into the brisk morning air. For the first moment all day, she felt good. Then the tears erupted, freezing in her lashes. She hadn't wanted to cry. A Skydaughter's heart must be ice, but left alone in the sun, ice will melt. The sun was strong upon her skin. 
There was something healing about being high above it all. Far below, the Sky Raiders with their whips dwindled into insignificant dots. Up here, the sky was what was important; the endless stretch of blue, that one could sink into forever. This wolf, this flight, this moment, they were hers, and hers alone. The frigid wind felt good against her face. It was real. It whispered: 'You are alive.'
 The splintered remains of the Weaver's statue lay shattered below, a memorial to Laeko's enslavement. A thin layer of snow blanketed it. To her right, huddled the canvas tents of the slave camp. Laeko would be down there now, shivering, toiling, gathering firewood, digging graves with the other slaves.
 "Red Paw and I could fly down and rescue her, and not come back," Alaina thought.
"You know very well they would track you down in a heartbeat," Nadra said, "Someday you'll be the Skymistress. Isn't that what you want: to be the queen of your little ant hill?" 
Is that what Alaina wanted? That's what everyone thought she wanted, and perhaps she had wanted it fleetingly, to wear a crown and sit like Gar on his mountain throne. From Laeko's library she had read many times The Tyrant's Daughter, touching the tome gently avoiding getting oils onto the precious parchment. The story featured a princess who was the daughter of an iron-fisted king. The monarch had cut out his own heart and placed it on a pedestal where it petrified. The princess did her best to protect herself and her little sister from her father's wrath. Once, while shielding her sister from one of her father's bouts of rage, she vowed she would never be like her monstrous father.
When the girl had just barely become a woman, the tyrant died making the princess a queen. As part of the ritual of accepting the throne, she sliced out her own heart and lay it on the pedestal. Staring at her heart, she told herself it didn't matter. She would never let her heart petrify like her father's had. One of her generals questioned her and made her look foolish. She sent him to his death. Then one of her advisors, who had been her advisor and like a kindly grandfather had tried to weaken her power. She had him killed as well. The princess's heart became harder with each killing. Then her own little sister plotted to seize the throne from her. When she asked her sister why, her sister had replied, 'Because you've become like father.' The Princess shrieked, 'Liar' and plunged a dagger into her sister. Then the princess went into the Heart Chamber. She wanted to weep, but tears wouldn't come. She rushed into the heart chamber, and found her heart had become stone.
It's just a story. I won't become like that. I swear I won't.
Red Paw passed over the boulder known as the Anvil. The winds were at their back and it was a short notch of the sundial later that they reached Dark Fist. As she drew closer, the faint beating sound of the Heart Stone grew louder. Was it truly the Tyrant's daughter's heart beating beneath Deep Fist? 
"Heart Stones are real, but your children's story is not," Nadra said. "Some say the Ancients created them. They were already here when the Immortals arrived."
Usually there were a few Raslonian bone guards posted outside the opening, but not today which seemed odd. Marks in the snow hinted at sleds pulling something heavy. Around the tracks, red splatters flecked the snow. Blood from a hunt? 
She flew through the breached wall into Dark Fist. Red Paw spiraled downwards. No guards inside either. 
She landed in the inner ring, next to the podium, where the bodies of Asgaroth and the Dragonking lay, covered in slithering bands of crackling energy snakes. The Guardian magic gave off some heat, and Alaina rubbed her numb hands. 
Through the amber shell of Guardian magic she could see the Immortals' bodies. The Dragonking's face was covered in a thick red beard, thick as the pelt of a wolf. He was a large man with a bulbous nose and bushy eyebrows. Asgaroth, on the other hand, was clean-shaven with chiseled cheek bones and a square jaw. His charcoal black eyes stared lifelessly at the crystalline ceiling. 	
Alaina's breath caught in her throat. Streaks of red were strewn across the floor here as well. She touched one of the crimson stains with a gloved finger-and tasted it. Blood. Perhaps it was just an animal that had climbed through the breach.
Footsteps sounded behind her. She spun just in time to see a figure dashing through a doorway on the west. Alaina felt the Pull towards whoever it was, like she felt to the prophet slave boy. Had he escaped somehow? 
She knew her duty and had been trained well. She pulled out her dirk. Desha's mantra from combat drills resonated through her mind, 'Steel in hand and heart when battle calls.' The blade reflected the amber Guardian magic humming all around. She prepared to take her first finger. 

Chapter 14 
A Lovely Couple

If you can't retreat from the flames, you must enter into them. -Nadra

-<>- 
 
Alaina leapt over the Guardian field to the outer ring. The crackle of amber energy snakes, that wove together to make the Guardian field, sizzled against the heels of her deerskin boots. The escaping figure, wrapped in a dark cloak, ran through a corridor that Alaina could have sworn wasn't there a moment prior. She hesitated at the open door, which led to a descending passage. The Connection Spell pulled at her, emanating from ahead. 
 "It feels different than the pull we felt towards the slave boy," Nadra thought.
Something was off. Nevertheless, forward she went, into the darkness. A Skydaughter shows no fear.
The beating sound grew louder as she descended into the dark tunnels. This must be part of the legendary Weaver's World. She'd explored some of the tunnels that led under the Nest that the Weaver had left behind, but they all dead ended before they went too far. These tunnels seemed to stretch further. Her heartbeat accelerated. She slowed her breathing, trying to regain control. "I won't feel fear."
"Then you're a fool," Nadra said, "Everything about this spells trap."
Alaina gathered the Source energy in her mouth, preparing a puff of flame to light her way. She had to be careful. Too much and she could burn up her air supply. She whispered, releasing thin lines of flame through the air, illuminating the corridor. She took a few steps, before the luminescence succumbed to the surrounding shadows.
 "You're inching your way into a death trap," Nadra said. 
"A warrior shows no fear."
"Your no warrior, you're a frog." 
Alaina's stomach twisted. Fifteen years being inside her hadn't made Nadra any less prejudiced against the Mantu race. The insult bristled, but only slightly. If Nadra hadn't grown more tolerant, Alaina had grown more accustomed to Nadra's barbed words. And Alaina had learned that if one filtered out the crude part of Nadra's speeches sometimes wisdom could be found. In this case, it was the words 'death-trap' that rang the truest. She'd heard tales of the dark things that lived and died beneath the temple Dark Fist.
She had been trained to charge into battle, like any good little Sky Raider, but she had never been particularly adept. A warrior should be wary of walking into a trap. Bravery was one thing, but this was foolishness.
 Alaina retraced her steps to the main chamber. The doorway had vanished. She heard sounds from behind her, and her neck frills extended. She let out another puff of flame in hopes of finding the exit, but she illuminated only rough rock.
 Heart pounding louder than the distant thumping, she searched the wall with her hands for a knob, a lever, a crevice. She felt only cold stone. Had she descended into her own grave? 
 "If you can't retreat from the flames, you must enter them," Nadra said. 
Alaina chewed her lip, wracking her brain for how to escape this dilemma. If she caught the slave boy, or whomever the Connection belonged to, she could force him to locate and open the hidden door. She whispered another tendril of fire into the air. 
Wherever this was had plenty of air to fuel her flame. The Weaver's World's tunnels stretched for endless leagues if the histories wrote it true. Enter the Weaver's World but never will you leave, the legend went. She trembled. It's only the cold and damp, I have no fear.. 
"Then you're a fool," Nadra thought. "You should be deathly afraid."
Fire welled in her mouth, swirling around her tongue. She inched forward. The beating sound intensified, matching the thumping of her heart.
"Keep your eyes open," Nadra said. "Someone might be lurking ahead ready to bash your skull in."
Alaina opened her mouth, but only a couple of sparks emerged. 
"Your Source energy needs time to replenish," Nadra said. "The whispers of flame were never meant to be used as a glorified lantern. Bursts of flame should be short, concise, and precise."
The corridor widened and twisted as she descended. The darkness made the going slow. She rested, meditating for a moment, letting the Source regenerate. She released a flare, revealing a tunnel with stalagmites and a stream traversing it. 
Around the next corner, hints of amber light illuminated the walls. Guardian Magic- was it Centuron? The histories suggested Centuron stood guard over the Shadow Queen. Could this cloaked figure she was following be a Guardian Mage? As her eyes adjusted to the Guardian Magic, she stopped in her tracks.
In the center of an enormous cavern, a six-foot wide stone heart expanded and contracted. The stone stretched like flesh, glowing as if heated in a blacksmith's furnace. Metal tendrils spiraled out from it, writhing like a kraken's tentacles. Guardian energy flowed from these into a clear energy sphere which enveloped a milk-white woman. Her eyes, her hair, even her gown were bone white, but around her feet stirred a puddle of darkness.
A second Guardian Field formed a ring on the ceiling, matching the one on the temple floor. I'm right below the inner ring. This is the Heart Stone that produced that eerie noise.
A short blue-haired boy stood with his back to her. He wore a black robe, filigreed with golden snakes winding around his waist. He ladled wax from a cauldron into a plaster mold. Scores of life-size wax figures, partially covered by linens, populated the room. Each representing half animals: a wolf man, a bird man, a lizard man, a bear man, a horse man . . . 
"Who are you?" Alaina asked the boy, but he ignored her and continued to work molding the statue. By his side were buckets filled with plaster, wires, brushes, chisels, rollers, and hammers.
Stones grated to her right, and a wall slid open. Three figures emerged. Woven strips of linen bound their legs, torsos, and chests. The mummy-like wrappings stopped at their necks. 
They were a mixture of races. The first was a half-Ozac male, wearing a dark cloak over his linen wraps. Long silver hair cascaded across red eyes, and gray skin. He was smaller and lighter skinned than Skarak. 
The second was an elderly Mantu female leaning on a staff. She appeared to have no eyes, yet she moved nimbly about. The last was a young woman wearing a fox's mask. Long black hair cascaded down her back. The connection she felt centered on this fox-girl, not the slave boy after all. Why do I feel the same pull towards this Woven One and the slave boy?
 The half-Ozac's eyes locked onto Alaina. The redness in them was mottled with blacks and white, like staring into hot coals. Alaina jerked around to run, but the Ozac lunged and grabbed her wrist. She bucked backwards, but he pinned her against his chest. 
Her heart and body beat like the wings of a wolf struggling to break free of its tethers.
 "Who . . . are . . . you?" she panted. "What do you want?" 
"My name is Anaz, servant of the Weaver. She has a message for you, girl," the Ozac said.
The blue-haired boy turned. His face was half flesh, half skeleton.

-<>- 

Wayden sank his spoon into the pool of white sodden curds Cook called porridge. It was delicious, flavored with near starvation. "What was Night telling you about when she called you up to visit with her?"
"N-n-nothing." Rif prodded his more suspiciously, examining each bite thoroughly before putting it into his mouth. "Some more of her m-m-madness."
"What was that about you blowing life into some statues?"
"Like I said . . . Hey! You were listening in weren't you? We thought we heard someone."
Wayden blushed.
Rory came in from the yard. "Some silver-veiled Fire-Whisperer and a Dragon Knight are heading this way with a mass of Flickers."
Crag frowned. "Rory, did you-"
"I didn't be saying peep," Rory said. 
Were they here to arrest Rif? It wasn't Rif's fault he had Arth in his mind.
	Crag donned his hat.
Rory held the door open. The infamous Royal Companion Jereth Thunderstone entered first. Sunlight glinted off the dragon knight's serpentine helm. The man's worm-like lips sneered.
A Flicker thumped the base of his spear onto the hardwood floor and bellowed, "Make way for Fire-Whisperer Ko, grandson of Borleat, son of Neruk." 
Fire-Whisperer Ko entered
"May your ember glow in the darkest of nights," Crag said, falling to his knees. 
The orphans followed Crag's example. Ko wore the silver veil of a high-ranking Fire-whisperer draping over his mouth and chin. What marked him as distinct was a burn mark branding his sloped forehead. It was almost in the same position as Wayden's, though Wayden's was an irregular mess, while Ko's a perfect circle.
"That's the mark of a Purist," Kolram explained. 
"Who are the Purists?"
 "Really, Wayden, do you - never mind- no one is perfect I suppose. Just try to be more attentive in the future. The Purists want to exile all non-humans from Helos. They burn themselves to cleanse sinful thoughts from their heads."
"Even the Mantus?"
"Some do, others of them favor enslaving the Mantus. They claim we should go back to the days when they received no compensation for their work and wore iron collars."
Ko peered down at Crag. His blue eyes were ringed with steel gray. "Enough. You're wasting valuable state time."
Crag's face flushed, as he pulled himself off the floor.
 Ko handed a parchment to Crag, stamped with the Dracon's wax seal. "I'm here due to a violation of The Use of Unauthorized Magic Act."
Crag trembled. "I didn't mean to. I just want to be a Fire-whisperer. Is that so bad?"
"We aren't here for you, though thank you for bringing that to my attention. I'll make mention of that to the Dracon. I've been authorized to take into custody the two orphans who used magic illegally in the Dracon's fields."
Wayden's stomach knotted. Did their justice lack all logic? Rif possibly killed Big Darius, but they were arresting them because they used magic in self-defense. They mustn't know about the incident with Big D, or surely that would be mentioned. It didn't matter, saving someone bore a worse consequence than killing them.
 "No need to tell the Dracon, is there?" Crag pleaded. "About me?"
"We'll see how cooperative you are."
Crag straightened. "Right." He pointed at Wayden and Rif. "These two used magic. My man, Rory, saw them. One summoned a wolf; the other did some spell with a cloud. I guess a weather wizard of some sort? Anyhow, they're yours."
 "So you knew about this but failed to report it?" Ko asked Crag.
"We . . . we were in the process."
"Quite a lengthy process it would seem," Ko placed his hands behind his back and paced. "As well as the two boys, I'm to take custody of Mistress Night."
Crag's quadruple brimmed hat had fallen to the floor, and without realizing, he took a step backwards and stood on it. "That's my grandmother!" 
Ko handed Crag a parchment. "You were a candidate to become a Fire-Whisperer, were you not, Master Crag? I seem to vaguely recall voting on your nomination. May I assume then that you are literate?" 
"Of course, I am," Crag said, examining the parchment. "I'll have you know I'm nominated again for the coming Choosing." 
"You might have to tone your garb down when you go before the Selection Tribunal," Ko gestured downwards with his chin, veil swaying. "We can't have you out-brightening the volcano. Though the hat on your foot is original, I'll grant."
Crag followed Ko's gaze to his crushed cap. He tried to disentangle and almost tripped himself.
"Work on your foot adornments at a later date," Ko snapped. "You're wasting time with your toe hats. Will you read the document, or do I have to read it to you?"
Crag blushed again and squinted at the document, his lips moving as he read. "Rory, go fetch my grandma. Rif and Toast, you'll be taken to the Red Palace."
Rory nodded and headed up the stairwell.
"We weren't using magic, Sir," Wayden protested. "We were just praying. The Source or the Dragonking must have sent the wolves."
Ko glared at Wayden. "You will not speak unless requested."
Wayden moved towards Ko. "It's not fair -"
Thunderstone and another grabbed Wayden, and pulled him away from Ko. Soldiers flanked Rif as well. Wayden tasted bile.
"If we hadn't used magic, Rory and the rest would have been killed," Wayden thought, "And now, as our reward, they're arresting us."
"Justice was the first victim of the Dracon's reign," Kolram said.
"Sir, if you would just let me explain," Wayden said.
Ko turned his withering glare on Wayden. "You may not address me, unless requested, then you must call me Your Holiness. Do not speak. Nod once if you understand."
"But-" 
A slap sent Wayden reeling back against a Flicker's shield. His cheek stung from the pain and the room wobbled.
"I believe I requested a nod," Ko's voice was cold and calm.
Rif stepped forward. "It was m-m-me that used the magic. Leave W-W-Wayden out of it."
A shove from Ko sent Rif flying into a guard, who caught the Tulkarian.
"One more word out of either of you, and you shall make this journey bound and gagged," Ko said. "Attempt escape and there will be painful repercussions. I have orders not to kill you, but maiming has not been expressly forbidden. Escort them to the wagon."
Flickers flanked Rif and Wayden. 
"This can't be how it all ends for me," Wayden thought. "The Source. The Prophecies. I was meant to die fighting Gar, not rotting in prison." 
Rory came down the stairs followed by Night. Her milk-white hair was coifed into elaborate plaits. She wore a clean black dress adorned with sky jewels and a golden bonnet over her braids. Her scars were covered with henna.
 "She were already packed," Rory said, scratching his head. "Did she be knowin' about this?"
"Grandma!" Crag yelled to Night. "They want you to go with them to the Red Palace."
"I'm not deaf, nor blind, just old and ugly." Night adjusted the strings of her bonnet. "If you came up to visit your grandmother once in a while you would know that, but you were born a fool, and age has not improved you."
"I meant to, its just -" Crag began.
"I live in the same tower you do. You have only to go up the stairs. If you knew the slightest bit about me, you would know I knew we were leaving, because I saw it in the water."
"Now grandma stop your joking, I know you wouldn't use unauthorized Splasher magic."
"What does it matter now, they are arresting me anyways. Yes I used magic, and I need no man's leave to do so. Your great-great grandmother, who you've been so ashamed of, is rising again soon. All this time I've been praising her name, and you've been denying any connection with her, hoping to curry favor. We shall soon see who gets stuck in an attic when she reigns supreme."
Crag's face paled.
"I like this one," Ko said to Thunderstone.
The Dragonknight rolled his eyes and muttered. "The two of you would make a lovely couple."

Chapter 15 
 A Double Edge		 
And what is strength? Is strength the ability to frighten others or to inspire them? Is it to control others or oneself? - Grandmaster Baltoo

-<>- 

Alaina winced as Anaz forced her arm behind her back. His grip was steel wrapped in linen and his red eyes seemed to burrow into her.
"Stop struggling," Anaz said. "You're just hurting yourself."
He was right. There was no doubt who was stronger. Her eyes settled on the boy whose face was half skull. He seemed to be smiling at her. His one good eye seemed to be the eye of a normal child.
"Are you the Weaver?" Alaina asked the boy. 
"Is he the Weaver?!" The girl with the fox mask laughed. Alaina felt the pull towards her even more strongly now. Her hands glowed bright as embers. "The boy is one of the Cursed."
"The Weaver would have your head for calling him the Cursed, Finder," the female Mantu said, leaning on her staff. The pits where her eyes should have been appeared dark and endless.
Anaz shrugged. "Leave her be, Queranos. Denying hard truths doesn't change them."
Alaina didn't care what a Cursed was or why had they lured her here. What she wanted to know was how she was going to get out of this in one piece. She tried once more to pull free of Anaz. "Let me go. I'm the Skydaughter. Gar is my father. He'll have your head for this." 
"Cease struggling." Anaz twisted her wrist. Alaina gasped in pain.
 "You'll follow orders or you can be in the Weaver's cell next."
Alaina couldn't make sense of what they were talking about. Centuron was head of the Guardians. Had they rescued this Anaz from the Guardian's prison?
The girl with the fox mask leaned over Alaina, long black hair cascading like a waterfall. She touched Alaina's skin with the tip of a glowing finger. A tingle coursed through Alaina's body. 
"Greetings Nadra's Host," the fox-girl said. "You may call me Finder."
Finder's hands turned yellow and an image of lips whispering a flame danced in her palms. She was a Magic-finder like Goat or Zaburn. She was about Alaina's age, yet she already knew magic.
 "How did you know about Nadra?"
"I host the Grandmaster of Magic-finding, Zaburn." Finder's voice had an eerie quality to it. "Jijari foresaw that the Grandmasters would be separated on Three Moons' Night and she warned Zaburn. He cast a spell binding us together, so we could find each other after the prophecy came to pass."
This information fit with Nadra's memories of Zaburn. She remembered him casting a spell on them at Dark Fist before the Dracon's deadly ritual. The slave boy who was painting the prophecies for her father must host Jijari- since she was the water prophet.
Finder leaned closer to Laeko. Beneath the fox mask she had swirling silver eyes. "You know my aunt, Laeko."
Laeko . . . her aunt? Laeko was a Strand Prophet. A follower of the Weaver.
"How did you know? Splasher Prophecies like Jijari does?"
"Her highness, Cala the Weaver, sees the future, not in water, but in weavings."
The Heart Stone beat, illuminating Finder's face. "She sees the junctures. You must save the burnt boy." 
"I don't understand. What burnt boy? Who is that woman floating there? What is that blue-haired boy doing? Why is his face like that?"
The boy smiled, a smile that was half adorable and half out of Alaina's worst nightmare.
"The cursed -," Finder said, "I mean, His Highness, is making bodies for the dispossessed. As for the woman, do you not recognize Lila the Immortal, true Queen of Shadows, friend of wraiths, and ally to the Weaver?" 
"Why is she attached to a Heart Stone?" Alaina gestured with her chin towards the pulsating stone.
"Centuron trapped her in it a millennium ago."
Queranos glared at Finder. "You say too much. Did the Weaver ask you to tutor the girl?" Her golden slit eyes met Alaina's. She touched Alaina's cheek with her wrinkled webbed fingers. "Listen closely, Skydaughter. Free the Burnt Boy. Remember the four thousand bones. And when the knives fall, save Laeko."
Four thousand. That number- she'd heard someone else mention it recently.
Finder's hands flashed bright yellow. She glanced at them. "We need to go."
"Trouble?" Anaz asked, loosening his grasp on Alaina. 
Finder held up her hands. Flashes of gold and silver danced across her palms. "Guardian Knights."
Guardian Knights- all the myths were turning out to be real. Centuron's order that kept the Immortals trapped was real as well, apparently.
They raced down a long hallway, Anaz guiding Alaina, Finder lighting the way with her glowing hands. The boy with the half-skull face ran with them. 
They moved quickly through the tunnels, despite Querano's old age and blindness. Their only light came from Finder's hands. 
"What . . . do you . . . mean . . ." Alaina panted. ". . . four thousand bones. And who is - Burnt Boy?" 
"We will tell you no more," Queranos answered. 
"A riddle? That's why you lured me here? Did you kill the Raslonian guards just for this? Why not just talk to me up in the inner ring?"
As she asked Alaina suddenly guessed the answer. They wanted her to see something: the Shadow Queen, the Cursed, the Woven Ones, or the Heart Stone. But which and why? 
"Killing Raslonian Bone guards is never a bad thing," Finder said. "They think this place is haunted and we like to keep it that way. In a way it is, and we are the ghosts." 
"Once again you say too much," Queranos said. "Give her the Sleep, Finder. Anaz will carry her the remainder of the way." 
Finder raised her hand, the eerie blue light dancing across Alaina's field of vision. Her eyes fluttered and closed. 
It could have been moments or hours later when a rough tongue licked her awake. Red Paw loomed over her, panting. Alaina lay in snow, under the great rock known as the Anvil. The Woven Ones hadn't even left footprints in the snow. Had she fallen from her skywolf and dreamt the whole incident? She stared down at her wrists. They were still red where Anaz had squeezed them.
She clutched her wolf, letting tears roll down her cheeks. Unbecoming for a Skydaughter, but she didn't care. 
"Red Paw, I have never been so happy to see you."
	
						-<>- 

Wayden, Night, and Rif shared a wagon, pulled by two crotchety draft horses. The boys were quiet and sullen, and their wrists were manacled so they could cast no magic. Wayden's nose itched and he had no way to scratch it. The weight of the iron made his arms feel like they would fall out of their sockets. Night, in contrast, hummed what Wayden assumed was a jaunty tune, though she was so off-key it was a bit hard to be certain. They hadn't bound her hands and she was knitting with black and gold yarn.
"It must be nice to have blind faith that we'll get out of this," Wayden thought. With so many mounted guards around them, there was no way to escape.
 Ahead of them, Sir Jereth Thunderstone and Fire-Whisperer Ko rode thick-bodied Dragonlanders, green-scaled horses. Ko's horse left large droppings on the path. 
Rif nodded his head in the direction of Sir Thunderstone. "Is that one of the C-C-Companions? Like Sir Longreach?" 
"Aye." Wayden's chains clinked as he moved. "He's my least favorite of them. During the Selection tournament, he insisted on the ancient tradition that real weapons be used. A woman in the crowd got too close and lost an ear to one of Thunderstone's missed blows. When his opponent turned to aid the woman, Thunderstone thrust the blade through his back."
"And they still made him a Royal C-C-Companion?" 
 "No one ever accused the Dragonknights of being overly soft. It's cold steel that makes them, not a warm heart."
The chill of autumn was replaced by the warm humidity of Cook's Lake, as the caravan descended into Devil's Valley, zigzagging down switchbacks.
"Mistress Night," Rif said. "What did you mean we won't all arrive at the prison?" 
Night had black yarn wrapped around her fingers and her needles were crossed. "I foresaw that your burnt friend here has to play tug of war with the Skymaster over a fiery cat. And as for you, Rif, I see that you will play your own deadly game of chase with Sir Thunderstone."
Rif's face grew pale at news of this prophecy.
Wayden felt his anger twist like a red hot dagger to the gut. "Rif fights Thunderstone? I fight Gar over a fiery cat? Talk plainly, for the love of the Source."
"I speak as plainly as the water that greets us," she gestured with her knitting needles at Cook's Lake. Night spoke as plainly as this water at least, which was a froth of murk and foam, erupting in spots into spouts of angry mist. 
On a distant island in the center of the large lake, rose the Tower of the Loons. Wayden wondered how they were able to boat people out there without getting scalded.
To the east, rose the volcanic fortress known as the Red Palace. Its crater had been sculpted into a dragon's mouth and the sides of the mountains folded wings. Was it Wayden's imagination or was a squadron of soldiers riding their way from the castle? Thunderstone must have noticed it as well, for he ordered the caravan to a halt.
"Riders heading this way," Thunderstone shouted. His eyes must have been keen, for it took Wayden a moment to notice what the Dragon Knight had.
