In the distance, tiny dots rode down a switchback road from the Fire Gate dug into the side of the volcano. The dots turned into horses as they drew closer, and the sound of galloping hooves grew louder.
Night smiled. The yarn on her needles appeared tangled up. "The future is riding our way."
 "If she says one more enigmatic thing, I swear I'll throw her in Cook's Lake myself," Wayden thought.
"Being enigmatic is no crime," Kolram said.
"No. Only saving people from scagazi is."
"The Dracon condemns you as unjustly as you condemn Night." 
Soldiers galloped towards them, holding aloft the banner of Helos: a dragon in front of the sun. As the riders drew closer, Wayden identified Swiftrider, a Royal Companion, leading a squadron of mounted Flickers. Swiftrider rode on his famous Streaked Lizard Horse, Green Lightning. 
	"Now, this Royal Companion is more to my liking," Wayden whispered excitedly to Rif. "That's Swiftrider, the winner of last year's Race of Fire. You should've seen it. Swiftrider won by jumping Green Lightning over a shortcut: a channel of lava." 
	Swiftrider handed Ko a parchment bearing the Dracon's wax seal. 
	While Swiftrider spoke in a hushed voice, Ko's was raised in anger. He thrust the parchment back in Swiftrider's hand and turned towards Wayden. "Young men. Come hither. Now." 
	A Flicker helped Wayden and Rif out of the wagon. They stumbled forwards, chains clinking, across rocky ground. Wayden's legs were numb from the long wagon ride but the manacles were the worst. He'd heard about prisoners who had to wear them day after day. He didn't know how they could bear it. 
"Hail there, young magi," Swiftrider said, "Your skills are being requisitioned by order of his majesty Dracon Niar, son of Terok, Possessor of the Red Blade, Wearer of the Crown of Fire, First Seat upon the Burnt Throne, heir to the Dragonking, and leader of the land of Helos. A dragon was sighted in northern Deep Woods. The Dracon ordered us to bring it back. You will use your magic to acquire the dragon." 
A tightness compressed Wayden's chest. "What? Even Kolram couldn't control Volkanus. And how am I to cast magic with my hands shackled?"
"If you capture this dragon, your freedom will be restored to you." Swiftrider said. "Do you swear upon the Holy Flame not to try to escape if I release your bonds? Will you undertake this mission on behalf of Helos?"
"I promise I'll try my best," Wayden said.
"I will do my b-b-best to help him," Rif said. 
A Flicker unshackled and removed their manacles. 
Wayden rubbed his red and sore wrists. "I can try, but even Kolram couldn't control Volkanus. How do you know I can control this dragon?"
 "This dragon is smaller than Volkanus," Swiftrider answered. "The Dracon believes you will be able to control her." 
"Her? A female?"
Ko, leaned down from his scaled horse, and smacked Wayden hard on the back of his head. "Do you see this seal, boy? It is a direct order from the Dracon. His royal majesty is not in the habit of having his orders questioned by burnt orphans."
Burnt boy, Toast, burnt orphans - they lived in the Land of Fire, yet they treated him like an anathema, because he wore the mark of fire's kiss. Wayden felt a different type of fire well up inside of him, but bit his lip.
Ko's ice blue eyes bore into Wayden. "You will bring that dragon to us, or you can swim in Cook's Lake. I'm not sure which would give me greater satisfaction."
"Troops!" Swiftrider bellowed. "Fall in. Direction, South Fork."
Wayden clambered back onto the wagon, feeling some satisfaction that his wrists were no longer manacled and the possibility of freedom had been returned to them.
"N-n-night was right," Rif said. "She said we'd be diverted. Do you think her other prophecies are right too?"
If they were, then Wayden would be freeing the Shadow Queen. He couldn't see that happening.
Wayden was glad to see that Swiftrider and his men joined their cadre of soldiers. A plump, yellow-robed healer rode up to Wayden on back of a tan palomino. He was a sandy-haired man, with a vine tattooed on his face. The vine encircled the image of an apple. He was sucking on a licorice stick. He pulled another from his satchel and handed it to Wayden. "I'm Healer Conrick. Pleasure to meet you."
Wayden thought he might die of shock from meeting someone in the Red Guard who was actually pleasant. He took the sweet warily. It looked like a twig or a cinnamon stick. He'd eaten sweets like this when he was little. He half expected a Cook-like gag, where Conrick would squeeze his hand or give him something disgusting. He placed the stick in his mouth warily. His tongue tingled with the sweetness and flavor. Conrick handed a candy to Rif as well. 
"Th-th-is is delicious," Rif said. "Thank you."
Conrick smiled. "One gets as much from the giving, as the getting. With that he spurred his horse forward.
Wayden shook his head in disbelief, examining his chaffed wrists. "This day is going a lot better than I expected. Now let's just hope we don't actually run into this dragon."
Their caravan turned south around the road that looped the lake, and took the southern junction up a steep hill. The road passed wattle-and-daub houses, wooden shacks, and straw huts. It wound past farmlands, fields of wildflowers, and vast stretches of grassland. It rolled over hillocks and traversed wooden bridges and high-running streams until they reached Deep Woods. 
The forest was a riot of color. Autumn had turned the green leaves into a quilt of copper, bronze, and gold. The fallen leaves crunched beneath hoof and wagon wheel. The air turned cooler as they rode, and Wayden pulled his hood tight.
 The rhythm of the road lulled Wayden into a dream, or was it a memory of Kolram's drifting across his mind? Kolram was in a large chamber with grooved wooden walls, studying with his teacher, Grandmaster Baltoo. His fellow acolytes Gar and Belza were dabbing feather pens into ink pots and scrawling on parchments. 
Gar had yet to lose hair, but scar tissue covered where his eye ought to have been. He'd said to Kolram once, while they were both sharing a bottle, that his mother had taken it for looking at what he wasn't supposed to. Gar was dressed in the maroon robes of an acolyte, not the shiny black leather of a Sky Raider. He already wore his pearl necklace and a gold armband. 
Wayden wished he could go back in time and warn Baltoo about Gar. 'Don't teach him. Don't make him stronger. He's going to kill you.'
Kolram had been the one to find Baltoo's body, a memory Wayden had seen in many a nightmare.
Grandmaster of Beast Tongue, Baltoo-the-Gentle, petted a sick cat, which had curled up in his lap. His head was shaven, but his beard was long and purple. "Soul-stealing is a dangerous process," Baltoo lectured. "And one we had thought lost, until Arth and Gior's recent rediscovery of Raylar's texts."
Baltoo had assigned Kolram the task of finding out more of what the Soul-stealers were up to, but so far Kolram's espionage had achieved nothing more than getting a goblet of brandy tossed in his face.
"There are five states of matter," Baltoo lectured. "Solid, liquid, gas, energy, and spirit. Spirit can be converted to energy or even gas."
"He's already full of gas," Gar muttered to Kolram and Belza. Neither student laughed. 
If Baltoo heard Gar's mutter, he said nothing. "When someone dies, what do you think happens to them?"
Kolram had always been puzzled by that question. Do souls just cease to exist? 
"They go to the Great Flame Lands," Gar whispered in a sarcastic tone. "To be friends with the fire angels and the lava imps," 
Baltoo had surely heard him. Why did he not reprimand Gar? Instead, he continued, "No energy disappears. The energy is simply transmuted into a different form. Think of rock changing into magma and then hardening again into rock, or, if you prefer, mist becoming rain and then rain into the sea."
"If a spirit is changed to energy or a gas," acolyte Belza asked, her shock of red hair bobbing, "would it still be a spirit?"
 "And do stones live? These are age old questions." Baltoo said. "We know a gas, energy, or stone cannot grow or breed, but can it be imbued with spirit still? What does it mean to live or to die? Are there true beginnings and ends, or are we simply in a constant state of flux?"
Baltoo's cat meowed pitifully
. Kolram sensed something from the cat. A relinquishing of will. He gestured towards the feline. "She's dying, isn't she? Is there anything we can do?"
"Nothing physical," Baltoo answered. "But we can remember her. No energy truly disappears. This cat has been a faithful pet. More faithful than some of my acolytes." His eyes seemed to rest on Gar as he said this. "This feline and I share a spirit bond. When she dies part of her will live on inside of me, as I will live on in inside of you, when my time comes."
Gar laughed. "It's a wraithin' cat. When it dies, you should stick it on a spit and cook it. Then it'll truly be part of you. Animals respect strength."
"And what is strength, Gar? Is strength the ability to frighten others or to inspire them? Is it to control others or oneself?" Baltoo asked. "Fear is a powerful tool, but a double edged one. You can gain surface control, but never a true and lasting loyalty."
Gar jabbed a finger in Baltoo's direction. "As long as they're afraid of me, that's all the loyalty I need. Why do I even bother coming here anymore? I'm a better Beast Tongue than you, old man. You should retire and let me be the Grandmaster."
"If you have no more to learn from me, you should leave, yet the most important skill eludes you. Wisdom. Power without wisdom is like fire without a hearth. It is dangerous and deadly. I'd no sooner make an unwise man my heir, than to assign the task to a forest fire."
Wayden opened his eyes and saw a ceiling of dazzling leaves. How long had he been asleep? Perhaps moments, perhaps hours - the road was endless sameness, and yet paradoxically endless diversity: every leaf slightly different than the last.
Wayden stared at the leaves thinking on Kolram's memory. "Gar was awful, even back in his early days. I'm surprised Baltoo allowed him in his school." 
"Baltoo's fault was giving people too many second chances," Kolram responded. "He was convinced he could save Gar, but Gar did not want to be saved."
 Low hanging boughs of cedar and hickory hung over the wagon. Rif had dozed off, leaning on Night's black cloaked shoulder. 
A league down the road, Sir Swiftrider brought his dragon horse to a sudden stop. He turned, his brow furrowed.
 "Bodies."

-<>- 

Jazlyn clutched her mother's necklace, the stone warm against her chest. I don't know whether I should be grateful to Gol for giving me the necklace or angry that she hadn't done so sooner.
 Jazlyn walked briskly towards the southwestern part of the Red Palace, known as the Commons, Org at her side. Mother might be locked away somewhere and Ember Haldur might hold the answers. What would Jazlyn do about it, if she was? Would she be in a position to help her mother? 	
"One step at a time, first I must find her," Jazlyn thought to herself. 
"She's likely dead," Asgaroth said.
"Lock your lips."
"My lips are a hundred leagues south, in a temple of stone."
"Would that your poisonous words were trapped there as well."
"What is so poisonous about the truth? The Dracon had no reason to spare her. What is poisonous is allowing yourself false hope."
A drunken Flicker stumbled out of a tavern, almost knocking her over. His breath stank of whisky. "Hello . . . beautiful . . . ." 
 Org stepped between Jazlyn and the Flicker. The drunk's head was level to the Ozac's massive chest. He tipped his helm. "Oh, I'm sorry, Sir. Is this your daughter? A very lovely - hic - day to you both."
The Flicker stumbled off. Jazlyn tried not to smell or touch anything as she made her way past the tavern. A moment later, they reached the South West Loading area. Barrels, boxes, crates, and sacks were being loaded and unloaded by a dozen sweaty workers. 
 Jazlyn recognized Ember Haldur's pock-marked face from Gol's description, besides he was the only one wearing the blue cape of an Ember. Two Flickers were inspecting people's papers as they came through. Jazlyn approached Haldur and said, "Ember Haldur. A word. Privately."
"It would be my honor, Your Highness. Shall we retire to the commerce office?" 
"That will suffice."
Haldur led her up a wide hallway, until they reached a small stone room, which served as the office of public records. Two acolytes were sorting through parchments. She commanded Org to wait for her outside and Haldur told the acolytes to take their midday meal. She sat opposite the Ember, across a small pine table. 
"What an unexpected honor this is."
"I require assistance for which I'd be most grateful." Jazlyn laid three shiny gold coins on the table.
Haldur glanced at her, surprised. "You don't have to do that, Daughter Draconi." 
"I insist."
He smiled. "Well, who am I to refuse an order?" The coins clinked as he slipped them into his pocket. "What can I help you with, Your Highness?"
Jazlyn's voice was soft, more from emotion, than fear of being overheard. "My birth mother. What happened to her?"
Haldur's face turned white. Shaking, he fumbled in his pocket, attempting to return the coins, which spilled on the floor, but Jazlyn stayed his hand. 
"You'll tell me-"
"I can't."
"Or I'll report you for taking bribes."
"You wouldn't . . . you insisted I take it."
 "And whose words will they believe? Now-you are going to tell me where my mother is."
"Dead." Haldur slammed his hands on the tabletop, overturning an ink pot, which flowed like a pool of blackened blood. "Dead and buried, all right . . . ach, look what you made me do. I'm sorry, Your Highness. Your mother was a fine Draconess. A beauty. But even pretty flesh withers in the end. She's dead and gone. Let her enjoy the rest of the dead. Poking where you don't belong, it won't do nobody no good."
"Dead. You're sure?" Jazlyn heard the words come out of her mouth, but somehow they felt disconnected from her body.
Haldur didn't meet her eyes. "I'm sure. I had the misfortune to see it happen with my own eyes."
Jazlyn wished she hadn't come here, hadn't asked, and hadn't forced the truth from him.
 No.
 It was better to know. Anything was better than not knowing. 
"How did she die?" Jazlyn felt her mother's necklace, warm against her neck.
Haldur looked away, trying to busy himself shaking the excess ink off the stained parchment. He was making the mess worse.
"I asked: how did she die?"
Haldur slapped the parchment down on the tabletop and reached for Jazlyn's hands, his fingers staining hers black. "Child. Princess. Save yourself some grief. This is something the devil would spare you."
Jazlyn felt her chest tighten. "You will tell me."
"I won't."
"Now. Or I'll have my guard come in here and beat it out of you."
"She struggled as they took over Cook's Lake to the Tower of the Loons and she escaped my . . . the guard's grasp. I reached in to pull her out, but it was too late. She . . ."
"Tell me."
"Boiled to death calling your name." 
Jazlyn's inside coiled. Where her heart had been was now a frozen wasteland. 
Haldur slammed a gauntleted fist against the table. "Wraithin' hell, girl, look what you made me do. Are you happy now?"
Happy? What was happy? She'd once heard of the word, in another life. Jazlyn bit back a tiny sob. Not now. She would cry later. No one could see the Daughter Draconi cry. Her mother's necklace seemed to whisper to her, "You're all right, Jazlyn. I'm still here with you. Be strong, sweet dragon."
Haldur leaned across the table, his voice the softest of whispers. "I'm . . . I'm sorry. I'm so sorry. I loved her, you know. We all did. She was a good woman, the Draconess. The real Draconess, not the cow who calls herself the Draconess these days. So beautiful. The paintings don't capture it right. The Dracon sent her to the Isle of the Loons, but she leapt off the boat into Cook's Lake, calling your name. I . . . tried to warn you. There's no comfort here. Some truths ought not be told."
Jazlyn wanted to scream at him. Instead, she rose. "Thank you. I'm glad you told me." She wanted to fall on the floor and sob, pounding her hands bloody against the stone. Instead, she turned and walked out of the room as if she were in a trance. 
Were these her feet that were moving? Was it her hand opening the bronze door? 
"Mother. Why can't you be alive?"
"I am," a woman's voice whispered in her mind. "I'm inside of you."
"I'm losing my mind," Jazlyn thought.
Org stood there, his large, liquid red eyes staring at her with a curious expression.
Her voice was hollow. "Let's go, Org."
The huge Ozac stopped her and placed a meaty finger under Jazlyn's chin. He said, "Little Princess needs to cry."
"I'm fine," she lied.
Org raised an eyebrow. "Little Princess not fine."
"Oh, Org." She leaned the side of her head on his huge gray chest. She could hear his heart beating, larger than a human heart. She sobbed for what felt like a long time. Finally, Jazlyn sniffled and pulled her head away from Org. She straightened her hair. 
With a sausage-sized finger, Org brushed a tear from her eye.


Chapter 16
A Roar that Shook the World

Prophecies are slippery fish. Trying to avoid them is often what makes them come true.
 - Night
-<>-

The wind shifted and the smell of corpses assaulted Wayden. 
The smile vanished from Healer Conrick's portly s face. He galloped on his palomino, leaping off to search the bodies. After several moments Wayden's wagon caught up. Conrick shook his head slowly. "No survivors."
Wayden's wagon pulled to a stop a mere ten paces from the corpses. Rif retched over the side of the wagon. 
"Arrows and wolf bites," Swiftrider had removed his gauntlets and his hands were covered in blood. "Unless wolves have learned to fire bows, or men to chew like beasts, this is Sky Raider work."
Ko adjusted his silver veil. "Bandits killed by raiders is almost as excellent as raiders killed by bandits." 
	"These aren't bandits or raiders." Healer Conrick felt the corpse's wrists with his pudgy fingers. "These are Woodsmen. See the tattoos?"  He lifted the wrist of a corpse which was covered with a weaving-vine tattoo. It matched the tattoo on Conrick's cheek. Terrifying tales about the Woodsmen robbing and maiming people abounded, and Wayden was surprised to hear Conrick defend them.
	"If they lived in the woods, they paid no taxes," Ko said. "And that makes them bandits."
	"Robbing someone means you're a bandit," Conrick said. "Living in the forests means you're poor."
	Dragon Knight Jereth Thunderstone laughed. "How else did they survive out here, if they didn't rob?"
	Conrick cleared his throat. "Nuts, berries, roots, trapped game, and hunting with bows and slings. We fished the streams and survived on what the Primordial gave us." 
 "You were one of these . . . Woodsmen." Thunderstone said, running his blade's edge against a whetstone. He appeared to be the most uninterested in the corpses.
	"Proud to be one." The vine tattoo on his cheek coiled as his face hardened. "It was a hard life but an honest one. I learned as much herb lore from the woods as I did from tomes. In fact, one balances the other."
A Flicker had found a body beneath a towering iron bark tree. "Sir, this one's breathing."
	Ko rode over, dismounted, drew his dirk, and thrust it through the wounded Woodsman. "There. Now he's not."
Wayden went cold. Ko was nothing but a murderer and a pompous one at that.
	Thunderstone laughed. "You're my kind, Fire-whisperer."
 Conrick reddened. "That was badly done, Sir."
	"It is no mercy to let a man die of festering wounds."
"I could have healed him. You might have at least allowed me to try."
 Ko turned away from the healer, cleaning his blade with a cloth. 
	A while later, Conrick was still brooding, riding alongside the wagon.
	"I'm s-s-sorry Ko killed the Woodsman," Rif said.
"Your sympathy is a rare untarnished jewel," Conrick said. "I hope age will not robe you of it."
A Flicker guiding a pack mule chimed in. "Ko ought not to have done that. The trees have eyes in Deep Woods and the Woodsmen avenge their own."
The woods whispered and groaned about them as if in agreement. A wind picked up, singing, and Wayden stiffened. The trees swayed from side to side, casting long, dancing shadows. Wayden felt like he could still smell the corpses, even though they had travelled far from them by now. 
Swiftrider yelled. "More bodies! Flickers this time. Hurry, one is breathing."
	Conrick spurred his horse, leaving their wagon in a cloud of dust. By the time they caught up, Conrick was crouched over a Flicker, examining his wounds. The rest of the squadron of soldiers lay as decimated as the Woodsmen had been. Their bloody robes bore the Helesian emblem: a silver dragon in front of a white sun, but silver and white had drowned in a sea of red. 
Wayden recalled Dade's argument with the Draconess over purchasing the troops better armor.
Ko ordered the survivor set into the wagon. "Tend him as we ride, we have no time to waste."
"It's not wise to move him yet-" Conrick said.
"Move him on the wagon. Now." 
The Flickers obliged.
"Gently!" Conrick shouted. His face flushed, as he clambered into the wagon, and stripped the bloody cloak from the injured soldier. His wound beneath was a weeping red sore. Wayden fought back the urge to vomit, trying to be as brave as the healer.
 "Can I help?" Wayden asked Conrick, but it was the wounded Flicker who responded, his voice barely a whisper. "My necklace. It helps me. Put it on me." 
	Wayden glanced around, but no one else seemed to have heard the man. Conrick was fetching honey, lard, and muslin from a supply basket. 
The Flicker opened his hand. Between bloody fingers a golden necklace emblazoned with a leaf rested in his palm. The chain had been cut in half, but Wayden bound it together around the man's neck. Instantly, color returned to the man's face.
 "A leaf. The symbol of the Immortal Bantos," Kolram said.
The wound closed and healed itself before their very eyes. The man clutched the necklace in a closed fist. 
	Conrick turned back around to apply gauze, and froze, a look of astonishment widening his features. "You must be a Descendant of an Immortal to heal like that. Amazing. What's your name?" 
	"They call me Dragonclaw," the man said, pulling his blood-matted silver hair back into a pony tail. "Anyone have something to drink? I have quite a thirst."
	Rif handed him a water skin. Dragonclaw took a sip and spat it out. "What the wraith - are you trying to poison me? This is water!"
	Conrick laughed and handed the man a wine skin.
Wayden whispered to Dragonclaw. "Don't mention your necklace to Ko our leader. Don't let on that you've healed completely. He's not to be trusted."
Dragonclaw nodded. "Thanks, boy."
	 At twilight, they arrived at South Watch. Four towers rose from the corners of the wooden palisades. The planks on the southeastern tower had suffered scorching. Men on scaffolding removed blackened timbers and replaced them with freshly hewn logs. 
	A Flame strode out of the postern gate, flanked by half a dozen Flickers and a female healer in flowing yellow robes. The Flame's eyes sought Dragonclaw. 
	"Fire-Whisperer, thank you for returning one of my men."
Conrick and the healer woman helped Dragonclaw from the wagon. Dragonclaw, feigning weakness, rested his arm helplessly across the healer woman's bosom. She repositioned his arm quietly.
"Did you see sign of the rest of the squadron?"  the Flame asked Ko.
	"Dead. A few leagues down the north road. Ravaged by Sky Raiders." Ko showed the Flame the parchment with the Dracon's seal. "We are on a mission of the utmost importance. Have you seen a dragon?"
	"Only Dragonclaw left, of my entire scouting party?" The Flame paled. "They were two dozen of my best. Did you bury them?"
	"None of them asked for a burial, or seemed to mind that we didn't waste crucial time giving them one. I'll repeat myself. The dragon. Have you seen her?"
	"You didn't bury them?"
	"Are you deaf, stupid, or insubordinate? If you force me to repeat myself one more time, I'll have you trialed by fire."
	The Flame turned to one of his men, a gangly man in the blue cloak of an Ember-ranked soldier. "Take two units and a wagon to bring the bodies back."
	The Ember nodded and waved to several Flickers who began readying the wagon. Ko's face reddened. 
"These delays are insufferable. I'll ask you one last time-"
 "You already asked me one last time. Aye, we saw the dragon. What do you think scorched our walls? A late autumn thunderstorm?"
	"Which way did she fly?" 
	 "South by South-East. Cat-like face, just like the mother of Volkanus in the paintings. Young. Not much bigger than a warhorse, white as Tulkarian ivory. A pretty thing."
	"I don't recall asking your aesthetic opinion."
	"I'll waste no more words then, My Lord." The Flame said. "Will you be staying the night? We cannot house all your soldiers, but they can sleep in our bailey. We can clear a room for you in one of the towers."
	Ko shook his head. "I'll sleep with my men. How about the Sky Raiders? Any sightings of them?"
	"Got a pigeon today as a matter of fact saying winged wolves were sighted over Edgewater. They didn't attack though, just flew past."
	"That will be all for now. Open your bailey."
	"Open the gates!" The Flame called.
	"The Dracon will hear how you questioned my orders," Ko said. 
	"As you say, Sir."  The Flame spurred his horse back through the portcullis.
 "We should turn back on the morrow," Swiftrider said to Ko after, "The Dracon ordered us back by the ninth. If we run into delays, we risk missing the deadline."
Wayden wasn't sure what to hope for. Which option was worse-being dragged in front of a dragon or being thrown in a prison? As usual, his options seemed to range from bad to worse.
Ko glared at the Dragon Knight. "The Dracon gave us a parchment with his emblem on it bearing orders to bring back a dragon. No deadline was mentioned."
"Orally, it was."
"A codex-stamped message is what I'll abide by. I'll brook no more arguments."
	That night the temperature dropped sharply. Wayden, Rif, and Night huddled together. Breakfast was hardtack in the wagon before sunrise. South Watch shrank away as the horses clip-clopped south east. They rode past a busy lumber camp on the river. Logs were being poled downstream.
They rode for a notch longer, up and down hills and valleys. Flurries thickened into light snowfall, but then tapered off again by midday. An ancient stone ruin slumped under a cliff face, the remnants from some ancient civilization or tribe. A huge mirror tree grew over what had been the temple entrance. Its bark was flecked with crystals, glittering in the sun, an ancient arched doorway nestled beneath its roots, though the walls around the door were all but gone. A thumping sound, as regular as a heartbeat, resonated faintly from below their feet.
 "That's a temple of Bantos," Swiftrider said. "Back in the day, the Druids studied and practice Grower Magic there."
"What's Grower Magic?" Wayden wondered.
"Tis a form of enchantment more common in Tulkar than in Helos," Kolram said. "They control foliage with their power."
"What happened to Bantos?" Wayden asked, his stomach heaving, as the wagon rolled over a root.
"No one knows," Kolram answered. "He was the first Immortal that disappeared. Many assume Centuron captured him, like she did with Asgaroth, Dragonking, and the Shadow Queen, but his body was never found. Others say he is still around today, posing as a beggar, and if you throw a coin in his cup, he'll grant you three wishes."
Wayden watched the temple shrink into the foliage as they rode away. He wished they could stop and look at the temple. He felt drawn to it, and his rear end was sore from riding. He'd told them from the start he could no more capture a dragonthan the sun, but would they listen?
If they were going to throw him in prison, they might as well take him to the Red Palace and be done with it. It would still be better than endless riding. Or would it? If this was tedious, what would it be like spending day after day behind iron bars? At least here he could taste fresh air, see the fireworks of leaves exploding from the trees, feel the cold wind of freedom. When he was young he'd seen a Glower mage street performer dragged off for putting on a show without authorization. Had she been sitting in a prison cell all this time? And for what? Entertaining children was such a terrible offense? And Rif's mother hadn't even done that.
"We should make a run for it," Wayden whispered to Rif and Night. "I don't want to end up in the Dracon's prison."
"I thought they said we w-w-won't be if we bring back the dragon."
"I don't think I'll be able to do it. Kolram couldn't control Volkanus."
"This dragon is sm-sm-smaller."
"It doesn't matter. Ko doesn't know what he's talking about. Beast Tongues are good with different types of animals. Kolram is generally better with warm-blooded animals."
"Run or stay, it won't matter," Night said. "You won't end up in the Dracon's prison. You'll end up in Gar's."
Wayden's skin prickled. 
"What do you mean?" 
"I see you bound to a tall tree, by the one eyed-vulture. The vulture's chick is with you. Then I see you in the stone nest."
"Gar captures me? When does this happen?"
"Soon."
"Is there any way to avoid this?"
 "All junctures lead to it. Prophecies are slippery fish. Trying to avoid them is often what makes them come true."
Wayden brooded on this as they made camp in a clearing in the center of a heavily wooded area. Flickers established a perimeter of spears. Wayden, Rif, and several Flickers were sent to gather firewood in the twilight.
 They returned just as the sun set, sighing as they unloaded the heavy fuel. Ko and Swiftrider were arguing in loud whispers over some parchment, while Conrick organized freshly picked herbs. Thunderstone had brought back a stag and the smell of roast venison soon filled the air. 
Wayden and Rif huddled close to the fire. If only Ko had allowed them to bring a change of robes. It was too cold to wash.
Wayden craned his head upwards. The cloudless sky was awash with countless stars. The constellation known as the Eye stared at them in heavenly judgment. Rif handed Wayden a piece of hot venison dripping with juices. 
Wayden smacked his lips. "I haven't eaten this well in seven years." 
"I don't think I-I-I've ever eaten this well."
"That soup you and your mother made smelled pretty good."
Rif swallowed.
"Y-y-you Glimpsed that?"  
Wayden leaned in towards Rif and whispered. "Aye. At night when we were sleeping. Gar might have been the better Beast Tongue, but Kolram had the Glimpse."
"G-g-gar wasn't really a better Beast Tongue. He had Raylar's God Weapon, the pearl necklace. It amplifies p-p-power."
Wayden's jaw dropped. 
"This explains much!" Kolram said.
An owl hooted in the dark.
"Are you sure? How do you know that?"
"Pretty sure. R-R-Raylar wrote a tome about the God Weapons."
"Rif, did Arth know what Dakarth and Dracon Niar were doing with Soul-stealing magic?"
Rif ran his finger along one of his seashell beads. "Arth couldn't understand what they were up to exactly, but he m-m-mistrusted them. He kept a lot to himself and fed them as much false information as he dared to."
 "Why did all the souls go into newborns?" Wayden asked.
"The baby's s-s-soul is in a state where it won't resist a second soul's entry," Rif explained. "The two souls become linked." Rif inched closer to Wayden. "Raylar studied wraiths. Wraiths can cohabitate with a host. He applied the same principle."
Wayden poked the fire with a stick. Sparks hissed like angry cats. "So it was Arth's false information stopped them."
"Delayed them for s-s-sixteen years. This is the first Three Moons' Night since our birthday coming up."
"Things didn't go as planned for Dakarth and Niar on Three Moons' Night. They were quite upset about it. But if something doesn't work out the first time, you try again right? By now they have probably gathered the information they need. Rif . . . is Arth the Striker?"
"No. Maybe. I don't th-th-think so. It might be Belok. I thought we had him mentally imprisoned, but I'm not sure." 
"I don't understand. Who's Belok?"
"A year before we were born, Arth returned home to the cottage in Raslo, where he and his sister, Genika, were staying. The door to the cottage was wide open and there were tracks in the snow, footprints and what looked like a sled. Or someone being dragged into the c-c-cottage. The tracks were sprinkled with blood. Arth rushed into the cabin. Belok was on t-t-top of Genika with a knife, st-st-stabbing her."
"Source have mercy."
"Genika was d-d-dying . . . Arth's rage was out of control. Soul-stealing is linked to emotion. Arth had only meant to suck Belok's soul, not Genika's too."
"Wait, so they are all inside of you? Genika with the soul of her murderer?"
Wayden recalled the woman's voice inside of Rif. That must have been Genika!
Rif nodded, tears running down his cheeks. "Arth, Genika, and I- we trap Belok in a mental prison of sorts, but sometimes he escapes and we have to put him back in. He hides in the recesses of my mindscape. It's hard to c-c-catch him."
How terrible it must be to have a murderer hiding in your mind. A murder. Like the Striker. If Belok could get free from time to time, was it possible he was the Striker?
Wayden held his cold hands up over the glowing embers. "Rif . . . the woman who was found dead in the pine grove . . . she was a red-haired woman just like Genika. You were with Big D when he died. You blacked out."
"I don't know what happened!" Rif threw up his hands in distress. "I don't think I k-k-killed anyone. Belok is trapped."
"But you just said sometimes he escapes."
"Yes, but . . . Oh, Source no! What if it is me?"
Wayden studied Rif's face. He looked genuinely upset.
 "Denial can be a powerful obstacle to overcome," Kolram said. "And if this Belok is in his mind, who knows how much he can manipulate Rif."
"Could you do that to me?"
"Possibly. I wouldn't. It's a morally repugnant."
"Just like Belok."
Rif looked close to tears. "Do you think I'm k-k-killing people? How can I stop it? What should I do?"
Wayden rubbed his burn-marked forehead. He exhaled a small cloud into the cold night air. "I don't know."
A Flicker approached. "You two. No talking. Stamp out them coals."
Rif threw dirt on the remaining embers. Wayden laid his head on a pile of crunchy autumn leaves and fallen pine needles. He stared up at the stars. The constellation of the Eye stared back at him. In the distance crickets chirped. A shooting star flew overhead, trailing a tail of gold and blue.
Wayden fought off sleep. He was afraid Belok might take over Rif and kill him in his sleep. When he finally drifted off, he dreamed of being chased by a veiled man with black wings. Wayden climbed through tunnels, through a wood, and into a mire, but still the man pursued. Wayden turned and confronted his assailant, yanking his veil away to reveal Rif. Rif shrank away, but holes opened in the ground all around him. Each hole contained someone: his nanny, his mother, Kazor, Mavik, Big Darius, a red-haired woman. 
Wayden rushed to Mavik's hole. As peered through the depts, he could see through to the other side of the world. 
"Wayden," he heard the voice of his mother call. "It's coming."
 He looked up and saw her, pale as milk, floating in the sky surrounded by a sphere of energy. She clutched a bouquet that was a mixture of red roses and purple arrows. She handed him an arrow. "The dragon. It's coming."
"I can control the dragon, ma. I'm the Dragon King."
"No," said a voice like a roar. "You're not."
Wayden bolted upright, wide awake. 
He heard the dragon's voice again. "I am Harth. I am fire. Beware my wrath."
The sentries looked half-asleep, slumped against their spears. Wayden walked, half in a trance, past the perimeter of half-buried spears that surrounded the camp in a make-shift fence. Swiftrider was on duty, mounted atop of Green Lightning. His scaled horse flicked its forked tongue, its hooves and scaly tail digging grooves into the muddy ground.
 "You're supposed to stay within the fence," Swiftrider said, rubbing his hands together.
The dragon's thoughts felt louder now, closer. "I am claw. I am fire. I am doom. Out of my way Beast Tongue, you are nothing to me."
Wayden's skin prickled. He was now as awake as if someone had poured a bucket of ice water on him.
"Sir Swiftrider!" He stepped towards the Dragonknight. Green Lightning's ears pricked and she snorted. 
 "She nears," Wayden said. "The dragon comes!"
 "Easy, girl," Swiftrider said, steadying his horse. "Are you sure? I don't hear anything. You were just dreaming." 
Wayden reached out with his mind, seeking the dragon.
"Do not try to hold me, Beast Tongue," The dragon thought. "Interfere with me, gnat, and I'll cook you and eat you. You are nothing. I am flame and death. I am Harth."
Ko, from behind the fence of spears, shouted, "What is going on?"
 "The dragon. . ." Wayden said.
But then they heard it. A roar that shook the world. 

Chapter 17			
In the Belly of a Dragon

Yield? You may as well request the hurricane succumb to your breath. - Harth


						-<>- 

Jazlyn parted the silk drapes that enclosed her four-poster bed. A folded yellow note sat upon her goose-feather pillow. Unfamiliar handwriting read: Magi in Plague Room. Your father up to no good. You are in danger. Burn this note. It was signed Rebel.
She read the message thrice, then paced the room. Who could have left it? Her new maid, Ravenna? Impossible, maids weren't literate. Could it have been Gol or Haldur? Neither had access to her room. Verica? Why would she bother with a cryptic note? Org? Now I'm just being ridiculous. Perhaps I shall visit the Plague Room.
"Perhaps," Asgaroth said, "this Rebel wants you to go there, in the hope that you contract the disease and die," 
"Maybe I should die," Jazlyn thought. "Then you would die with me and the world would be safe."
"Safe?" Asgaroth asked. "You are badly misinformed. Do you know who started the Second Dark War? Darius Dragonking. His Sword of Luminosity brought more darkness than light. And your father is as bad as he ever was. You Red-Landers, you're red from the blood on your hands, not the fire in your veins."
 Her head ached as one of Asgaroth's memories pounded through it.
She was Asgaroth now, sitting across a stone table from Darius Dragonking. The fool didn't even realize he had crumbs in his long red beard. He shouted arguments over borderlines as usual. Asgaroth let his two sons, still in their twenties, argue for him. Dakarth and Karsgoth were better at it than he was, even at such a young age. They cared more. Asgaroth was tired of it. The same old argument that went nowhere. 
Asgaroths eyes kept gravitating towards Darius's wife, a mortal of such beauty that the Silver Lady herself had surely sculpted her: sparkling eyes, magic smile, and blonde curls cascading over her delicate shoulders, But the work of art was marred, a bruise inflicted on her eye.
 Darius's work. To hit a woman was despicable. True, Asgaroth craved bloodying the Shadow Queen or the Weaver in battle. To strike a defenseless, mortal woman like this went against the will of the Silver Lady. The Dragonking was a monster. How could Asgaroth have ever looked up to the brute? Darius deserved death, and if his soldiers chose to support him, then they die too. 
Asgaroth's memory faded.
"You loved this Lyssa, didn't you?" Jazlyn thought. "I'm sorry you lost her. Finding out my mother dove into Cook's Lake, calling my name -."
"You dare compare your petty loss to mine? You're a gnat." 
"And you're a voice inside a gnat's head."
"Not for long."
The smugness in Asgaroth's tone prickled Jazlyn's skin. Did the Bone King have a plan to escape? And who'd left the note? How could someone have obtained access to her bedroom? 
Jazlyn went into the main room. Her maid lay sleeping on a divan. 
"Ravenna," Jazlyn said. "I need your assistance."
Ravenna sputtered and sat up, her tousled black hair defying gravity. She blinked sleep from her peach-colored eyes. "What ails My Lady? Is it your headaches again?"
"I require strong tea."
"Yes, My Lady."
"Did anyone enter my chamber today?"
Ravenna filled a kettle from a basin of water. "Not that I noticed, Your Highness. But I'm afraid I sleep most sound."
"I don't trust this Ravenna," Asgaroth said. "I smell a spy."
"And I smell a distrusting dictator who thinks killing people is okay as long as you're just making a monument out of their bones. How could a simple maid conduct espionage and rebellion?"
"Who better to spy than a maid?  Who can overhear lords and ladies talking while being completely invisible in front of your pompous nose."
Jazlyn's insides squirmed. Could Asgaroth be right? 
"Your Majesty?" Ravenna asked. "What ails? You seem to have drifted off."
"I most certainly did not. Ravenna, I don't know much about you. What was your mother like?"
"If it pleases My Lady, I'd prefer not to talk about it."
 "You see? She avoids the question," Asgaroth said.
"Something painful probably befell her mother, "Jazlyn thought. "When I learned my mother died it made me feel . . ."
"Angry?" Asgaroth suggested. "Like you wanted to do something to strike back against the worm that calls himself a Dracon? The snake that calls himself your father? And what if that snake struck down Ravenna's mother as well? Would she do everything she could to bring down the government?"
Jazlyn frowned. It was a possibility. "Ravenna, what thinks you of the manner in which my father rules Helos?"
Ravenna let out a tiny chuckled, before making her face stone again. 
Jazlyn raised an eyebrow. "That was a question, not a jest."
Ravenna placed the kettle over the hearth. "I'm sorry, My Lady. Why ask me? I'm just a maid, and never offer my opinions on matters of weight." 
"Why not? Do maids not have brains?"
"In spades, Your Highness. That's why we don't offer our opinions."
Jazlyn smiled. It was a strange sensation. Her face had grown stiff and masklike. This is the first smile since I found out . . . her smile vanished. She died in boiling water, screaming my name. 
The amulet around Jazlyn's neck grew warm. For a moment, Jazlyn thought she heard a woman's voice whispering, but she couldn't make out the words
"Did you hear something?" Jazlyn asked Asgaroth. "A woman's voice?" 
"Death-speech."
Death-speech was one of the forbidden forms of magic and all such Magi had fled Helos long ago, to places like was the Temple of Shadow and Light in Kaldia. Had Jazlyn heard the voice of the dead? Tension gripped her shoulders. 
A portrait of the Dragonking with his seven beautiful wives hung on the rear wall. Could Asgaroth's Death Speech abilities be affecting her?
"Do you speak to Lyssa using Death Speech?" Jazlyn asked.
A memory of Asgaroth shot through her mind. He was holding back tears, after Karsgoth delivered the news. Lyssa, dead. Beaten to death by the Dragonking. 
"Are you sure he killed her?" Asgaroth asked his youngest son.
"Three of our contacts confirmed it, father," Karsgoth said. 
Asgaroth drew his Sword of Night. It's black metal glittered with lights, like winking stars in the night sky. "Then he shall pay."
The memory disappeared, but Asgaroth's sadness and anger lingered inside Jazlyn, a tide that washed away everything precious.
"I've been led to think of Asgaroth as the monster and Darius the saint, but things aren't that simple," Jazlyn thought.
"The Land of Light- more like the Land of Lies," Asgaroth said.
"I might have learned more sooner had you done more than growl at me when I was little. Why did you spend the first dozen years inside of me silent and sullen?"
"How do you think it feels for me, being in the body of the princess of fire? Being in the palace of the Dragonking?  Looking at his painting, seeing the face of the man who murdered my love? Darius did not love Lyssa. He kept wives like the Sky Raiders keep wolves. She was nothing but chattel to him, and everything in the world to me." 
"You Immortals were not Gods," Jazlyn mused. "You're just fools like us."
"I'm nothing like you." 
"And I thank the Source for that."
"One day, I'll be free of you and then I'll-"
"Tear my bones out?"
"One by one."
"Are you alright, My Lady?" Ravenna asked. "You seemed lost in thought."
Jazlyn faced her maid. "I command you to answer my question honestly and plainly. I won't breathe a word of reproach for any answer besides silence, which I would consider deliberate insubordination."
Ravenna twisted the ends of her long black curls together nervously. After a moment she said, "Very well, but I hold you to your oath, for what I speak might be construed as treason. These arrests of magi are unjust. Your father and others practice magic, and yet they arrest others for doing the same. What's more, it is unwise. The magi are one of the lines of the defense. Imprisoning them is as dangerous as surrendering our arms and dragon. My own parents are now in the pl . . . are in custody."
"It's you!" Jazlyn exclaimed. "You left me the note."
Ravenna paled. "That wasn't me."
"What wasn't you? You never asked what note. And you were about to say Plague Room."
The kettle was hissing. Ravenna tried to pour the water into dragon-enameled tea cups but her hands were trembling.
This is my chance. Vengeance for what was done to my mother. Justice.
Jazlyn took the boiling kettle from Ravenna's hands. "Oh, Ravenna, don't you see? I want vengeance for my mother. I want to be a rebel too."

-<>- 

"The dragon is here," Wayden meant to sound brave, but his voice squeaked. 
"I hear her. The deaf hear her." Swiftrider's brow creased, his eyes narrowed with resolve. His reptilian horse, Green Lightning, flicked her tongue. Mist rose from her scaled snout.
 Several sentries sank to their knees and nocked arrows. Others raised steel-tipped javelins. Wayden shook his head. What good were spears and long bows against a dragon's thick-scaled hide? How would chainmail protect against dragon fire?  In the stories, the knights triumphed, but in the histories it was the dragons.
The wiry she-dragon appeared overhead, morning sun glinting off her white wings. The Flame's description had been accurate: not much larger than a war horse, with a cat-like face. She let out a belch of flame. I hope she doesn't set the forest on fire.
 Every emotion and its opposite raged through his body: dread and excitement, terror and wonder, despair, and hope. Maybe he could control the dragon. Wayden imagined himself on dragon back, Gar Skymaster trembling on his knees below him. Defeating the Sky Raiders by himself wouldn't be impossible with a dragon on his side. He could do it. He just had to believe in himself. 
Wayden reached out with his mind, "By wing and fire I command you. I seize your heart. Your scales are my armor. I wear you." 
When Wayden influenced a rat or a dog, their minds bent like wet clay. The dragon was more like solid brick. "Man Child, your flesh is weak. What are you to Harth? Harth was born amongst earth and fire. Harth's mother's milk was lava. Harth is searer of bones, eater of flesh, and burner of worlds. The man child is nothing." 
"I'm your master. You will yield to me!"
"Yield?" The dragon continued its flight. "You may as well request the hurricane succumb to your breath. Do you expect the mountains to bow to your height? Fire to freeze for you, dead men's blood to re-enter their veins?"
The dragon disappeared behind a gray patch of clouds.
"She's getting away!" Ko shouted. 
 "Getting away?" Wayden shouted. "We're lucky she didn't toast us." 
Ko grabbed at the spear-post fence, like a Tulkarian ape straining at the bars of its menagerie. His silver veil quivered and a vein protruded from his forehead. "Failure is unacceptable. Swiftrider, take the Beast Tongue. Bring back that dragon or don't come back at all."
"Aye, Lord Ko." The Royal Companion pulled Wayden onto Green Lightning. The scaled horse galloped, clawed hooves and spiked tail leaving tracks in the ground and broken foliage in its wake. 
Two other Flickers mounted their palfreys, but they soon fell far behind Green Lightning's cheetah-like pace. The creature leapt over logs, boulders, and streams, swerving between tree trunks, forcing riders to duck beneath low lying branches. Trees whirred by, and Wayden held onto Swiftrider for his life.
"This isn't going to work!" Wayden shouted over the pounding hooves. "The dragon's will is too strong for me. I've tried my best."
"You will succeed," Swiftrider answered, ducking beneath a low-lying hickory branch. "Or Ko will have your hide."
 "I'd rather Ko have it than the dragon."
"Courage, boy." Swiftrider steered Green Lightning around a gray iron-bark tree. The horse leapt a moss-covered log.
"Is this courage?" Wayden wondered. "It feels a bit like madness." 
 "The Royal Companions often confuse one for the other," Kolram said.
Maybe they'd lost the dragon's trail. But then he felt a rush of wind and the smell of sulphur. The dragon was flying straight at them.
 "This is going to hurt!" Wayden thought.
Was this where his destiny lay? In the belly of a dragon? Green Lightning leapt a granite boulder and burst into a brown meadow of dying grass. 
As the dragon grew closer, Wayden balled up all the strength he could muster. "Dragon! Tail, claw, fangs, and flame, you are mine. You will bend like grass to me. I command it."  
 "Puny man child. You will not own a single scale. I feel your wolf riders approaching, but they will avail no better than you did."
"Wolf riders . . . Sky Raiders? Harth, listen to me, you have to get out of here. The leader of the Sky Raiders is a bad man and a powerful Beast Tongue. Don't let him come in range of you."
"Harth is scared of no man."
Wayden could feel Gar's presence now. It was approaching like a storm.
"Please, Harth, listen to me. You must flee." But it was too late. Wayden heard Gar's voice in the dragon's mind. It felt like nothing Wayden had ever experienced, it was like seeing a mountain for the first time, when all one had ever seen before was plains. Gar's power dwarfed Harth's, as Harth's strength dwarfed Kolram's.
"No. . . Impossible . . . such strength. No mortal could possess . . ." the Dragon thought.
	"Flee!" Wayden cried out, feeling the power of Gar's magic seize the beast. 
"Too late," Harth thought. 
"No! Gar can't win."
 Wings beat overhead, furs and feather became the sky. Wayden's stomach clamped. The Sky Raiders had Harth and they'd have him next. 
Wayden shouted to the Royal Companion, "Sir Swiftrider, I've lost. Gar Skymaster has control of the dragon. We have to get out of here."
"Nay. We bring the dragon back with us, or we shall not return at all."
"That's exactly what I'm afraid of."
"The fool won't understand this is a battle we cannot win," Kolram said.
The dragon landed in the clearing, not ten feet from Wayden and the Royal Companion. The dragon's head bowed, her tongue flicked against her lips, and she lay on her wings - all signs of submission.
"Take-" An arrow thudded into Swiftrider's jugular. Blood spurted on Wayden's face and the knight slumped off the side of Green Lightning. Wayden managed to hold onto the scaled horse, even with his eyes closed and his stomach roiling in horror.
"Swiftrider!" Wayden thought. "No! I'm cursed. Death follows me like a dog."
"Remain calm, we have to escape," Kolram said, "Think. You can't control the dragon, but you can control Green Lightning. Get us out of here."
Wayden spread his fingers and turned his wrists skyward. He shouted aloud, "Hoof, and mane, run like thunder, save us from this colossal bl-"
A weighted net sent Wayden sprawling. He tumbled onto pine needle cushioned ground, in a tangle of hemp cord. The scaled horse bolted into the trees, several arrows embedded in her side.
The wolves landed in a circle around Wayden. The more he struggled against the net, the more it snared him in its fiber tentacles. A tall Sky Raider wearing a lacquered goat's mask leapt off a winged wolf. 
Wayden's stomach lurched. The goat man that had taken Mavik had been no nightmare. Here he was in all his horror. Black studded leather covered his body, but no gloves or gauntlets. His hands glowed bright yellow with dancing specks of purple.
"It's Kolram's host," Goat said, examining his hands.
"He's a magic-finder," Kolram said.
Gar Skymaster fingered his necklace. "I thought I felt a gnat pulling at Harth's mind." 
Rif had said Gar's necklace might be Raylar's God-weapon, a power amplifier. No wonder Gar was so powerful. 
"All these years," Kolram said. "I thought I was a failure because Gar was the better mage, but it was all from a God-weapon." 
Wayden squirmed, while muscular Sky Raiders bound and gagged him. He wanted to retch, not so much from the taste of the filthy rag, but from the flavor of failure. A dozen feet away, Gar Skymaster might as well have been a million leagues out of Wayden's reach. 
The Sky Raiders strapped Wayden on a skywolf, its matted fur stinking of dried and frozen excrement. His wrists were bound and fastened to a hemp cord that stretched from the saddle through a leather loop. 	
There was no escape.

Chapter 18 
The Plague Room

It's human nature. We don't acknowledge the world might be about to blow up under us. -Verica

-<>-
Verica 

Verica grit her teeth. Turning to wraith form was as comfortable as jumping into an icy lake in winter. A stinging sensation started at her scar and spread across her body. Within a heartbeat, her body numbed and the pain faded.
 "The things I do for Jazlyn," Verica thought. "Peel off my skin. Rush into labs. Spy on kings." 
 "Why profess doing it for Jazlyn when we both know your motivation is curiosity?" Lukor, the wraith who resided inside of her, asked.
Verica grumbled. Jazlyn was lucky. Asgaroth only tore bones, he wasn't a know-it-all wraith who called you on every half-truth.
It felt strange having no one in the apartment. Her father and his assistant had traveled to Kaldia for a Healer's conclave. Her father left in such a hurry, he almost left without leaving coin or provisions. Luckily, Verica helped herself to some coins from his money bag. She'd been debating for hours on whether or not to spy for Jazlyn, but it all came down to this. She was too curious to ignore it. Things were not adding up. What was the Dracon up to? 
Verica left her apartment. A Mantu servant stared at her. Can she see me? No, she's probably puzzling over how her door opened and closed by itself. Verica stuck to the edge of the stone corridors, making her way past a gaggle of children on their way to the school room and a pair of Flickers making their rounds. 
She reached the gilded gate and passed several more guards as she entered the off-limits area, the Court of Flames. The huge cavernous chamber was nestled in the center of the Red Palace, beneath the crater of the volcano.
On the north side of the room, sat the Burning Throne with a ring of basalt benches surrounding it. On the eastern side, beneath a hanging tapestry of the Dragonking, an acolyte practiced projecting tendrils of fire into the air. Servants knocked on doors, delivering trays of food: slivers of pepper-fried pulled pork and roasted potatoes drizzled with honey. Verica had eaten lunch not an hour ago, but the smell still made her mouth water. Wraith form always worked up her appetite.
 On the southern side, lay the dragon, sleeping. Volkanus's head and wings rose from the deep caldera of boiling lava with every thunderous snore. The dragon rarely left the healing bath these days, and even so he looked terrible. His scales had flaked off in large chunks, and cantankerous boils dappled his raw flesh beneath. His golden eyes fluttered open only for moments at a time. What would become of the Palace if the dragon died? The volcano wouldn't erupt with a dragon feeding off the magma, but without Volkanus nothing stood in the way of an explosion. 
"This whole place could erupt," Verica thought, "yet everyone stands around complacently waiting for the dragon to recover."
"I must admit, I find this surprising myself," Lukor said. "Why is the palace not evacuated?"
"The Splashers claim that when Volkanus dies, he'll be replaced by another," Verica explained.
"But prophecy is an inexact science. Wouldn't it be wise to take precautions?" 
Verica maneuvered past another guard station. "It's human nature. We don't acknowledge that the world might be about to blow up under us. We just go about our business." 
The southern side housed Verica's destination: the Dracon's office. She headed through a wide, obsidian corridor. Verica ran her hands over the surprisingly smooth stone. 
Verica's tutor had told her the Dragonking had dug the palace himself.
"That is a fallacy. The Dragonking did not practice Digger magic. Two millennia ago, Centuron dug the tunnels with earth magic."
"I thought Centuron and Dragonking were enemies?"
"So were Asgaroth and the Dragonking at one point," Lukor said. "Allies turn enemies, and enemies become allies." 
"Is it true that Centuron trapped the wraiths as well as the Immortals?" 
"Centuron's Order of the Guardian trapped me," Lukor said with no hint of bitterness. "That much I can attest to. I cannot say with certainty what happened to most of my brethren, as I was one of the first wraiths to be captured."
"How were you captured?"
"I was sent as an envoy to talk to the Immortals. Dragonking ambushed me, killed the host I was linked to, and Centuron's son trapped me in the sarcophagus."
"I'm sorry."
"I fail to see how it's your fault."
"I just mean I sympathize."
"Why would you do that?"
"I mean . . . never mind! Just leave it!"
The passageway widened as she entered the Royal Chambers, where the highest ranking officials held their offices. She passed Glower magi in white shawls, Lesser Beast-Tongues training wolves or hawks, Fire-Whisperers, dozens of acolytes, servants and guards. She hugged the walls to avoid crashing into anyone like she had with Wayden. She'd been careless then, rushing too fast. If she made a mistake like that now, it could mean her life.
A honeycomb of doorways dimpled the stone walls, each with a different insignia: an armored fist for defense, a golden coin for the treasury, a wolf for the skywolf kennel, a water droplet for Prophet Crow, and the flaming crown marking the Dracon's gilded door. It was engraved with an emblem of a crowned dragon in front of the sun. Two magic-eaters and a pair of Flickers stood at either side of the entrance, along with the largest of the Royal Companions, Sir Oz Strongfist. 
Some claimed the Strongfist family descended from Ozacs, and Verica might have believed it, if his skin were gray. The muscle-bound Dragon Knight stood near seven-foot tall. Verica had made the mistake of watching Strongfist fight in the Choosing and she still had nightmares of the mess he'd made of his opponent.
"You sure the Magic-eaters won't affect me?" Verica thought, eying the slug-like creatures held on chains by Flickers.
"Yes. Raylar's creations interrupt source-derived magic, while wraith form is a biological process-"
"You're like my father. The more you explain, the less I understand."
Fire-Whisperer Dade strode down the corridor and shoved a parchment with a codex seal into Strongfist's gauntleted hands. The Dragon Knight glanced at it, knocked on the Dracon's door. An acolyte answered. "Chief Treasurer Dade seeking access to your Majesty."
"Granted," the Dracon's voice sounded from inside the room.
 Verica entered behind Dade, a shadow within his shadow. She moved too quickly and stepped on the back of the Fire-Whisperer's robes. Dade paused midstride, a puzzled expression travelling across his brow. Verica tensed.
"Something ail, Your Lordship?" Strongfist asked in his deep, booming bass. 
Dade stared right at Verica. Finally, he shrugged. "No, nothing."
Dade entered the Dracon's chamber. Once inside, Verica ducked into a dark corner, near a tall wooden bookshelf, behind a table where two acolytes were writing on parchments with quills. 
The Dracon's quarter was crammed with hundreds of ancient ceramic vases, suits of Dragonknight armor, vials filled with viscous liquids, jewel-encrusted skulls, necklaces strung with coins, drum lutes, colorful cross stitches, thick white furs, and buxom statuettes. Dozens of cabinets, shelves, and chests lined the room and a large closet in the back overflowed with labeled chests and drawers. It looked like her father's lab, packed with a thousand curiosities.
A painting of the Dracon hung from the wall behind the actual tyrant. The artistic rendition portrayed a man trying to looking heroic, arm extended, chin raised, and stilted resolution written on his brow. The real Dracon resembled a bureaucrat. He sat behind a desk, and not upon a warhorse, and he was surrounded with stacks of parchments not epic battle. Niar ceased dictating to his acolytes and looked up at Dade wordlessly.
Dade handed the scroll to one of the scribes. "Your Majesty, the acolyte we suspected was indeed embezzling. My men have accounted for every coin he's taken and it adds up to five hundred and forty."
"You said there were nine thousand gold-bones unaccounted for."
"There are. But it wasn't the acolyte that took them."
"Then who?"
"Perhaps we should talk of this matter in private."
"My scribes are sworn to secrecy. Any word you say in front of them shall not be repeated. Who took the money?"
"You did . . . Your Highness. Here is the proof."
Dade handed Niar yet another parchment.
The Dracon's face reddened. Then paled. Then finally, broke into a a laugh. "Impressive, Dade. You're both smarter and stupider than I thought. I command you not to speak of this to anyone."
"Help me understand why, Sire."
"You over-estimate your importance." The Dracon refastened his golden veil. "The allocation of those resources is classified."
"As Treasurer of the Court of Flames, how can I balance the budget, without knowing where our treasury went?" 
"How can I be expected to govern a country without secrecy?"
The argument had seemed promising at first, but soon went round in circles, until even Verica's foot fell asleep. After a notch, the Dracon dismissed his treasurer. Dade left with one less shadow than he had entered with. 
Remaining quiet proved harder than Verica would have guessed. A sneeze was building up that she couldn't repress. She let it out at the exact moment Oz Strongfist announced, "Beast Tongue, Belza, daughter of Baltoo, Dragon Keeper, and Mistress of wolves seeks entrance!"
"Yes. Yes," the Dracon said in an exasperated voice. "Is everyone determined to visit me today?" 
 Belza pulled up a chair across from the Dracon, her shock of red hair swaying like a burning bush. "Your Majesty, the chase for the dragon is on. The Beast Tongue and Swiftrider are in pursuit."
Verica perked up at this. Another dragon? 
"I thought Volkanus was the last of his kind," she directed her question to Lukor.
"Clutches of dragon eggs are laid as deep underground as the dragon can hide them," Lukor said, "Sometimes they do not hatch for hundreds of years."
Belza handed a parchment to the Dracon. "Sky Raiders are in the vicinity as well."
"Raylar's Teeth! We have to hope Gar doesn't get to the dragon first. Delay the prisoner transport a day, have the skywolves ready to depart two days prior to Three Moon's Night."
Belza nodded.
"Very well, dismissed," the Dracon said. 
Verica wasn't sure how long her shadow form could last. She had to leave soon, but she had yet to hear anything truly useful.
Oz bellowed, "Chief Prophet Crow seeking access to his Majesty."
"Ah, at last. Enter," the Dracon said. "Crow. What kept you?"
Verica wondered the same thing herself. 
"I apologize for my lateness," the Prophet answered, adjusting his lacquered beak.
The Dracon dismissed the two acolytes. Verica took that as a good sign. When the door closed behind them, the Dracon turned to Crow. "So the two children host Arth and Kolram? It's confirmed?"
"The pigeon came in from Ko a few moments ago. It's confirmed." Crow unfastened his black cloak, but despite the warmth in the room, he left his bird mask on. "Are you sure this is wise, to risk them on this venture with the dragon? If they die, or their return is delayed till past Three Moons' Night, you are denied three powerful magi."
 The Dracon paced the room, almost crashing into Verica. "It's of the utmost importance we acquire this dragon. Volkanus is dying." The Dracon turned and studied his own portrait. "Crow, how old are you?"
"Old enough to know not to say."
The Dracon chuckled. "Well, Crow. You might be too young to remember how bad things were under Dracon Coralis." The Dracon stepped over to a portrait of his father, Terok the Terrible, a huge man with a scowl on his face. He ran his finger across the bottom of the frame. "The man almost brought Helos to ruins. Our military was weak, our coffers bankrupt. Great nobles were destitute and had to dismiss their servants. Even my own father . . ." Niar turned away from his father's portrait and stepped close to Crow. His voice grew so soft, Verica almost couldn't make out the words. "I swore to myself if I were accepted for the Great Choosing, I would run things differently. I would make sure the Drakingdom was as powerful as possible. And that's what I will do no matter what the cost."
"I understand." Crow stepped in front of the door. Verica trembled. Her power was waning, but the prophet was blocked the exit. 
Verica chewed her lip. "I'm going to get caught."
"Not necessarily," thought Lukor, "Perhaps you'll be lucky and the volcano will blow up first."
"I should never have explained sarcasm to you."
Crow stroked his beak. "I saw nothing in the water about you acquiring a new dragon."
"The water doesn't tell all though, does it? What about Dakarth? Do our sources in the Bone Palace have any word for us?"
"Dakarth's planning on freeing his father. He doesn't want his advisors jeopardizing that with any subterfuge. He is aware you have eyes in the Bone Castle."
"Free Asgaroth? But he's inside of Jazlyn," Verica thought. "How do they plan to get him out?"
"Perhaps they have discovered a way of putting Asgaroth's soul into a new body," Lukor said. "Or they have discovered a way of breaking the Guardian field and returning him to his original body." 
The Dracon returned to his cluttered desk, sorting absently through parchments. "Very well then. Dismissed."
Crow bowed and departed, unaware he was followed by a second shadow. 

-<>- 

The Draconess and Jazlyn stood beneath the gaze of a tall Flicker with a silver mustachios. Next to him lounged a second Flicker, short, with traces of greasy-black hair smeared across a balding head. The tall one's chain mesh draped like a tent across his skinny frame and the short one's was tight over his bulging stomach, giving the impression that he was attempting to smuggle a melon beneath his mail. A magic-eater slithered nearby. The horrid creatures always gave Jazlyn ghastly nightmares. She could feel Asgaroth's telekinetic powers being drained by it. Which was a shame, since she felt an urge to tear the bones out of these guards.
The Draconess appeared to feel the same way. "I'm the Draconess! What do you mean I can't enter? 
"It means you can't come in, Your Majesty," said the short Flicker, pronouncing each word slowly. "Enter is a fancy word for come in."
The tall Flicker smacked the back of the short guard's head. "I apologize for my companion's impertinence, Your Majesty. I'm afraid in essence he is correct, however. We must allow no one entrance to the Plague Room by strict order of your lord husband, His Royal Highness the Dracon Niar, leader of Helos-"
"Yes thank you, I know who my husband is." 
But the guard went on unperturbed. "- Son of Terok, First Seat on the Temple of the Third Moon, and first seat upon the Court of Flames, may his ember burn ever luminescent."
"May an ember be forever shoved up his posterior," Jazlyn thought. 
"That can be arranged," Asgaroth said.
"If you want to tear his bones out, I'm all for it."
"Just bring me to him and get rid of the magic-eaters. I'll do the rest."
The offer wasn't without its temptations, but Jazlyn felt her future lay elsewhere than patricide. 
It was infuriating that even the Draconess was being denied access to the Plague Room. Jazlyn had been turned away on an earlier attempt, so she dropped a hint to the Draconess that it would be charitable to visit the sick, not guessing the guards would deny her entrance as well. Still, discovering that the level of security was so high was a type of information as well. 
The Draconess glared at the guards. "I am the Draconess, the highest ranking woman in the Drakingdom. I demand you allow me entrance."
"It's called the Plague Room," said the short Flicker. "It just might be because people have the plague in there."
Or do they? It was becoming clear that the Plague Room was not what it seemed. Doblin had supposedly come down with the plague and was quarantined, yet the day before he'd seemed perfectly healthy. Ravenna's parents had been in perfect health when they were seized. According to Verica, her father had offered to look at the Plague victims, but had been turned away. The Plague Room seemed nothing but an excuse for the Dracon to gather the authorized magi.
The tall guard shook his head apologetically. "What my ill-mannered compatriot is attempting to articulate in his crude, low-brow fashion is that the disease in question is of a highly contagious nature and might pose a threat to her majesty's delicate constitution." 
His translation is harder to understand than the original, Jazlyn mused. He thinks it more mannerly to say no with larger words.
"A servant bearing food left a moment ago. He appeared to be quite alive and well upon his exit," the Draconess said. "As a Descendant of an Immortal, I have never caught a contagion in all my years. I am the daughter of Kero, granddaughter of Borleat, great-grand daughter of Dragonking."
The short guard rubbed his nose. "Yeah, well they can't come in either." 
The tall guard rolled his eyes at his companion. "I am most sorry for my partner's manner, Your Majesty. His heritage is not as noble as your own and sadly more than a little bit lacking. He is the son of a washer woman, daughter of a gambler, and grandson to a whore."
"How come you don't announce that every time I come into the room?" The short guard asked. Turning to Jazlyn he whispered. "He forgot great-grandson of a boiled pig and brother to a chamber pot. Those are allowed in, by the way." 
The tall guard ignored his companion. "His breeding leaves much to be desired, but alas, in essence, his summation is correct. You may not enter."
"Can we just peek in?" Jazlyn asked.
The tall guard bent down on a knee, eye to eye with Jazlyn. He took her hand, and looked at her so tenderly that for half a moment Jazlyn thought he might be preparing to propose. "My dear, I am afraid our orders were quite explicit. No one may, as you say, 'peek'."
"Trust me," the short Flicker said. "There ain't much to see in there."
"No?" Jazlyn asked innocently. "What is there to see in there?""
 "Just a bunch of old people sitting around looking depressed," the short Flicker said, picking at something in his ear.
"So no one in there with . . . say . . . an actual plague?" Jazlyn asked, backing away from a magic-eater that slithered up to the hem of her dress. 
"As for that I couldn't say," the short Flicker said, catching Jazlyn's eye meaningfully. "They seem well enough to me, but what do I know? I'm the great grandson of a mangy stray cat and the half-brother to a dung beetle. Hex me, I can't even tell the difference between a plague room and a dungeon."



Chapter 19 
Fugitives from the Law

There are the wars fought above ground, and worse ones fought far below. -Laeko

-<>- 

Alaina had just given Red Paw a raw piece from the kill, when she felt the Connection spell, grab her gut and tug, hard. After giving her skywolf one last pet, she wandered over to where the burnt boy was bound to a tall, bare-branched, iron-bark tree. 
The Weaver had foreseen this, she realized. 'Free the burnt boy,' the fox-masked Magic-finder had told her. But if she followed that advice, her father would have her executed. How could trust the words of the Woven Ones, anyway?
She shared a bond with this boy though. Zaburn's bond, like she had with Finder and with the slave boy. 
"That means he hosts a grandmaster," Nadra said, "The accursed Beast Tongue."
"How do you know that?"
"You heard him casting the Beast Tongue spell on the horse. Kolram son of Halbreth. My enemy."
A memory of Nadra talking to Kolram by a fountain. He was so handsome with his square jaw and the glint in his blue eyes. Nadra grabbed at him and turned him to her. "Please. I'll change. Kolram. We were promised to each other."
"I'm sorry, Nadra. My heart belongs to another."  Kolram turned away, his red curls swaying with the movement.
 "Our marriage had been arranged by the Court of Flames. You defy a holy edict!"
"So be it."
"The Guardian witch has enchanted you."
"On that we can agree."
Nadra yanked the memory away angrily, but Alaina pushed deeper into Nadra's memory. The scene changed, Nadra stood before Kolram and Solita's two-story house in Adonia. Nadra sent a curl of flame from her lips, encircling the newly wed's house. Flames leapt up in the windows. Kolram leapt out a window, Solita in his arms.
Nadra, cackling, rode off on her winged wolf.
Alaina gasped. "You burnt their house down! You're insane." 
"Fire will wreak its vengeance, something a weak frog-skin like yourself can't understand."
No matter how many times Nadra used the derogatory term Frog-skin for Mantus, it still cut at Alaina. She hated hosting Nadra, but there seemed no way to be rid of her. Once Alaina had once asked her father how Nadra came to reside in her and if there was a way to get her out. Gar slapped her. "You talk about it one more time, and I'll have your tongue cut out." Her loving father. 
The noise of drunken debauchery carried through the night. Over by the bonfire, her father fondled two Sky Raider wenches. Her father disgusted her.
"Of course he disgusts you- he's a barbarian," Nadra said. "All your people are." 
If only she could prove Nadra wrong, but all around her, the other Sky Raiders behaved similarly or worse.
Alaina slumped against a boulder. Thank the Source for Red Paw. The wolf put its head in her lap. Alaina ran her hand over the beast's furry back, scratching between her folded wings.
Finder's words kept passing through her mind: 'Free the burnt boy. Remember the four thousand bones. Save Laeko.' What did it all mean?
Voices carried across the night air. Alaina drew closer when she heard them mention her name. 
"How is his daughter a Mantu?" a woman asked. "Gar don't look like a Frog-skin." Alaina recognized it as the voice of one of the Sky Raiders camp followers.
"A half-Mantu. Her mum's side," said a male Sky Raider warrior. "The Frog Queen Bitch died in the birthing. The whelp killed her own mother, so she be cursed."
It wasn't the first time Alaina had heard of her birth, and her mother's passing, but the words stung anyway. Her mother had been an exiled Alatian Princess. 
 I've killed my own mother and let Laeko be imprisoned, the only ones whoever loved me.
"Assuming your mother loved you," Nadra thought. "For all you know it may be a blessing you killed her."
Alaina moved, inadvertently snapping a twig. 
"You be hearin' somethin'?" the Sky Raider male asked.
"Let's get out of here," the woman said, followed by the sounds of brush crunching.
"You should talk to the burnt boy at the least," Nadra advised. "Kolram might have information for us. I know you are as eager to find a way to be free of me, as I of you."
Alaina stared at the boy tied to the elm. He was thin as a rail, burn-mark on his forehead quivering, tears streaking his dirty cheeks. 
And he might just be her only hope.

							-<>-  

Mavik's breath was a frozen cloud lit by firelight, his whispers solidified by the cold night air. "We need to be gone by Three Moons' Night." 
The other slaves were gathered huddled around a second larger bonfire, nearer the center of the ring of slave tents. Mavik had started a smaller fire, so he and Emerelda could talk alone. The vine tattoo's on her face danced in the fire's glow with each word she spoke. "And your vision be showin' me opening up a doorway? In this anvil?"
Mavik nodded. "You were touching it with the energy snakes and a door opened in it."
The new slave, Laeko, approached. Her hair was gray, and her skin wrinkled, but her eyes gleamed with a vibrancy that seemed to dispel the darkness. "May I sit?"
Mavik patted the log beside him, scooting closer to Emerelda to make room. "Please." Laeko was the oldest Sky Raider Mavik had ever seen. Even her wrinkles had wrinkles. Warts dappled her forehead and chin. "May I ask, why you were imprisoned?" 
 "You may," Laeko answered, "And you have."
Mavik waited for an answer, and then realized her jest. "Well then, I ask it."
"Gar had a statue made of himself, sculpted and erected in the Hall of the Ancients, and had the statues of the Weaver and the Wolf Woman thrown out off the side of the Nest." 
"Ah, so that's how that statue ended up in the woods." Mavik said. "I saw the remains of it while collecting firewood."
"I denounced Gar's foolishness," Laeko continued. "That was the excuse I used to get placed here, but truth be told, I need to be here. Crucial junctures are approaching."
"You're a Splasher?"
"I don't use anything as insubstantial as water for my prophecies," Laeko said. "I'm a descendant of the Weaver. We use threads to see the future." 
"Strand Prophets, friends of devils and demons, cursed be their darkness," Jijari said.
Laeko pulled out a piece of fabric. A thousand images were woven into it, but her wrinkled finger pointed to a green circle surrounded in a halo of darkness. "Three Moons Night." Then her finger moved back to a second image, a crossroad of light threaded with crisscrossing golds and orange threads. "This is a day before, a juncture." Then her fingers moved to a third image, prison bars under a vulture's nest. Her finger moved again, pointing to a red-haired boy and a blonde girl placing a gleaming snake against a black Anvil.
"Same thing you be seein' Mav," Emerelda said.
Laeko nodded. "The Source is the Source no matter whether tapped by strands or the fluidity of water. You need to leave tomorrow."
"Can you see how we be gettin' out of the camp?" Emerelda asked.
"Kava root," Laeko said. 
"Kava root?" Mavik repeated. "Is that a riddle?"
"It's the sort of riddle you slip into someone's drink." Laeko shuffled over to a bush and pointed. "Dig up that Kava bush and get me the root, eh? We'll grind it and make a nice draught. Sometimes guards sleep, eh?"
Emerelda nodded. "I should have been thinkin' of that. Our druid used to be usin' that sometimes."
"Thank you, mistress. Do you want to come with us?" Mavik asked.
Laeko chuckled. "What did you see in the water? Did you see yourselves carrying an old lady while running towards the Anvil?"
Mavik blushed. "Well, no." 
"My path lies elsewhere. Don't you worry about old Laeko, eh? The Weaver's webs will catch me." Laeko tapped the side of her nose, a superstition to ward off bad luck. "Be careful, young ones. Dark things live and die in the Fist. There are the wars fought above ground, and ones fought far below."

-<>-
