Verica jumped as the Dracon slammed his fist against the top of his desk. The mounted animal masks on the walls vibrated. They seemed to be staring straight through Verica's shadow-form.
 This was her third attempt at spying. The last time had been a dismal failure. But, as the saying went, the third try brings either gold or death. She was hoping it would be the former. 
"In my experience, boring can often be preferable to exciting," Lukor said.
"Aye, you're the King of Boring, Lukor."
"Thank you . . . I think."
The Dracon slammed his fist on his desk. "Gar snatches the Beast Tongue right from my hands, and now the burglar expects the robbed to pay."
"Won't we?" Crow asked.
The Dracon stood and paced, the pleated fringe of his long red robe sweeping past Verica's feet. "We have no choice. It galls, but in the long run, it will not matter. Gar will get his just reward come Three Moons' Night."
Crow adjusted his beak. "Well about that, Your Majesty. Gar wants reassurance that he won't end up like the other magi in your sacrifice."
"Curses upon curses. What type of reassurance?"
"The Daughter Draconi must be in his custody before the ceremony. He demands we send her right away."
"You were right," Verica thought, her stomach churning with worry. "Boring is good." The animal masks on the wall seemed to nod in agreement. Verica swayed, then caught herself. Her Source energy was waning.
"The Skymaster knows Jazlyn will have to be cut for Asgaroth to be released," the Dracon said.
"He does, but cut is not killed, Sire. Jazlyn's presence will insure Dakarth's good behavior as well as your own. After all, she's your daughter and the host of Dakarth's father."
The Dracon lifted a figurine of a young girl. "He thinks I'll not sacrifice Jazlyn, but I'll do what's necessary. My father called me worthless. My older brother was far better in everything." His face grew as red as his veil. "But now that my brother and my father are dead, it is up to me to be the strong. A leader makes sacrifices for the good of the many and I'll sacrifice whomever gets in my way."
"Hypocrite," Verica thought. "Jump into Cook's Lake, if you want to do Helos some good."
"Still," Crow strode straight towards Verica and stopped. "You'll have to do without the Skymaster's Beast Tongue abilities. Besides Gar commanding a small army, there is the fact that Dakarth will not take kindly to Asgaroth's host being slain."
"True. True. Well, I must not be too greedy. A hundred magi's powers will have to suffice. After Three Moons' Night, we'll see if Gar is still laughing." The Dracon adjusted a statue so it was even more crooked than before. "We continue as planned. Tonight round up the rest of the magi." 
"You still want to include the Draconess and Dade?"
"We've been over this. You tell me it is a risk, and I tell you it would be more dangerous to leave them a force unchecked. Arguing it a third time won't change my mind. The evidence is ready?"
"It's been arranged. It will be revealed that the Draconess and the Dade have been plotting a mutiny." Crow paused. "I'm sure it wasn't necessary, Your Majesty, but I hope you'll forgive me that I kept evidence that it's a fraud, in case you're thinking of adding me to the sacrifice. Should anything sudden happen to me, incriminating information would come to light."
A vein throbbed in the Dracon's forehead. His knuckles turned white, pressing against the desktop. Then his expression softened, and he laughed. "Well played Crow. Your cunning is second only to my own. So be it. Let it begin!"
"Very well. I shall alert the Fire Guard to begin the round up." 
Crow opened the doorway, giving orders to Oz Strongfist and the Flickers. If Strongfist's face remained passive, as if the Dracon were ordering a salver of pepper fry instead of the imprisonment of the Draconess.
Verica chewed her lip. She had to reach Jazlyn before they did. The tips of her shoes were reappearing from fading shadow. She had to sneak past Crow and the Dracon before she was caught. She edged along the wall, nearing the exit. The Dracon froze mid-stride, eyes on Verica's shoes, which had completely rematerialized. 
The Dracon stared. "How did those . . .is that . . . Berik's. . ."
 Verica seized hold of a corner of a mid-sized cabinet and tried to pull it. It didn't budge. She put all her weight onto it. She strained and it tipped. Knick-knacks, manuscripts, and musical instruments rained onto the Dracon. A Tulkarian string harp hissed in atonal protest as it struck the stone floor.
"By the Silver Lady's Chalice!" shouted Crow. 
The Dracon was pointing at Verica, looking shocked. "Berik's . . . daugh-"
"Berik? Does Your Majesty require a healer?"
"The half wraith . . ." the Dracon gasped. 
Crow moved to help the Dracon while guards rushed in. There was a narrow gap now. Verica rushed through it - and tripped on one of the fallen knickknacks. She skidded across the stone floor, feeling her skin burn. 
Strongfist's great stride took the Dragon Knight straight over her, but one Flicker still stood in the doorway, his legs spread. Verica scurried ungracefully through the gap between the guard's greaves, and shot out, racing like the winter wind.
She could see her own knees, her cuffs, her fingertips. It was strange watching her disembodied nails, Jazlyn had painted them red and orange, floating through the air. She tried to remain calm as she dashed through oncoming Flickers and Fire-Whisperers, who hurried towards the yells from the Dracon's quarters. 
She sprinted around a corner and collided with a Mantu servant whose dislodged dishes clattered against the stone floor. Verica continued her mad dash.
 "Running won't work," Lukor said. "You need a new plan."
Verica looked down and saw Lukor was right. Her entire lower body was visible. As she turned another corner, she spied the door to a supply room. She ducked inside, just as the sound of boots pounded around the corner. 
 The closet contained bundles of rushes, boxes of lye soap, brooms, brushes, buckets, and bags of sweet smelling herbs. The rest of Verica's body reappeared. An alarm horn blew in the distance and muffled voices shouted,
 It wouldn't be long before someone searched the supply room. She left the supply room by a rear door, walking at a brisk pace. 
Two Flickers approached. Her forehead felt slick and her shoulders tightened. Verica waved at them, shouting, "You're needed at the Dracon's!" They nodded and rushed past her. 
"Well done," Lukor said.
"The Dracon knew it was me. He said Berik's daughter."
Verica's stomach twisted. She was in as much trouble as Jazlyn. They were going to be taking the Draconess, Dade, Jazlyn, and who knew how many others into custody. She had to warn Jazlyn, and they had to get as far from the Red Palace as possible. Maybe Verica could find her father at the Healer's Conclave? No, that would be the first place they would look for her.
 A heavy sadness settled over Verica as she realized she might never see her father again. He hadn't been the best father, but he was the only one she had. She would miss him, as well as their servants, like the cook, Ec, and her delicious lemon biscuits. There was nothing she could do about it now. She and Jazlyn were fugitives from the law. 

Chapter 20 
The Shadows Inside

The shadows found me a long time ago. -Rif

-<>-  
	
"No sign of the Beast Tongue, alive or otherwise." Sir Thunderstone lived up to his name, booming as loud as thunder, hard as stone. "Gar must have him or else the Woodsmen got him. Either way he's gone."
Rif's heart sank. It was too much. His father and sisters taken by the slavers, his mother by the Red Guard, Kazor eaten by scagazi . . . and now Wayden too.
"A good riddance to him," Arth said. "Kolram is no friend."
"He tried to help you," Genika said. Arth's sister's presence in his mind had been getting stronger of late. Her calming influence helped them all.
"His eyes were spy's eyes," Belok's soft voice sent snakes of ice slithering down Rif's spine. "You should have given him the gift."
Rif jumped. Belok- how could he have escaped? He, Genika, and Arth had trapped Belok in the mindscape. Rif thought they trapped him a dozen times. It was like trying to drown a cork.
"Focus," Arth said. "We can imprison him again. Breathe."
Rif pictured a peaceful place: a Tulkarian waterfall: fronds of broad-leafed tropical plants on the banks, waterbirds with stripes of pink and gills of orange, strutting with chests puffed out. Then the birds scattered, half diving into water, and half shooting up to the tree tops. Out from the fronds came a silver tiger- with a veined forehead and cold gray eyes - the face of Belok.
 "Breathe," Genika said. "Stay calm."  Her voice warbled, betraying her message. Having her killer inside the mindscape with her . . . it was hard. He could sense Genika employing the Alatian meditative technique: three short breaths, followed by a long one.
Rif tried the technique himself, but his breaths came out ragged and tight. Somehow Belok made Rif forget the most basic of instincts. Fear was Belok's knife, and he used the weapon formidably. 
"Don't give in," Genika said. Her voice sounded calmer this time, and that gave Rif courage. If she could be brave in the face of her own murderer, then surely Rif could do the same.
Short, short, short, long. He saw the mindscape. A silver tiger chased Genika and Arth through a Tulkarian jungle. Rif charged in, imagining spears which suddenly appeared in Genika and Arth's hands. The two of them drove the tiger into a bamboo cage. Rif slammed the door shut with his mind. 
A hand grabbed Rif's shoulder, jolting him from the mindscape. Mistress Night leaned over him. The remains of a campfire smoldered. How long had he been in the trance? He must have been an odd sight.
"Are you alright, dear?" Mistress Night asked.
"Just a h-h-headache."
Her gnarled hand thrust a root at Rif. "Suck on this. It'll help your headache. And your fears. Don't worry dear. The shadows will be coming for us soon." 
 "The Shadows are inside me," Rif thought. "The Shadows found me a long time ago."
The Flickers had found the corpses of Swiftrider and Green Lightning. The skywolves left just enough to be recognizable. They'd searched for Wayden for half a day. 
Ko cursed so loudly his veil fluttered.
 "Your holiness, we must return," Healer Conrick said. "We'll be hard pressed to make it back by the Dracon's deadline."
"Curse of the Faceless," Ko said. "Scouts, forward. Archers, rear guard. Troops, flanks. Fall in."
The clink of boots and the snorting of horses filled the crisp fall air. Gray clouds overhead mirrored Rif's mood. Rif had expected a Flicker to come riding in bearing Wayden on the back of his horse. But now they were leaving, and his friend was gone. Rif's ribs compressed, as if his whole being was being sucked inwards into a whirlpool of despair.
The wagon about-faced northwards, drawn to the distant volcano like iron to a lodestone. The air grew colder, star-like flakes descended, gracing the branches with a crystalline embrace.
On the second day of the return journey, a faint rumbling noise caught Rif's ear. The noise was familiar. Claws striking rock, tearing through sand, pushing upwards, clay swirling. It was sound that had been haunting Rif's nightmares since the last harvest.
"Sc?sc?.scagazi!" Rif yelled. Pincers burst through the lightly snow-dusted ground. 
Thunderstone drew his blue sword, shouting, "For Helos!"
Trembling, the Flickers readied their spears. Thunderstone's blade cleaved through a gap in the scagazi's exoskeleton, severing its neck from its body. The head rolled through the mud and landed by Rif's foot, the creature's cavernous eyes staring into his own.
"Scagazi attacks are rare. Twice can't be a coincidence," Genika said.
"Someone is sending them after Rif," Arth said. "Someone who wants to stop me . . ." 
A heavy force knocked Rif off the wagon, hard ground slamming into him. Pincers gripped him and the acrid smell of Scagazi assaulted his nostrils. The compound eyes on the creature's wasp-like head loomed over him.
Rif's hands were pinned, making the gestures needed for magic use impossible. The beast leaned forward, mandibles like black daggers aimed towards his throat. Rif prayed, "Bantos, forgive me my wrongs."
"And who will forgive Bantos for what he has done to us?" Arth said.
A sensation of burning heat surprised Rif. A whip of flame barreled into the scagazi, searing the brown-skin black. The creature gripped its neck, and Rif rolled loose.
The creature smelt like burnt meat. Ko turned and whispered again, his flame pouring from his mouth, enveloping a second scagazi who shrieked in a high-pitched whine.
Rif scurried behind a thicket, and away from the heat of battle and fire. He kept his head down, listening to the howls and screams, thumps and curses. 
 "Steal their souls," Belok urged. "Grant them the gift, then disappear into the woods."
How had the silver tiger broken free again, so quickly? But even as he asked himself, he realized the answer. Rif had opened the bamboo cage himself. His fear had called to Belok.
"Belok is right this time," Arth said. "Kill. They want to imprison you."
"No!" Genika said. "Flee, but do not kill." 
Rif struggled up a wooded hill, dodging between tree trunks.
 "Men!" Ko's voice boomed. "The soul thief is bolting. Catch him!"
Rif ran faster, noises growing closer and closer behind him: men's voices, crunching bramble, and clinking metal. Reaching the summit, he raced down the hill. A root grabbed his foot, and Rif fell into a murky brook, slamming into rock. Icy water embraced him. Rif pulled himself to his feet, when someone barreled into him knocking him back down. A sharp stone dug into his leg and Rif swallowed a mouthful of water. He pulled his head up, gasping for air. Thunderstone's silver boots were aligned with Rif's eyes. 
"Ungrateful little bugger," Thunderstone bellowed. Gauntleted hands shoved Rif back into the water. The burbling and coldness of water enveloped him, the Dragonknight's armored hand counteracting buoyancy. His lungs burned. He resisted an urge to breathe, willing his lips to remain sealed. They betrayed him. He breathed mud and water.
"No. Help me," Rif thought.
"Let me," Belok thought. "I can give Thunderstone the gift."
 Thunderstone yanked him back out. Rif gulped for air, struggling to get away. Thunderstone must have slipped, for he lost his balance and fell on his ass. Rif shot up and ran. Thunderstone's curses and heavy steps dogged him, growing closer and closer. 
Rif leapt into the branches of a scrappy pine tree. The branch he clung to cracked, and he dangled helplessly. He wasn't high enough to escape the big knight's reach. Thunderstone grasped Rif's ankle, slamming him into hard ground. The Dragon Knight leered, his face a mixture of cruelty and anger. 
"Suck his soul," urged Arth. 
"But don't kill him," Genika said. "Just enough. Stay calm. Anger makes the power unstable."
"Weak," Belok thought. "You can't half way open a bottle. Let him drink deeply from the Silver Lady's cup."
The Source burned to the surface, beneath his eyelids, a fire in his veins. He gestured and the Dragon Knight gagged, his soul mist clinging to his lips. Thunderstone fell to the ground. He grabbed Rif's leg and squeezed. Anger raged inside Rif.
"Stay calm," a woman's voice said, but it was faint, distant.
"Let me give his gift," Belok thought. "It's simpler this way."
Tears raced down Rif's cheeks. Life was so hard. Everything had gone wrong for him from the beginning. If he just let go, then Belok could do what needed to be done. Rif was weak, but Belok wasn't. 
"I'll just let go for a moment," Rif thought.
"No! Rif, you have to fight him!" Genika said. "Breathe. Picture a peaceful place. A time when you were happy."
Rif pictured the beach on the Tulkarian Sea where he and his family used to live. The massive frame of his father towering over his sinewy sisters, all three with their long purple hair, fishing from a log boat.
His elder sister pushed the younger in. They laughed. His mother had a fire going on the shore, and the scent of roasted rain fish wafted through the humid air.
 Rif entered the tepid waters with his net and harpoon, the undertow pulling at his ankles. Something cold wrapped around his ankle and pulled. His world became salt and sand as he went under. He was eye to eye with a lake kraken. No, not a kraken. It had tentacles, but its face . . . veined with gray eyes. It was a face that Rif had seen many times, seared in Arth's memory, stabbing his sister over and over again.
Blackness enveloped Rif.
 He awoke, hacking water from his lungs with violent exhales. For a moment, he thought the water was from the Tulkarian Sea, but it tasted fresh and cold. He lay in the brook Thunderstone had tried to drown him in. Somehow, he'd rolled down the hill back into it. His leg bled where a sharp stone had slashed him.
Where was Thunderstone? Rif turned. The Dragonknight was sprawled on his back beneath the tree Rif had climbed. His head was turned sideways, lifeless eyes staring into Rif's. 
Rough hands grabbed Rif. A Flicker shouted, "Wraithing Tulkarian took out Thunderstone." 
The cold iron of manacles clamped Rif's wrists.
 Conrick fingered the side of Thunderstone's neck. The portly healer shook his head. "He's gone."
Gone. 
With that simple word Rif felt like his head had been shoved underwater again. If he had slain the Dragon Knight, that meant he'd killed the others as well. Thunderstone, Big Darius, they weren't the nicest of fellows, but they didn't deserve to die. And what of all the others? That poor red-haired woman at the pine grove. The girl by the fishmonger's. The little girl by the well. He could still see her freckles. She couldn't have been more than ten. He'd killed her. He was the Striker. 
"I should let the scagazi kill me," Rif thought. "I should let Ko throw me in prison."
"It's Belok," Genika said. "We have to learn to find a more permanent way to imprison him."
"You killed me." The voice of Thunderstone boomed from inside Rif. "You bastard!"
"And me as well," said an angry woman's voice, shriller than Genika's. "You killed me."
"He didn't mean to," said a young girl's voice. "It was Belok."
That stabbed worse than one of Belok's knives. A young girl, an innocent. He'd murdered her. It was as if a dam had broken open, and now the memories poured out. The voices emerged like corpses from a graveyard in the stories of Necromancers. The girl's face turning blue. Tears streamed down Rif's face. I'm losing my mind.
"Make sure the ropes are firm, Ember Timeons," Ko said. "I want you and Ambrose on him at all times. Be a good man, and make sure the boy doesn't leave us all corpses, would you?"

Chapter 21 
The Rope

Will your sanctimoniousness help you sleep tonight? - Alaina
-<>- 

The rope was his enemy. Wayden imagined it a vengeful snake, which punished his attempts to escape by constricting, biting into his wrists till they were sore and raw. His back was thrust against a knot in the elm tree which dug between his shoulder blades. It was as if the world had become his enemy, mocking him.
	Harth looked no merrier. The dragon lay staked and tethered, a dozen paces away. Her cat-like face rested in the mud, lower jaw bearded in grime. She could have snapped her ropes with ease, but Gar's magical bonds were less easily overcome.
The aroma of burning herbs, roast boar, and rabbit wafted over the bracken of Deep Woods from the bonfire. It had been a day since he'd dined on venison with Rif, and the Sky Raiders had yet to feed him. 
The sounds of goblets clinking, bottles shattering, men shouting, and laughter filled the night air. How could the guilty be happy, and the innocents be dead or captured? Why did the Source do nothing?
The camp was as barbaric as he imagined. To his left, two young Sky Raiders stumbled into the brush with a wineskin. To his right, a game of swordplay degenerated into a wrestling match. One of the drunken fighters, a tall human male, pricked a male Mantu. The Mantu threw down his sword and charged the man. It looked like they were hugging except a bloody point of a blade protruded from the Mantu's back. The man dislodged his dirk from the Mantu, letting the corpse drop onto the cold ground. He wandered back to the bonfire, drenched in blood. "I just killed Elkar. Give me some wine." 
Roars of approval met this announcement. One Sky Raider said, "Never liked that wraithin' frog-skin."
	For a while, Wayden was alone, except for the hemp snakes, digging into his flesh with their fiber fangs. He fought the urge to cry. Heroes don't blubber. Even if they felt like it. Even if they needed to. He'd clench his anger like a knife and when the opportunity came, he'd thrust into the slimy organ the Skymaster called his heart.
Footsteps and the sound of crunching leaves altered him to an approaching girl. Half-Mantu, he realized, as he caught a better glimpse of her. Her skin was green tinted and her hair a mix of red and green. Her yellow eyes weren't the cruel eyes of the other Sky Raiders, but softer, wider, sparkling. Her demeanor seemed less cocky, her face pensive. She wore no finger necklace. 
He felt . . . he felt a bond with her . . . the same sensation as he felt with Rif and Mavik.
 "She bears one of the Grandmasters!" Kolram said.
The girl said: "You feel Zaburn's Connection Spell as well, don't you? I can see it in your eyes."
Wayden tried to wipe the look of shock off his face. "A Connection spell . . . Zaburn." It came flooding back into Kolram and Wayden's memories. When he and Solita had been in Dark Fist, Zaburn had been muttering some words. At the time, Kolram has assumed the Sunken Priest had been praying, but what if it had been more than that? A spell to bind them after they had been separated.
"You host Kolram right?" the girl asked.
"Aye," Wayden answered. "Which mage is inside of you?"
The girl spat out a wad of half-chewed red leaves. "Kolram's ex-fianc, Nadra."
 "Source help us," Kolram said.
Memories of Nadra, the grandmistress of Fire-Whisperering, whom Kolram jilted, passed through their mind. She may have cast spells of fire, but her cruel words froze like ice: 'I hope the wraiths take you and your bride both, Kolram. May the Faceless Ones drag you into the realms of the dead.' Any hope of acquiring an ally disappeared like a stone skipped across a mire.
The girl uncorked a water skin and held it to Wayden's chapped lips. 
Is this some sort of a trick? Regardless, the water felt blissful. 
Wayden swallowed. "How did you know I hosted Kolram?"
"You cast a Beast Tongue spell when we captured you." The girl pulled out a square of hardtack and fed Wayden a bite. "And my father's magic-finder said so."
"Your father is the . . ."
"Skymaster. I'm Alaina Skydaughter." 
The spark of hope in Wayden's heart was extinguished with those words.
Alaina screwed up the corner of her mouth, as if appraising a questionable piece of meat. "You look just like your brother. Well, except the burn mark."
"Mavik! You know Mavik?"
Alaina brushed a tangle of red and green hair behind her pointy ears. "He's a prisoner in our slave camp. He seems healthy enough, though a bit scrawnier than you." 
Mavik is alive!
 "Your father's there too, though . . .he's . . . "
"He's what?" Dread coiling in Wayden's chest. "Crippled? Dying? Mad?"
"Well . . . he's been with the slave camp a long time and has gained rank by cooperating."
A traitor. Crippled, mad, and dying would have been better. 
Alaina pressed another bite of food against Wayden's lips. As her skin touched his, Wayden Glimpsed his father: disheveled, standing with the other Sky Raiders, holding a whip, and a rat perched on his shoulder. He spat out the tack. It was too hard to swallow. "My father . . . is . . . a collaborator?"
Alaina turned sideways to stare at the tethered dragon. Shadows played off her high cheekbones. "A lot of slaves seek rank, but only your father was picked. It's considered an honor." 
A shooting star zoomed across the sky. The night sky seemed to be crashing in on Wayden. "An honor. An honor." 
Alaina shrugged. "We're all a victim of our circumstances," She offered him another bit of tack.
Wayden didn't bite this time. "Is that how you justify keeping slaves? Kidnapping people? Circumstances? Is that how you sleep at night?"
Alaina pitched the jerky into the dirt. "I sleep at night by closing my eyes and laying my head on the soft goose-feather pillow my father gave me. Will your sanctimoniousness help you sleep tonight? All you Red-Landers think you are so much better. But are you? With your Mantu servants? How free are they?"
Mantu servants weren't the same as Gar Skymaster's slave camps, but Wayden was realizing this wasn't exactly helping him with this opportunity to gain an ally. His mother used to say, "Tis stronger to listen than to fight.' He bit back the urge to retort and said, "You're right."
Alaina turned away. "No . . . I'm not. When I'm Skymistress, the slaves will be freed. The old Sky Raiders never kept slaves, back in the days when they worshipped the Wolf Woman."
They stood in silence. The pounding of drums echoed from the bonfire, punctuated by shrill celebratory howls, both human and wolf. The orange and yellow moons were full tonight, and it seemed to bring out the beast in all of nature.
Two nights until Three Moons Night. Mavik had painted a watercolor a week before their home burned. He depicted a one-eyed vulture with a blue beak standing guarding fingerless slaves. In the background loomed a giant green moon. 
Wayden met her eyes. "What do they have planned for us?"
"My father's gathering magi for a ceremony the Dracon will conduct on Three Moons' Night." 
"Like the ceremony that killed Nadra?"
Alaina looked away. "I don't know what the Dracon has planned. My father won't discuss it."
The dragon let out a sad whining sound and sank its head deeper into dirt.
"I met another like us-Arth's host."
"Arth . . . "Alaina said. "He was one of the few Grandmasters that could compete with Nadra for the highest cell in the Tower of the Loons." 
A skywolf howled in the distance. 
 "Aye, he was mad enough to study Soul-stealing, a type of wraith magic. That's what Dakarth and the Dracon used on Nadra and the others. The souls traveled like mists and entered babies born on Three Moons' Night. You host one of the souls your father is selling for an outlandish profit."
"What are you saying? You think my father would sell me?"
"You tell me," Wayden said. "He's your father. Is your father's knife blue? When we were young my brother Mavik painted a watercolor prophecy - a vulture with a blue beak, dripping with blood. We didn't know what it meant at the time. Let me ask you this. Does your father love you more than gold?" 
Alaina's golden eyes quivered. "I'll listen to no more from your snake tongue." She retreated into the night.

-<>- 

Mavik waited with baited breath for the drugged wine to take its toll.
 "Does something taste different about this wine?" Desha asked.
"All human wine taste like donkey piss," Skarak replied. He chugged down the goblet and turned to Emerelda, "More."
Mavik was getting nervous. They were out of the sleeping root. A notch later, Desha drifted off, but Skarak was still awake. He stumbled over to Desha and shook him. "Come on. Gar have our fingers . . . he finds out . . . we sleeping . . ."
The Ozac himself then slumped over; his huge gray head resting on the Tulkarian's shoulder. His mouth opened wide, producing thunderous snores. 
Mavik itched with the temptation to slit their throats. The Sky Raiders deserved to die, but what if they awoke? He couldn't risk it.
"The effects of the kava come quickly, but won't last long," Laeko said. "You'll have to run as fast as you can." 
So he and Emerelda raced, pushing against the cold biting wind whistling through the scrubby pines and boulders dotting the valley floor. His heart pounded and his fingers were so numb, he didn't think he'd know it when they'd chop them off. Even his missing pinky felt cold.
No sounds of pursuit followed them. Wind, not wolves, howled across the plains. They reached the broken twelve foot statue of the Weaver's shattered torso and legs.
Emerelda grabbed his arm. "Someone be comin'."
A wolf snorted. Men's voices carried on the wind. The crunching of pine needles grew louder. They hid behind the huge broken statue. A Sky Raider foot patrol approached.
"Wraithin' cold tonight," a Sky Raider said.
"Wraithin' cold every night."  The voice belonged to Mavik's father. The rat with the rat.
 Mavik chewed his lip. He risked a peek through the stone legs of the statue. His father and a blond-haired Sky Raider headed straight towards them. His mouth went dry.
Then Kelsen froze in mid step. His eyes caught Mavik's. My father's seen us. Mavik's heart sank. He and Emeralda would be captured and lose a finger each at the least. Probably worse after drugging two Sky Raiders.
 Kelsen and Mavik studied each other for a moment, the choice being weighed. Kelsen squared his jaw. "I heard something. Over there." Kelsen pointed out towards the pine forest. "Voices."
"Best we check it out then." The blond Sky Raider drew a sword. "I've been wanting a fresh finger."
They headed towards the evergreens. 
"My father . . .he . . . he saved us!" Mavik stared into Emerelda's hazel eyes, stunned.
She shrugged. "I be knowin' he can't be all bad. He be sirin' you after all."
Warmth flushed Mavik's face, despite the cold. As they continued their journey towards Dark Fist, the wind kicked up a spray of ice. Only constant running kept them warm. Mavik's legs stiffened. Emerelda's breathing grew ragged. They forced themselves on.
 They skated more than ran across an icy lake. When they could run no more, they walked. A wolf's howl encourage them into a run again. Past the lake's edge, the ground spiked upwards. The cold seeped into their lungs, their breaths becoming heavy and ragged. They struggled up the icy hill, digging their feet into the ice to prevent slipping. They treaded diagonally, and even so they found themselves sliding more than once. When they at last reached the summit, they were rewarded with a view of the Anvil ahead. They had travelled so far, and it still seemed a distance away.
Emerelda glanced backwards. "They be comin' fer us."
 In the sky behind them, four skywolves flew in front of the orange and yellow moons. Mavik gripped Emerelda's frozen hand, and they increased their pace to a sprint.
Emerelda panted. "Yah . . . Hold on tight . . . to me fingers. Don't let 'em . . . take 'em." 
The thought of them cutting off Emerelda's fingers was more than Mavik could bear. His legs, which had felt like giving out, suddenly gained new purpose. He pushed them faster, dragging Emerelda alongside him. He prayed: "Darius protect us, guide us, let our fires burn bright inside us."
"May the Source Grant you strength," Jijari said. "May you find the power inside yourself."
The bitter wind swept up a spray of snow. The Connection Spell tugged at Mavik from below his feet, from the Weaver's World. Could the Source be leading them this way to another Soul Host?
As they drew closer to the Anvil, the beating of the Heart Stone grew louder, deeper, more resonant. He felt it, as much as heard it. The sound echoed the rapid beating of his own heart. Danger loomed. Terrible danger.
 A chunk of ice beneath his foot broke off, and he fell on his belly, sliding down the steep, slippery hill, towards the base of the Anvil. The coldness of ice slid against his skin and bits of ice kicked up blinding him. Despite this, he caught a glimpse of the huge obsidian rock. He was heading straight towards it. He grasped for a handhold, digging into the hard packed snow. He twisted himself, to try to stop his descent. Emerelda slid too, behind him. The huge rock wall grew larger and larger, his own body would be the ore to be hammered on this anvil. 
He twisted, clawing at the ice. He extended his feet, cushioning his crash. His legs pushed into the rock. A heavy force slammed into his back. The Sky Raiders have me! But then he saw tufts of blonde hair, hazel eyes, and a vine tattoo. Emerelda gave him a sheepish wave. Despite everything Mavik laughed. He stood up on sore and wobbling legs. A skywolf howl pierced the air, sounding too close for comfort.
Mavik helped Emerelda clamber to her feet. He shook snow from his mane of red hair and cloak.
"Can you open the passageway?" Mavik shouted over the howling wind.
Energy snakes glowed on Emerelda's fingers. She touched the Anvil with her Guardian magic, but nothing happened. "Er, did the Source show ya how I be doin' it? Cause, I right don't know."
Mavik took Emerelda's hand and guided it against a crack in the stone. "In my vision, you placed your hand here." In contrast to the cold, her skin burned like fire.
"Let go of me hand." 
Blood rushed into Mavik's cheeks. "I-I-I'm sorry."
"You ain't bothering me. I just need be summonin' the energy snakes. I don't want yer hand bit, is all."
"I wasn't bothering her!" Mavik's heart reversed course from its plummet, and just as speedily rocketed towards the stars. "Does that mean she liked me touching her?"
"Sky Raiders are coming to remove your fingers and you worry about this?" Jijari asked. "The sins of the flesh will blind."
Emerelda studied the rock, running her fingers over the space Mavik had shown her. The howls were closer. Mavik chewed his lip.
Emerelda lifted her hands, spreading her fingers. "By the Order of the Gold, be lettin' us in from the cold." She winked at Mavik. "See? I be talkin' fancy when I needs to."
The Glowing amber snakes slithered towards the center of her palm, spinning in rapid circles, before peeling off one by one and burrowing into the Anvil. A sound like a sigh came from the rock, which glowed for a moment, and then rumbled, a hole sliding open, until forming a large doorway. 
An obsidian ramp formed. They headed down into the catacombs. As the passage curved, the light of the moon diminished. Emerelda summoned Guardian snakes to light the way, for even a dim light was preferable to stumbling in pitch darkness. The distant thumping of the Heart Stone grow louder as they walked further into the blackness. They weren't far in, when a series of flapping and growling sounds erupted from behind them.
	Mavik caught a glimpse of their pursuers: Desha with his bow, the blond haired Sky Raider gripping a spear, and Kelsen with a net. Kelsen had saved them before, so why help the Sky Raiders recapture them now? Had he changed his mind? 
Emerelda conjured a Guardian shield, blocking the passage, just as Desha's arrows shattered against it. 
Desha shouted over the crackling energy. "Drop the shield, girl, and we'll leave yer fingers." 
A lie. They always took at least one finger. Mavik and Emerelda scrambled through the doorway. He looked for a way to close the door behind them, to lock the raiders out, but saw neither hinge nor knob. 
"Me Shield won't last long. Come on," Emerelda said. "We best be movin'."
The amber light of Guardian snakes illuminated only so much and Mavik cursed as he stubbed his toes on a stalagmite. Behind them, something pounded Emerelda's fizzling shield. 
"Can't you cast a stronger Guardian shield? The one around Asgaroth lasted a thousand years."
"Do I be lookin' like Centuron to you? It be takin' a specially strong spell to make a lastin' Guardian Shield. And Centuron had to use blood magic."
"Blood magic," Jijari said. "Blood from each branch of magic."
They ran as quickly as they could manage through the dimly lit corridors. They wove between stalagmites and crouched under low-hanging stalactites. Mavik was beyond tired, but he forced his legs onwards.
For a notch no sounds pursued. Had the shield held after all? The corridor changed, as they travelled, from rough stone to smooth metal. I've never seen so much steel in my life. An army of smiths and a mountain of ore must have been employed, or perhaps a lost art of metal magic. 
The passage was lit by something similar to glow stone, except they were glazed and set in the ceiling at regular five foot intervals. If they were lamps, they had no wick nor oil. Glower magic of some sort?
Approaching footsteps and deep voices interrupted Mavik's reveries. Skarak's bellowing threats were audible. Their pursuers had broken through the shield. Mavik willed his legs to sprint, but they did not comply. Running through the snow had taken its toll, and he managed a pathetic stagger. The darkness slowed their pace even further. Guardian magic shed only so much light, and the Sky Raiders had torches. They would be caught within moments.
"Please Darius, keep her from harm," Mavik prayed. "You can take me, just leave her."
"Child, the Source can help you, but it will not grant you wishes, only wisdom."
Their footsteps clanged against the metal grate as they raced down the corridors. The sound of Sky Raiders footsteps clanged behind them only moments later. They were as good as caught.
There was a juncture, one corridor muddy, the other metal. They left footprints leading one way in the mud and then removed their muddy shoes and jumped from rock to rock in the other direction.
They passed through another chamber with a junk pile of rusted shields and armor. The armor's glass visors lay shattered, atop of metal suits and backpacks. A strange rusted metal carriage lay on its side, split in the middle. 
Clanging footsteps and Skarak's deep voice sounded in the distance. "Look their footprints disappear," Desha said. "It's a trick."
Mavik's insides quivered. That had been their last hope. Emerelda summoned another Guardian Shield, but it had large holes in it. She was as weakened as he was.
They hurried down the corridor. The ground changed back to stone, and then to mud as the corridor snaked lower. 
They rounded a corner, and stepped into another cavernous room, this one traversed by an underground stream. Stalactites hung from the ceiling, red with minerals, like bloody teeth in a monster's maw. 
There was no exit.
"A dead end?" Mavik despaired. "What game is the Source playing with us now?"
"You must climb the cliff," Jijari said.
"What cliff?"
"It's a metaphor."
"You wish to discuss poetry? Now?"
"You are so high up, but you have to let go. Trust the rope. Have faith in it."
"And if it doesn't hold?"
"It does. It will. It has to."
"Let's see if we can find a secret passageway," Mavik said.
"Already on it," Emerelda said, "But no luck so far."
Mavik poked his fingers into crevices, with increasing desperation. Emerelda chanted an incantation. "Earth open your door, we be wantin' to live some more."
Sweat glistened on her brow, but the walls remained walls. The metallic clanging of footsteps and angry voices echoed in the distance.
Mavik's insides jellified. Emerelda mumbled to herself as she searched for a secret door, "The wraithin Source lead us here? Scagazi-humping Splashers with their wraithin' prophecies."
This wasn't how this was supposed to have worked. He meant to save Emerelda, not get her lovely fingers chopped off. The Source had betrayed him.
"Mavik," Desha's leathery voice called from the darkness. "Be sensible. You're making Skarak angry. You don't want that, do you?"
Mavik cursed. Time had run out.
"Skarak want to teach bad boy lesson," Skarak said.
"Now, now Skarak," Desha said. "I'm sure Mavik is sorry. He'll be a good little slave, like his father, and give himself up. Won't you Mavik? You can join your father. Rise up in our ranks. Things will be better for you if you do."
Mavik searched desperately for an exit, a hole, a hiding place, a weapon. Something! The best he found was a mid-sized rock. He didn't see himself taking out three seasoned warriors with a stone.
Desha's voice called out again, closer now. "Come on, Mavik. Don't be like that. We'll send your pa to fetch you. If you come back with Rat peacefully, we'll let you choose which finger."
Another lie. Desha knew that Mavik would see through it. What Desha was really telling Mavik was that his own father was coming first, and whatever trap Mavik had planned, Kelsen would spring it. 
However, there was no need. Mavik had no trap, no clever plan, no ploy, and no hope. Why couldn't he have been the host to a useful wizard like a Digger mage? Then he could seal the tunnel behind him. Or Glower magic could blind the Sky Raiders, a Fire-whisperer send a kiss of flame, a Weather witch a blast of lightning. Arth could suck their souls, Kolram would bring some sort of animal to help them, and even Magic-finder's had their Sleep Spell. 
He had nothing. He was nothing. All he could do was know something bad was coming, and that there was nothing he could do about it. He needed no water to tell him that. 
Kelsen drew closer. Mavik made out his hunched silhouette approaching. "Come on, Son, be smart. Surrender. They'll show mercy."
"Mercy, mercy, mercy," the corridor echoed back.
A third lie. There was no mercy.
Kelsen rounded the corner, clutching his net. His father looked even more haggard than normal. His rat peeked out from the pocket of his robe, staring at Mavik with two pink eyes.
 Two paces back followed Desha, Skarak, and the blond Sky Raider. Desha had an arrow nocked and Skarak, a rusty iron mace. The blond Sky Raider wielded a sword. Kelsen shifted from foot to foot, and wouldn't meet Mavik's eyes. Mavik had nothing but a handful of water. 
At least Emerelda could cast her shield. She formed one now, as the Sky Raiders approached. Her face looked strained and tired in the amber, writhing light. "I can't be holding them fer long. Any ideas? What about Jijari- she be any help? She be seein' anything about this in the water?" 
The water, why didn't he think of it earlier? He knelt down and gazed into the stream. He placed his hands into the brook. He felt a pulse, a vibration in the ground. The ground split open and a hole formed. The water glided through the growing aperture, a newborn waterfall.
As the opening expanded, a surge of hope coursed through him. Perhaps this was their salvation. This was what the Source intended them to find. Here was a secret door, right here in the water, opening on his touch. The streambed vibrated and churned as the hole widened. Mavik smiled. Everything would be all right. A singular sense of salvation elated him. This was bliss. Like Jijari had felt at the Blessings of the Water ceremony, after three days of fasting and vision seeking. She was right. He need only to trust the rope.
Then a pincer-like hand burst through the creek, and took him by the throat. 

Chapter 22 
The Seventh Rung

She can already cook a delicious lemon biscuit, and it turns out she is a rebel and a scholar. What else don't we know about her?" - Verica

-<>- 

Verica rapped thrice in brisk succession. She tried the handle on Jazlyn's door, but it was locked. 
Come on, Jaz. Please be home. What if I'm too late? She'd run all the way across the Red Palace and her heart raced like a jackrabbit pursued by a pack of scagazi. Had she been fast enough?
She knocked again. Come on. Metal rattled somewhere in the distance behind her. She turned, panic grabbing at her, half expecting to see Flickers approaching. It was just the wiry green Mantu chef, Ec, carrying a towering salver full of pots and dishes to the scullery.
Verica's knuckles pounded the dragonwood door.
"Who is it?" Ravenna's voice called through the door.
"It's me. Verica. Hurry, please."
Ravenna opened the door, her thin red eyebrows knit in concern. Org stood at her side gripping his spear. Jazlyn lounged on the divan, leafing through a leather bound tome. 
"Hullo." Jazlyn lowered her book gently onto a side table. "Any news?"
Verica rushed in. "The guards are coming for you. We have to run! Now!" 
"What? Why?"
 "We don't have time for what-whys-whose-how-do-you-dos."
Jazlyn stood, forehead scrunched beneath her ruby-studded tiara. Ravenna thrust Jazlyn's satchel into her hand. "Go. I'll delay them. I'll tell them you went to . . . the arboretum . . . that ought to hold them off for a bit."
Verica grabbed Jazlyn's other hand and dragged her towards the main stairwell. Org followed. 
Jazlyn placed her hand on his huge gray chest, between a V of leather armor. "Verica and I must go alone."
Org curled his lip like a defiant toddler. "Org no leave Little Princess."
"You're sweet," Jazlyn said, "but Verica and I would be recognized with you. If you want to help us, walk towards . . . what did Ravenna say . . . the arboretum. If they ask, we lost you in the glass gardens. That's an order, Org."
Org bowed his boulder-sized head. "Org obeys."
Jazlyn kissed Org's cheek.
 Org placed his hands flat against each other, in the manner of the Sunken Shaman. "Good-bye, Little Princess." Org turned and lumbered away, down the eastern corridor. 
"Every moment risks our freedom." Verica grabbed Jazlyn's hand, and dashed towards the main stairwell. 
The clink of armor ahead caused them to reverse course. They headed east, but approaching soldiers sounded from there as well.
"The scullery," Verica whispered.
"This is no time for a snack."
"Does being a Princess make you stupid or is your tiara restricting air flow to your brain?" Verica asked. "We can hide in there till the guards leave." 
 Jazlyn's face flushed, but she followed Verica into the kitchen. 
Verica spoke in the Red Tongue as they entered the kitchen. "Your father is sending people after you and any remaining magi they haven't yet detained. Even the Draconess and Dade! They plan to sacrifice you at a temple."
"You're sure?" Jazlyn asked.
"Yes. I'm in trouble too. The Dracon saw me spying." Verica stole a pastry off a tray of cooling honey holes. "I'm glad we're hiding in a scullery; I'm famished. Don't shake your head at me. You try keeping shadow form for that long and running up all those stairs to save your ungrateful friend who won't even let you eat a teensy little snack."
Ec stared at them, her bulbous eyes intense swirls of gold and black. Jazlyn pulled servant's aprons and hats off hooks.
Jazlyn said to Ec in the common tongue, "Verica and I want to pretend to be your assistants. Some of the Flickers are playing with us, so if they come in, say you haven't seen us."
Jazlyn and Verica threw the aprons and bonnets over their dresses and flowered hair. Ec continued staring. 
"Okay that was a lie," Jazlyn said. "The truth is we're in trouble, Ec. Please, don't tell anyone we're here. It's important."
Ec spoke fluently in the Red tongue, "Don't let them see your face."
Jazlyn's jaw dropped, mirroring the astonished feeling washing over Verica. Ec winked a leathery eyelid before flattening a lump of dough with her rolling pin. The door squeaked open. Verica and Jazlyn turned and feigned cutting vegetables.
The voice of Royal Companion Oz Strongfist bellowed, "Mantu, we search for the Dracon's daughter. Have you seen her?"
Ec slapped the dough down, keeping her back to the Dragonknight. "This one not see, Master."
Strongfist's footsteps drew closer to Verica. "How about you servant girl, did you see the Dracon's daughter?"
His shadow and she noxious odor enveloped her. She relaxed her shoulders, trying to appear no more nervous than any servant talking to a superior. She shook her head.
Strongfist stepped closer. His breath made her eyes water. "Look at me when I'm talking to you, wench." 
Verica chewed her lip. If she turned, the Royal Companion would recognize her. If she didn't he would grab her and turn her forcibly. Should she run for it? She could throw a hot pot of boiling oil in his face and race off. 
"All you need to do is find a pot of boiling oil and then have Strongfist help pour it on himself," Lukor suggested.
"Really should never have taught you sarcasm."
She was readying herself to turn into wraith-form, when Crow's voice called from across the hall. "They're in the arboretum! Strongfist, come."
Strongfist turned around and left, door clanging behind him. Breath returned to her lungs, as she steadied herself against the counter.
"Ec." Jazlyn approached the Mantu warily. "You know the Red Tongue?"
"What I know might surprise you, Child." Ec gestured towards a pile of crates. "Help me move these."
"This is no time to do-" Jazlyn began.
"Do it!"
Jazlyn turned crimson.
Verica helped Ec pushed aside the heavy crates revealing a trap door. "This leads to a storage area." Ec pulled open the trapdoor. A ladder descended into darkness. "The ladder is missing the seventh rung. Be careful. Go straight when you get to the bottom and tell the fat baker with the shaven head, Cyreves, that I sent you. He'll hide you in the Cubby. I'll meet you there with Ravenna and we'll find a way to get you out."
"Cyreves?" Verica asked.
Ec shooed them. "He's part of the resistance. Go."
"I can't believe she speaks the Red Tongue," Verica thought.
"Why is that difficult for you to accept?" Lukor inquired.
"Well, usually people in the lower caste aren't learned. I mean she can already cook a delicious lemon biscuit, and it turns out she is a rebel and a scholar. What else don't we know about her?" 
"We can only learn a small fraction of a human's totality."
Verica shook her head. Her whole universe had already been turned upside down a few times today. She hoped the day didn't hold any more surprises. She climbed through the trapdoor, feeling her way past the missing rung. 

-<>-

Wayden gathered firewood with the other slaves. He kept picking the wrong type of wood and getting yelled at by the Sky Raiders. "Not Stink Wood, you dolt! You want Gar to throw you on the fire for heat?"
Heat would have been welcome. It was freezing and the Sky Raiders that watched them turned his stomach. Mavik did this for the last eight years, Wayden had done it for one day and already couldn't stand another moment of it. How did he stand it?
A shadow fell on Wayden. Glancing up, he saw Isel's skywolf belly, as the beast spiraled into a landing.
 Yet another ghost from his nightmares come back to haunt. The one-eared sky raider straddled a silver wolf. A magic-eater slithering nearby drained Wayden's powers, or else he'd have the silver wolf eat his other ear off. 
Wayden had yet to see the Ozac who killed Nanny or the Tulkarian who shot the arrow into his mother. While they'd been gathering wood an elderly witch named Laeko had told him that they and his own traitorous father were chasing Mavik. Laeko also had him about how Mavik and a girl had run away just the other night. 
"Who was the girl he ran with?" Wayden had asked Laeko. 
"Her name was Emerelda. A young blonde-haired girl, a Guardian mage."
"A Guardian. . . Solita!" Kolram sobbed.
Wayden shared Kolram's disappointment. If he'd been captured a day earlier, perhaps he could have escaped with Mavik and Solita's host. Or if Wayden hadn't been captured at all, perhaps Mavik would have found his way to him. Instead fate had switched their places, keeping them just as separate as ever. 
"Let us be glad our loved ones escaped our fate," Kolram said, but beneath the Grandmaster's words, was pain as deep as his own. 
 Wayden had asked Laeko if he could follow after Mavik, but the Strand Prophet shook her head. "Even if they hadn't doubled the guards, only a Guardian can use Centuron's door. Do not worry, the Source has a plan for you. My prophecies show you entering Dark Fist from above, not below."
 "The Weaver worries me the most of all," Kolram had said, "What scheme is she plotting?" 
Wayden stared as Isel landed his Skywolf. He gestured to two Skyraiders.
 "Get Mavik's brother on the skywolf. The Skymaster wants to talk to him." 
The Skywolf took off at a dizzyingly vertical angle. The flight reminded Wayden of being on the ledge with Night. He was sure he was going to plummet, but the leg straps held solid.
A six-foot tall Dragonman Sky Raider with red and black scales all over his body pulled Wayden off the wolf and forced him onto his knees before Gar's Eagle Throne. The Skymaster turned his shaven head towards Wayden and glared at him with his tiny eyes.
 A scar ran from Gar's necklace to the base of his ear. Wayden knew the story behind that wound. A Flicker's blade cut Gar across the neck as he fled Vilanos after murdering Baltoo. He'd flown away, with a gurgling laugh, as his blood spilt like hot rain. How Gar survived had been the subject of speculation. Some thought he must be a descendant of an Immortal to have withstood such a blow. Others claimed he made a deal with the wraiths. However Gar survived, survive he did. 
The bonfire danced and shifted in the wind. Wayden was thrown to his knees before the triad of golden thrones. He'd met Gar and Alaina, but the sky wife was unfamiliar. She looked as muscular and lean as Gar himself. Her long blue hair lifted in the wind, revealing a bruised eye. 
The Dragonman Sky Raider and half a dozen human Sky Raiders stood between Wayden and Gar, black cloaks flapping in the fierce wind. With the Sky Raiders was Goat. If the Ozac and the Tulkarian returned, he'd have them all in one place. Vengeance would be his. Sort of. Not really.
"Do not despair," Kolram said. "The Source has led us here for a reason."
Wayden strained against the ropes, but his old enemy quashed his efforts. 
 "Kolram's host." Goat's voice oozed contempt. This was the fearsome Goat man from his nightmares? The creature who had abducted Mavik all those years ago was just a man wearing a crude, lacquered mask.
Goat's hands glowed yellow. A Magic Finder. Had they been seeking magi when they seized Mavik all those years ago?
"Where is your brother?" Gar's voice sliced like the winter wind. "How did you help him escape?" 
Whatever Wayden had been expecting, it hadn't been this. He knew Gar was cruel and powerful. But he hadn't expected stupid. How could a mage who mastered Beast Tongue magic be such a fool? "You think I know how Mavik escaped? That I helped him?"
Gar dug a blue knife into the gilded arm of his Eagle Throne. The chair was almost as scarred as its owner. 
"Don't play dumb with me."
"Fine, just as long as you don't play paranoid with me."
Gar leapt from his throne and brandished his knife in front of Wayden's face. "Talk, Kolram! The truth!"
"He's raging at Kolram, not me," Wayden realized.
 "He has grown even more unstable than when I knew him last," Kolram said.
"All right, the truth . . . yes, this was our plan," Wayden said. "I'd let you kill a Royal Companion, tie me to a tree, and take me prisoner so my brother could escape. I also planned for you to burn my house down, and I tricked you into killing my mother. If all goes well, soon I'll trick you into stabbing me with that knife."
"It worked," Gar said, pressing the knife against the side of Wayden's cheek. A bead of blood dripped down Wayden's neck. "Don't be smart with me, boy. Kolram was always so sanctimonious. He was the good boy. Our Grandmaster made him his protg, snubbing me, even though I was a thousand times the Beast Tongue Kolram could ever hope to be. The great Baltoo. You should have seen the look on the old fool's face when I ordered his own skywolf to eat him." Gar sheathed his knife. "Your brother won't get far. Your father, and some of my other men, are hunting down him down right now."
Wayden strained against the ropes again. "Face me like a man, coward. Untie me and let's fight this out once and for all, Beast Tongue against Beast Tongue."
"He'll kill you." Kolram said.
"I have a plan."
"Does it involve getting killed? If so, it's working brilliantly."
The leaf in Gar's gold armband seemed familiar to Wayden. 
Gar shrugged. "I have nothing to prove. I bested Kolram time and again."
Wayden sat up. "So you say, but have we seen it? I think you're a lying heap of scagazi dung. You weren't Grandmaster. Kolram was, but you were too-"
Gar slapped Wayden's face so hard, the world spun. The dizziness of the spinning changed to the deeper sinking sensation of the Glimpse taking hold. Wayden was Gar now. The Skymaster was inside a stone chamber adorned with tapestries. He sat on a divan, Sky Raider guards on either side of him. Crow and a quartet of Flickers stood before Gar. The Flickers were pouring out a large sack of coins into a cedar chest. Gar fiddled with his necklace. He never tired of the power he could feel vibrating inside of it, as hot as a coal, and as energizing as cool mountain water.
Crow's voice was a whisper. "Please forgive me if this is an affront, but I must ask you this . . ."
"Spit it out, man."
"How do you feel about your daughter? Would you consider adding her to the harvest for an extra three thousand gold-bones?"
Gar eyes fastened on the chest of coins. "No."
"I apologize for even bringing it up," Crow said, holding up a black gloved hand. "She isn't necessary to our plans. I heard false rumors that you weren't happy with her."
"Five thousand."
"Four is the highest I'm authorized to go."
"Agreed."
Four thousand Raslonian gold bones! Gar thought. I would have sold her for a hundred.
The memory faded. Wayden found himself back on top of the Nest, wind whipping the Beacon's smoke directly at Wayden.
"We already knew that Alaina would be sold by her father," Wayden thought. "Still the details could help us convince Alaina of it."
"And Gar's power does indeed come from his necklace," Kolram mused. "Did you feel the power emanating from it?"
Gar turned to Isel and Goat. "Enough, our time is out. Isel, take Alaina and the boy to Dark Fist. Goat, head down to the camp and make sure that everything is going alright with the shipping of the rest of the slaves."
Goat nodded and boarded his winged wolf.
"Tie the slave to Red Paw," Alaina ordered a Sky Raider.
Isel shook his head. "We'll take my wolf."
Two large Sky Raiders grabbed Wayden and bound him to the wolf's back. The Sky Wife stepped over to Wayden and whispered, "You are the one. Laeko told me you would help me."
The woman turned, blue hair dancing in the wind. Alaina strolled over and mounted behind Wayden. Isel talked to Gar in hushed tones. 
Wayden whispered to Alaina: "I Glimpsed your father selling you to someone called Crow for four thousand Raslonian gold bones."
Alaina said nothing. Did she believe him?
Isel climbed onto the wolf's haunches.
"Hee-yah!" he cried, and the wolf launched itself, spreading its long silver and black wings, catching a current of cold air.
 Dark Fist awaited. 
 
Chapter 23
The One with the Quickest Blade

When the monsters bother me, I tell them to go away -Laurana

-<>- 


Water in his nose. In his lungs. Cold against his cheeks.
The water had been Mavik's hope, now it was his doom. The scagazi's pincer-like hands squeezed his neck, dragging him into the cavern's creek bed. He struggled to break free, pulling at the wrist, as stubborn as an ironwood tree. The world grew faint, dizzy, his vision became flashes of dark and light. I can't die. Emerelda needs me. He fought against the monstrous arm.
The scagazi's grip weakened, and he pushed up gasping for air. The scagazi's wrist had one of Desha's black plumed arrows in it. Mavik had fletched those arrows himself, with feathers from the Tulkarian's own Skywolf. Blessed air rushed into his lungs.
 Scagazi emerged through a hole they had dug in the creek bed. Mavik and Emerelda found themselves ringed by the insects. 
One of the scagazi gurgled, swatting its neck, as if stung by an ice bee. It slumped onto its back, its white blood clouding the stream. 
"One down," Desha said, nocking another arrow. 
	A second scagazi lunged forward. The tips of its claws struck Guardian magic, amber sparks crackling upwards as if from a campfire. The beast's pincers pounded the shield again. A gap opened in the shield. A third blow widened it. 
 Emerelda's forehead was dappled with beads of sweat. "I be losin' it."
The scagazi stuck its hand through the gap in the shielding, grabbing Emerelda's neck. Then, a thwooping sound, and it slumped forwards, another black-feathered shaft protruding from its back.
"Now, I owe Desha two," Mavik thought. 
"You owe him two arrows launched from a bow," Jijari said. "Make sure to make them count."
"I thought Sunken Shamans were supposed to be forgiving?"
"Let the unrepentant pay for their sins, blood for blood." 
"Remind me not to irk any Alatians."
A scagazi hurled itself at Emerelda. She gestured and amber vines formed a web of frozen sunlight. The scagazi hissed, as it bounced off the ambient light, but soon recovered and renewed clawing at it. The Guardian coils shriveled, another hole widening in the new shield. 
A whirlpool of dirt formed beneath Kelsen. Two scagazi hands gripped Mavik's father's legs and yanked. His eyes bulged and his hand grabbed at the rocks and dirt, fingers digging tiny trenches. Then he was gone. 
I should be happy he's dead. Mavik bit back a tear. 
 "The bugs got Rat." Skarak's voice echoed through the cavern.
Mavik tried to push his emotions into a box, but found they wouldn't go. It was like trying to hold the ocean in a tiny cup. Sadness and anger swirled into one. Hot tears raced down his cheeks. 
Skarak's mace crushed a monster's skull, at the same moment a scagazi snapped the blond-haired Sky Raider's neck, while Desha parried a charge, using his bow to trip the beast. Desha's bow snapped and he cursed as he discarded the remains of the broken weapon. He unsheathed a jagged dirk. A scagazi charged Desha, but the Tulkarian stepped aside and the creature crashed over his extended leg. Desha pivoted lodging the tip of his dirk into a gap in the rear of the monster's exoskeleton. The creature sank to the floor and Desha's cloak was drenched in scagazi blood.
Desha grinned wide. "I got us a kebab for dinner, Skarak."
"Less talk, Pretty Boy, more fight!" Skarak bellowed. A scagazi bit into Skarak's wrist, and the Ozac roared. The gray behemoth dropped his mace and grabbed the scagazi, lifted him with both hands, and brought him down upon the tip of a pointed stalagmite. 
The Sky Raiders had lost two of their members so far, the scagazi a dozen, but the scagazi still outnumbered them three to one. Whoever triumphed, thug or bug, Emerelda and Mavik would be the next target. 
Emerelda's hand clapped down on his shoulder. "We need to be gettin' out o' here. Look."  Emerelda pointed at the burrowed hole in the stream bed, from which one of the scagazi had emerged. 
The water from the brook spiraled through it, then poured into a chamber below. Peering down the hole, Mavik gauged the distance the same as dropping from a mid-sized tree, except onto a rockier surface. Would they survive the fall? Even if they did, they'd be trapped down there. 
"The Source led you here for a reason," Jijari said. "Don't you see? This is where you are meant to go. A leap of faith."
Mavik hoped she was right.
Emerelda caught his eye. "We be jumpin' or dyin'." 
Mavik nodded. He hesitated for a heartbeat, mumbling a silent prayer. Then he leapt. 

-<>-

Sandwiched between him and Wayden, Alaina wondered which one to trust. Isel's breath stank and he was uncharacteristically quiet. She'd known Isel her whole life, and if the Skyraider was anything, it was her father's toady. If her father had said paint the sky black, Isel would do it. It all came down to her father. Was it beyond him to do this? 
"You know it's not," Nadra said. "Your father is a beast." 
 The wolf spread its wings, and launched itself from Mount Odesis, the only home Alaina had ever known shrinking as he rose. Was this the last time she'd see it? The last day she'd be alive? The icy peak dwindled away, , as the wolf veered towards the distant temple. 
"Wayden is just trying to save his own skin," Alaina thought, as her wolf flew down towards the slave camp.
"No, He isn't, you little fool," Nadra said. "Isel's breathing is strained. His movements tense. You're heading to your own murder. You have great faith in your father, but four thousand reasons not to trust him." 
Four thousand - the number she kept hearing - her father had said it to Yveka in the kennel, 'I have four thousand reasons for keeping her around'. The weaver had said four thousand bones. Had she meant gold bones, the Raslonian currency? 
She didn't want to believe it. It was her whole life she'd have to give up. It wasn't much of a life, but it was all she'd known. She'd never been anything but a Skydaughter. 
"What if I am just being paranoid? Maybe it's just a misunderstanding. Maybe Wayden is in cahoots with the Weaver."
 "There is a simple way to test Isel," Nadra said, "See if he'll let you go."
She could make out the Anvil up ahead. There wasn't much time.
Alaina let out a groan and then waited a moment, and groaned again. "Isel . . . I'm ill."
"What's the trouble Daughter Sky?" Isel asked, shouting over the wind. 
"My stomach. A sharp pain. I need to go back to the Nest and let the healer look."
"Nay, your father says you're to go to Dark Fist." 
"He didn't know . . . argh, my stomach. I would feel this . . . uggh . . . sick. I . . . have a very sharp pain in my stomach. I need the healers to look at me. The healer told me if I get pains like this, I have to see him immediately. It is a matter of life and death."
"Nonsense." Isel's voice sound stiff. "You just have a stomach ache. You'll be all right."
Alaina discreetly drew her blue-steel dirk. 
 "You warned him," Nadra said. "You told him it was a matter of life or death." 
		
-<>- 

Rif and Night had been brought back through Deep Woods in the wagon. Flickers kept an eye on him and his hands were manacled. It wasn't the iron chains that made sleep elusive though. His mind was in tumult. 
"You should have killed them all," Belok said. "I told you. I told you in my secret whisper."
"Go away," Rif thought. "We might not be in this mess if you hadn't killed Thunderstone."
"You should thank me for that," Belok said. "In this world and the ones between it, it is eat or be eaten. If I hadn't killed him, he would have us."
"Source help me," Rif thought. "Make him go away."
"There is no Source," Belok said. "There is only the one with the quickest blade."
"Don't let him goad you, Rif," Genika said, "Stay calm."
Stay calm, yes, but how? He kept seeing Thunderstone, Big Darius, and the girl in the pine grove, lying dead. There was the girl in Tulkar too- during the Blood Games. And the one by the well in the Mercy. She was so young, perhaps eight.
"How could I have done that?" Rif thought. "How could I have killed an eight-year old?"
"I'm ten and a half," a girl's voice spoke. He'd heard it before, but it had just been a whisper. Now it was as loud as a waterfall. "It wasn't your fault. I'm Laurana, by the way." 
Grief rushed through Rif. "Oh, Primordial, forgive me. Oh Laurana, I'm so sorry. I can't forgive myself."
"There's nothing you can do about it. It's not so bad in here. We're never hungry or beaten. Anyway, you didn't kill me. It was Belok."
"You're comforting me? You should hate me."
"Some of the other girls in here do. But not me or Genika. What's done is done. That's what my mama always said."
Rif would have preferred hate. It was no more than he deserved. Laurana said she forgave him, but he could never forgive himself. She was ten and would have no future except in the mindscape. She'd never kiss a boy, nurse a child, drink the worm wine on her woman's day, or learn to play a drumpharp. She had been murdered. Murdered by him. It's been me all along. He couldn't breath. He wanted to loosen his collar, but his manacles were too heavy to budge. He closed his eyes and let out a sob.
"Rif, Laurana is right," Genika said, "When there is naught to do about the past, look to the future. Make sure this never happens again. You have to resist Belok. Only you can do it. You have to tell Belok no."
"When the monsters bother me," Laurana said, "I tell them to go away."
"But I am the monster!" Rif thought, "They'll lock me up in a dungeon and then the Dracon will execute me."
"And what wrongs will the Dracon inflict when Niar absorbs your powers?" Arth asked, "At least you have a conscience. You can't let him win. You can't."
Night patted Rif on the shoulder, misunderstanding his tears. 
 "Don't despair," Night whispered. "The Night shall rise. And we will sweep over this land and wreak our vengeance."
Rif jerked away from her, chains clinking. "I don't want v-v-vengeance. I don't want to kill anyone. I never wanted these powers, these souls. I'm a danger to everyone. It's best if I'm k-k-killed."
"Rif, consider, you house eight other souls," Genika said. "If you die, so do we. Don't let go so easily. You must hold on. Don't give in to Belok or the Dracon. Find the middle path. It's the only way." 
Rif had never thought of the fact that he was now a home for all the souls Belok sucked. He didn't know what sort of a life Genika and the others had inside of him, but they were alive. He had to try to live, for Genika, for Arth, for Laurana, for the other girls whose souls now resided inside him.
"How? How do I resist?"
 "Belok preys off your insecurity," Genika said. "You must be resolute."
"Well even if I do resist Belok, how am I supposed to get out of here? I'm chained and guarded."
"I do not know. We must trust in the Source."
When they reached the Red Palace the wagon was escorted across the red moat, a river of lava that encircled the palace. A portcullis was raised and Flickers and a magic-eater forced them though a labyrinth of stone corridors. 
Rif and Night were escorted deep down into the dungeons, until they arrived at a door marked by a bronze plaque as the 'Plague Room.' A magic-eater slithered by the door. Two Flickers stood guard, one tall, with mustachios and the other short, heavy, with a shaven head.
One of the Flickers who had brought them untied Rif's bonds, saying, "For the Plague Room."
 The tall guard responded, "Throw the prisoners in. And be none too gentle."
The short guard held up a hand. "Wait. No need to throw them. And why 'none too gentle'?  I thought you were all refined and mannerly?"
"Oh, ask them politely, shall we?" A vein protruded from the tall guard's forehead. "These are prisoners of the Dracon. Traitors." 
The Flicker's head turned from one guard to the other, like a dog wanting to obey, but not knowing who to listen to.
The little guard rolled his eyes. "An old crone and a boy. They must have nearly thrown the Red Lands into ruins."
"This boy killed Sir Thunderstone."
"I would have liked to have seen that fight. What did he do, chew through his armor? Besides, I thought this was the Plague Room. Why do you want to throw a hardened murderer into a cell with innocent plague victims?"
The tall guard's face was wrinkled with anger. "Fine, we'll graciously welcome the traitors to their humble abode. Happy?"
 "Ecstatic."
But the tall guard yanked Rif and Night from the Flicker and shoved them harshly into the dungeon.
The door slammed shut.
"It doesn't matter," Rif thought. "No matter how nicely they let us into this room, it would still be a prison."
 It took a moment for Rif's eyes to adjust to the dim room. When they did, he half wished they hadn't. Old, sad men and women leaned against walls, or sat on the dusty stone floor. A series of overflowing buckets with flies buzzing around them, served as the privy and the room's perfume.
"Rif? Is that you?" a voice called. Rif turned around and felt someone grab him: hair and softness- a woman's embrace.
"Rif! Rif! Oh, my sweet Possum!" 
Even in the dark Rif could recognize his mother's voice, scent, and the feel of her arms enveloping him. Rif tasted the salt of tears running into his mouth, whether his own or his mother's he couldn't be sure.
"Oh, thank the Source, you're all right." His mother's voice was choked.
Rif sobbed on his mother's shoulders. He tried to think of the words to tell her. "How am I going to tell my mother, that I'm a murderer? How do I know that I won't black out and find Belok has murdered her?"
"You needn't worry," Belok said. "I only like redheads."

-<>-

Verica tied her red hair into a pony tail. She looked at the mid-sized keg. How long would she be stuck in it? It would be a torturous journey. Still, better than being caught.
 The storage room teemed with boxes, sacks and barrels organized by type and size. The ones on the right side of the room were empty, the ones on the left filled with dried goods of various sorts. Some of the kegs were stacked in a wagon, which was scheduled to leave the Red Palace for Tulkar. There were two empty ones, one for Jazlyn and one for herself. A concealed air hole in each one would ensure they didn't suffocate.
In the distance, men's voices and wolf howls sounded from the nearby skywolf kennel where many of the kegs were being loaded. Verica was tired, tense, and more than a little scared. It would be no easy thing to escape from the Red Palace.
Jazlyn gestured towards the barrel, her eyes wide with disbelief. "You expect me . . . to hide . . . in there?" 
Cyreves the supply master, a heavy man with double chin and a shaven pear-shaped head, smiled toothily at Jazlyn. "Quickly. You will be getting in the barrel, Your Majesty."
"How will we drink- or- care for our bodily functions?" 
Cyreves held up his hands apologetically. "This one knows it's not the most comfortable of accommodations, but it will not be for long. Half a day at most. And you will be safe and this is the most important thing, is it not, Your Highness?"
Ravenna helped Verica get one leg into the cask. "Just get in Jaz. Before someone comes."
Ravenna and Ec stepped in through a narrow side doorway, ducking their heads. "I've sent a pigeon to my brother. He'll take you somewhere safe."
"Food," Ec offered.
Jazlyn waved the lemon biscuit away.
"Can I have hers?" Verica asked, peeking up from her barrel.
"My brother is going to help keep you hidden," Ravenna said, handing the biscuit to Verica. 
"Whiwuheduethaferus?" asked Verica, wiping the crumbs from her chin.
"Can you swallow your biscuits first, My Lady?" Ravenna asked.
Verica swallowed. "Why would he do that for us?"
"He's one of the Resistance," Ravenna explained. "The Fire Guard captured my mother and father for performing Glower magic. We protested, tried to get the government to see sense, but they were stubborn beyond reason. We began to suspect they were planning to do something with the magi. Ec is the leader of our movement. She's a Splasher."
"There is a time for conversation and a time for hiding," Ec said, glancing at the door.
Jazlyn stared into the dusty, cobweb-filled cask. "There must be some other way?"
 "Look, Jaz," Verica said, "You're not a princess anymore. You're a wanted felon. So, unless you want your father to hand you over to the Skymaster, get in. Every moment you stand here in the open, you risk everybody's lives. So get in the wraithin' barrel, or I'll stuff you in head first."
Jaz looked taken aback, but climbed into the wobbly container. Verica huddled down in her own keg. The ceiling disappeared as the lid clunked down on top of her. Then all was darkness. She heard their footsteps leave. It was hard to breathe in the tight space. She should have asked Ravenna if she had any more biscuits.
It was dark and the only sound was her own breathing. It was warm too and she grew sweaty. She waited. And waited. Then waited some more.
"Why does time go so fast when you're doing something fun like playing mumbly ball, but creep along whenever you're uncomfortable?"
 "Time always flows the same speed," Lukor said, "It is simply your perception of time that has transformed."
"I know, but it's still driving me crazy."
"Your brain is constantly engaged during a game of mumbly ball," Lukor's voice took on that pedantic tone that reminded Verica of her father. For some reason it was reassuring to be lectured. "Whereas when you are waiting, you're doing little else. The solution suggests itself that if you wish the perceived time to advance more quickly, you must busy your mind."
"I see. Well, why don't you tell me a bit about the wraiths then, while we're waiting?" Verica asked, wondering if Asgaroth and Jazlyn were having a similar comforting conversation. Somehow she doubted it. According to Jazlyn, Asgaroth's favorite conversations involved threats of tearing bones out of people's bodies.
 "You've never asked me about this before."
"I know. I never liked the idea of being a half-wraith. I guess becoming an outlaw has made me accept my better half."
"What is it that you would like to know?" Lukor asked.
"Are all wraiths like you?"
"No. Though we have a hive mind, we are individuals. Some of the wraiths aren't even fully developed consciousness. Others, like myself have more forceful personalities. I must say, at the risk of sounding immodest, most wraiths are not as scientifically minded as myself."
"Do you have children?"
"No. Wraiths are not born nor do we die."
"Why would you want to be inside of me?"
"For the same reason you would read one of your fictional books. When you enter into someone else's life, you get a glimpse of things you could not otherwise see. For a wraith like me, nothing could be more satisfying."
"You're weird. I'm going to get something to eat."
"You should stay hidden."
"I'll just be a moment."
Verica clambered out of the barrel and found a box of hard tack. It felt good to stretch her legs. Jazlyn's barrel was awful quiet. Verica put her ear close and could hear quiet snores. At least she's getting some rest. We might need it later. I should try to sleep too. 
Verica was finishing the last of the tack when the sound of clinking metal and approaching footsteps caught her attention. She made out Cyreves's voice and another familiar voice: one that gave her the shivers. A horrible intuition struck Verica. She turned into shadow form. The door flung open, and Crow stood in the doorway followed by Cyreves and several guards and magic-eaters. The slug-like creatures slithered towards the barrel Jazlyn was hiding in.
"Like hounds sniffing for food, they smell magic," Lukor thought.
Crow pointed towards Verica's empty container, lying sideways on the stone floor. "Where is Berik's daughter?"
Cyreves's face paled. "This one doesn't know, Your High Holiness. She was in the barrel when I left, I promise you."
A Flicker opened the lid and a second guard lifted a struggling Jazlyn out. Jaz had picked up a few new curse words recently, but her feet thudded uselessly into the huge guard's breast plate. 
No! They have her. They're going to sacrifice Jazlyn, Ravenna's parents, and countless other magi. They'll unleash Asgaroth on the world. They'll give the Dracon more power than even a responsible leader could handle. And there wasn't a blessed thing Verica could do about any of it. 
Or was there? Part of Verica still believed that everything happened for a reason. The accident, her hosting Lukor, maybe it was all meant to be, was all leading somewhere. She was meant to do something - but what?
 A Flicker gagged Jazlyn and manacled her hands behind her back.
"Take her to the Plague Room," Crow said.
"Berik's daughter was in that empty barrel. She must have fled," Cyreves said. 
"She won't get far," Crow said. "Ember Tibbons, send out search parties."
 The Ember nodded and departed.
"Now, my reward?" Cyreves asked.
Crow thrust the reward into Cyreve's belly, and then pulled the dirk back out, slick with blood. Cyreves slumped to his knees. Verica stifled a scream. Crow stepped out of the way and let the supply master fall flat on his face. 
Crow held up his blood-covered blade. "Paid in steel. Flicker Darius, clean this mess up."
The Flicker looked pale-faced and ready to retch.
